Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Hiring Land for Cultivation: Conditions and Ancillary Rights
Detailing the validity of land hire for cultivation with ancillary rights and specification requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid ijarah of land for cultivation, explain why water and path rights are automatically included, and identify the ruling when the crop is unspecified.

Core Idea
In ijarah of land, the crop must be specified to prevent harm, but water and path rights are automatically included.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on hiring land for cultivation. The passage distinguishes between the automatic inclusion of ancillary rights (water, path) and the mandatory specification of the crop. We will also see how the owner's discretion can substitute for specification, and how this differs from sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling and its rationale
State that the ijarah of land for cultivation is valid because the customary benefit of land is farming, which is intended in itself.
The proof is based on custom (urf), not a specific text.
2
Recognize automatically included ancillary rights
Water for irrigation and a path to the land are automatically included in the ijarah contract, even if not stipulated, because they are essential for the usufruct.
This contrasts with seeds, which are not included because ownership of the produce is not the immediate purpose.
3
Identify the condition of specifying the crop
The contract is valid only when the lessee specifies what crop will be cultivated, otherwise it is invalid due to potential dispute and harm to the land.
Different crops have different effects on the land, some harmful, so specification prevents uncertainty (gharar).
4
Understand the exception: owner's discretion
If the owner says 'cultivate whatever you wish,' the contract becomes valid without specification because the owner's consent removes the potential for dispute.
Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i agree with this position, while Shuraih required specification even in that case.
5
Compare with sale contract
In a sale of land, water and path rights are also automatically included without mention, but the rationale differs: in sale, ownership is intended for perpetual use, not immediate usufruct.
This distinction helps understand why seeds are not included in ijarah (they lead to ownership of produce, not usufruct).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله و يجوز استیجار الاراضي الخ - اراضی کو کاشت کے لئے اجارہ پر لینا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اراضی سے متاد فائدہ یہی معروف ہے کہ اس میں زراعت کی جائے اور یہ فائدہ بذات خود مقصود ہوتا ہے۔ اب مستاجر کو اس میں زمین کے سینچنے کا پانی اور اس میں جانے کا راستہ ملے گا۔ اگر چہ اس نے اجارہ میں اس کی شرط نہ کی ہو اس واسطے کہ اجارہ تو انتفاع ہی کے لئے منعقد ہوتا ہے۔ حالانکہ پانی کے حصہ اور راستہ کے بغیر انتفاع ممکن نہیں تو یہ دونوں چیزیں مطلق عقد میں داخل ہوں گی۔ بخلاف بیج کے کہ اس سے ملک رقبہ مقصود ہوتی ہے۔ فی الحال نفع اٹھانا مقصود نہیں ہوتا یہاں تک کہ گدھے گھوڑے کے بچہ کی اور دلدلی زمین کی بیع جائز ہے اور اجارہ جائز نہیں ہے تو بیع میں ذکر حقوق کے بغیر پانی کا حصہ اور راستہ داخل ہوگا۔
قوله ولا يصح العقد ... الخ - بغرض زراعت اراضی کا عقد اجارہ جائز تو ہے لیکن یہ جواز اسی وقت ہے۔ جب اس چیز کو بیان کر دے جس کی وہ اس زمین میں کاشت کرے گا۔ اس لئے کہ آراضی کا اجارہ کبھی برائے زراعت ہوتا ہے اور کبھی عمارت بنانے پودے لگانے ، خیمے گاڑنے وغیرہ کے لئے ہوتا ہے پھر جس چیز کی کاشت کی جاتی ہے اس میں تفاوت ہوتا ہے جیسے گیہوں ، جو ، جوار، چاول وغیرہ جن میں سے بعض چیزیں زمین کے لئے نقصان دہ ہوتی ہیں اور بعض غیر مضر اس لئے ان کی تعیین ضروری ہے تاکہ بعد میں جھگڑا پیدانہ ہو۔ ہاں اگر اس نے یہ کہ دیا ہو کہ جس چیز کی چاہے زراعت کرے تو اس صورت میں جو چاہے کاشت کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ جب مالک نے مستاجر کو اختیار دے دیا تو نا دانستگی کی وجہ سے جو جھگڑا پیدا ہو سکتا تھاوہ دور ہو گیا۔ امام مالک و امام شافعی کا مذہب بھی یہی ہے و عن شريح انه لا يصح حتى يبين ما يزرع
The hiring of lands for cultivation is valid. Because the customary benefit from land is farming, and this benefit is intended in itself. Now the lessee will get the water for irrigating the land and the path to access it, even if he did not stipulate them in the contract, because the ijarah is concluded for usufruct, and usufruct is not possible without water and path, so these two things are included in the absolute contract. Contrary to seeds, because through seeds ownership of the land is intended, not immediate usufruct. To the extent that the sale of a donkey's or horse's offspring and marshy land is valid, but ijarah is not valid, so in sale, water and path are included without mention.
The contract is not valid... For the purpose of cultivation, the ijarah contract of land is valid, but this validity is only when he specifies what he will cultivate in the land. Because the ijarah of land is sometimes for cultivation, sometimes for building, planting trees, pitching tents, etc. Moreover, there is variation in what is cultivated—wheat, barley, millet, rice, etc.—some of which are harmful to the land and some not harmful. Therefore, specification is necessary to prevent future dispute. However, if he said, 'Cultivate whatever you wish,' then he can cultivate whatever he wants. Because when the owner gave discretion to the lessee, the potential dispute due to ignorance is removed. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i also hold this view. And from Shuraih that it is not valid until he specifies what he will cultivate.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage covers two aspects: (1) the validity of hiring land for cultivation with automatic inclusion of water and path rights, and (2) the necessity to specify the crop. The Hanafi position is that specification is required to prevent harm, but if the owner gives absolute discretion, it is valid. Imam Malik and Imam Shafi'i agree, while Shuraih insists on specification. The distinction between ijarah and sale regarding inclusion of rights is also noted.

Key Terms
زراعت (zira'ah): Cultivation or farming.
تعیین (ta'yin): Specification of the crop type in the contract.
اختیار (ikhtiyar): Discretion given by the owner to the lessee to choose the crop.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In hiring land for cultivation, what happens if the tenant does not specify the crop?
A) The contract is void
B) The contract is valid only if the owner gives discretion
C) The contract is absolutely valid
D) The tenant can only plant wheat

Key Takeaway
The ijarah of land for cultivation is valid only when the crop is specified or the owner grants discretion, but water and path rights are automatically included.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Post-Term Removal of Structures and Trees on Leased Land
Discusses hire of land for building/planting and post-term removal with inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on removal of buildings/trees after a land lease and explain the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i and Hanbali schools.

Core Idea
Buildings and trees on leased land must be removed after the term — they have no fixed end, unlike crops.

This passage addresses a practical scenario in leasing land for construction or planting. The Hanafi school holds that at the end of the lease, the lessee must remove all structures and trees and return the land empty. However, Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad differ, arguing that such removal is only required if stipulated. Understanding this dispute clarifies the school's reasoning based on the nature of the item — whether it has a known end or not.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The lessee must remove buildings and trees after the lease term ends and return the land empty.
2
Identify the opposing school
Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad hold that the lessee is not forced to remove unless it was stipulated in the contract; otherwise, removal is only if the landowner compensates for damage.
3
Follow the Hanafi dalil
Buildings and trees have no fixed end; keeping them causes indefinite harm to the landowner. Therefore, removal is necessary.
Contrast with crops that have a known ripening time.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opponent
The opposing view would allow indefinite harm. The Hanafi view balances interests by requiring removal, while crops with a fixed end can be left with rent until ripe.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, Hanafis enforce removal; Shafi'is and Hanbalis allow the lessee to leave buildings/trees without compensation unless stipulated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز ان يستاجر الساحة ليبنى فيها او ليغرس فيها نخلا او شجرا لانها منفعة تقصد بالاراضي ثم اذا انقضت مدة الاجارة لزمه ان يقلع البناء والغرس ويسلمها فارغة لانه لا نهاية لها ففى ابقائها اضرار بصاحب الارض بخلاف ما اذا انقضت المدة والزرع بقل حيث تترك باجر المثل الى زمان الادراك لان لها نهاية معلومة فامكن رعاية الجانبين قال الا ان يختار صاحب الارض ان يغرم له قيمة ذالك مقلوعا ويتملكه فله ذالک وهذا برضاء صاحب الغرس والشجر الا ان ينقص الارض بقلعها فحينئذ يتملكها بغير رضاه قال او يرضى بتركه على حاله فيكون البناء لهذا والارض لهذا لان الحق له فله ان لا يستوفيه. قال وفي الجامع الصغير اذا انقضت مدة الاجارة وفى الارض رطبة فانها تقلع لان الرطاب لا نهاية لها فاشبه الشجر
،
توضیح اللغة ساحه چوک، بیبنی (ض) بناء تعمیر کرنا، يغرس (ض) غرساً پودہ لگانا۔ نخل درخت خرما ، اضرار نقصان دینا بقل . سبزی ادراک اپنے وقت پر پہنچنا ، يغرم (س) غرما تاوان دینا ، مقلوع اکھڑا ہوا،قلع اکھاڑ نا مرطب سپست ۔ ترجمہ جائز ہے تیر زمین کو کرایہ پر لینا عمارت بنانے یا درخت خرما پھلدار درخت لگانے کے لئے کیونکہ یہ بھی ایسی منفعت ہے جو آراضی سے مقصود ہوتی ہے۔ پھر جب اجارہ کی مدت گزر جائے تو ضروری ہوگا مستاجر کے لئے یہ کہ اکھاڑ لے عمارت اور درخت اور حوالے کر دے زمین خالی۔ کیونکہ عمارت اور درخت کی کوئی انتہا نہیں تو اجارہ باقی رکھنے میں مالک زمین کو ضرر رسانی ہے بخلاف اس کے جب مدت گزرگئی اور حال یہ کہ کھیتی کچی سبز ہے کہ وہ پختہ ہونے تک اجر مثل پر چھوڑ دی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ کھیتی پکنے کی ایک انتہا معلوم ہے تو جانبین کی رعایت ممکن ہوئی۔ مگر یہ کہ اختیار کرے زمین والا اکھڑے ہوئے کی قیمت دے کر مالک ہو جاتا تو اس کو یہ اختیار ہے۔ اور یہ پودے اور درخت والے کی رضامندی سے ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ زمین ناقص ہو جاتی ہو اس کے اکھاڑنے سے کہ اس وقت زمین والا اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ مستاجر کی رضامندی کے بغیر ، یا راضی ہو جائے اس کو علی حالہ چھوڑنے پر ۔ پس عمارت اس کی ہوگی اور زمین اسکی ۔ کیونکہ حق تو مالک زمین کا ہے تو اس کو اختیار ہے کہ اپنا حق حاصل نہ کرے۔ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ جب مدت اجارہ گزرگئی اور حال یہ کہ زمین میں رطبہ ہے تو اس کو اکھاڑ لیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ رطاب کی کوئی انتہانہیں پس وہ درخت کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ تشريح قوله ويجوزان يستاجر ... الخ - اگر عمارت بنانے یا درخت لگانے کے لئے زمین کرائے پر لے تو درست ہے۔ اب مدت اجارہ تمام ہو جانے کے بعد مستاجر اپنی عمارت تو ڑ کر اور درخت اکھاڑ کر خالی زمین مالک کے حوالے کرے گا۔ یعنی اس کو اس پر مجبور کیا جائے گا اور زمین کا مالک نقصان کا ضامن بھی نہ ہوگا ۔ امام مالک اور امام مزنی شافعی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ امام شافعی اور امام احمد فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر انقضاء مدت پر اکھاڑنا شرط ہو تب تو یہی حکم ہے اور اگر عقد مطلق ہو تو اکھاڑنے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ الا یہ کہ مالک نقصان کا ضامن ہو ۔ ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ عمارت اور درخت کے لئے کوئی انتہا معلوم نہیں تو اجارہ باقی رکھنے میں مالک زمین کا ضرر ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے اگر زمین میں کھیتی کھڑی ہو اور مدت اجارہ گزرگئی ہو کہ وہ پختہ ہونے تک اجر مثل پر چھوڑ دی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اس کے پکنے کی ایک انتہا معلوم ہے تو جانین کی رعایت ممکن ہے کہ مالک زمین کو کرائیل جائے گا اور مستاجر کو کھیتی پخت مل جائے گی ۔
It is permissible to hire an open space to build in it or to plant date palms or trees, because this is a benefit intended from lands. Then when the lease period expires, he must remove the building and plantation and hand it over empty, because they have no end, and in keeping them there is harm to the landowner. Contrary to the case when the period expires and the crop is green, it is left with rent of the like until the time of ripening, because it has a known end, so consideration of both sides is possible. He said: Unless the landowner chooses to pay the value of that removed and take ownership; he has that. And this is with the consent of the owner of the plantation and trees, unless the land is damaged by their removal, then he takes ownership without his consent. He said: Or he agrees to leave them as they are, so the building belongs to one and the land to the other, because the right is his, so he may not exercise it. He said: In al-Jami' al-Saghir: When the lease period expires and there is moist crop in the land, it is removed because moist crop has no end, so it resembles trees.
Glossary: Saha: open space; bina: building; yaghris: to plant; nakhl: date palm; idrar: causing harm; baql: vegetables; idrak: reaching (ripeness); yaghram: to pay compensation; maqlu': uprooted; qal': uprooting; rutab: moist. Translation: It is permissible to hire land for building or planting date palms or fruit trees, because this is also a benefit intended from lands. Then when the lease period expires, it becomes necessary for the lessee to remove the building and trees and hand over the land empty. Because buildings and trees have no end, so keeping them harms the landowner. Contrary to when the period expires and the crop is unripe green, it is left with rent of the like until it ripens, because ripening has a known end, so consideration of both sides is possible. Unless the landowner chooses to pay the value of the removed items and become owner; he has this option. And this is with the consent of the plantation and tree owner, unless the land is damaged by their removal, then the landowner takes ownership without the lessee's consent. Or he agrees to leave them as they are, so the building belongs to one and the land to the other, because the right is his, so he may not claim it. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: When the lease period expires and there is moist crop in the land, it is removed because moist crop has no end, so it resembles trees. Commentary: If one hires land for building or planting trees, it is valid. After the lease ends, the lessee must demolish the building and uproot the trees and hand over the land empty. He will be forced to do so, and the landowner will not guarantee the loss. Imam Malik and Imam Muzni (Shafi'i) also hold this view. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad say: If removal at the end of the term is stipulated, then the same ruling; if the contract is absolute, he will not be forced to remove unless the landowner guarantees the loss. We say: Buildings and trees have no known end, so keeping them harms the landowner. Contrary to standing crop in the land when the lease expires: it is left with rent of the like until it ripens, because ripening has a known end, so consideration of both sides is possible: the landowner gets rent, and the lessee gets the ripe crop.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage deals with the hire of land for building or planting trees. At the end of the term, the lessee must remove the structures and trees and return the land empty. Buildings and trees have no fixed end, so keeping them would cause indefinite harm to the landowner. However, if the crop is green (rutab) at the end of the term, it is also removed because it has no fixed end like regular crops. There is a dispute with Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad who say removal is only required if stipulated; otherwise, the lessee is not forced to remove unless the owner compensates for damage. The Hanafi response is based on the absence of a fixed end for buildings and trees, which causes ongoing harm. The passage also discusses options for the landowner to purchase the structures/trees or leave them with consent.

Key Terms
ساحة (saha): Open space or courtyard; land for building or planting.
قلع (qal'): Removal or uprooting of structures or trees.
رطبة (rutba): Moist or green crops that are not yet ripe.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to buildings erected on leased land after the lease term ends?
A) They become the property of the landowner
B) The lessee must remove them and return the land empty
C) They remain until the lessee decides to remove them
D) The lessee must pay rent for the land as long as the building stands

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, any improvement without a fixed end (buildings, trees) must be removed by the lessee at the lease's end to prevent indefinite harm to the landowner.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
6 min
Leasing Land for Building or Planting Trees
Ruling on leasing land with removal obligation at end

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school obligates removal of buildings and trees upon lease expiry and evaluate the Shafi'i/Hanbali counter-argument.

Core Idea
A lease for buildings or trees obligates removal because their harm is endless; crops may stay because their end is known.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, we examine a dispute between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i/Hanbali schools regarding the lessee's obligation to remove structures and trees at the end of a lease. The key distinction turns on whether the benefit has a fixed end (nihaayah ma'loomah). Understanding this principle clarifies many rulings in lease law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Explain that leasing land for building or planting is permissible, but at expiry the lessee must remove them and return the land empty.
The obligation is wajib based on harm prevention.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Shafi'i and Hanbali schools hold that removal is only required if stipulated in the contract; otherwise not.
They consider the contract absolute and no implied condition.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Their dalil: an absolute contract implies no removal obligation unless agreed; the lessee's possession is lawful until expiry.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafi: buildings/trees have no known end, so keeping them causes continuous harm to the landowner; crops are different because they have a known harvest time.
The distinction is based on fixed vs. indefinite benefit.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi, lessee is compelled to remove at his own cost; under Shafi'i/Hanbali, he may leave them unless owner compensates or removal was stipulated.
The practical difference is significant in absolute contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الاجارات
لده
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۱
عمارت بنانے اور درخت اگانے کے لئے زمین کرایہ پر لینے کا حکم
ويجوز ان يستاجر الساحة ليبنى فيها او ليغرس فيها نخلا او شجرا لانها منفعة تقصد بالاراضي ثم اذا انقضت مدة الاجارة لزمه ان يقلع البناء والغرس ويسلمها فارغة لانه لا نهاية لها ففى ابقائها اضرار بصاحب الارض بخلاف ما اذا انقضت المدة والزرع بقل حيث تترك باجر المثل الى زمان الادراك لان لها نهاية معلومة فامكن رعاية الجانبين قال الا ان يختار صاحب الارض ان يغرم له قيمة ذالك مقلوعا ويتملكه فله ذالک وهذا برضاء صاحب الغرس والشجر الا ان ينقص الارض بقلعها فحينئذ يتملكها بغير رضاه قال او يرضى بتركه على حاله فيكون البناء لهذا والارض لهذا لان الحق له فله ان لا يستوفيه. قال وفي الجامع الصغير اذا انقضت مدة الاجارة وفى الارض رطبة فانها تقلع لان الرطاب لا نهاية لها فاشبه الشجر
،
توضیح اللغة ساحه چوک، بیبنی (ض) بناء تعمیر کرنا، يغرس (ض) غرساً پودہ لگانا۔ نخل درخت خرما ، اضرار نقصان دینا بقل . سبزی ادراک اپنے وقت پر پہنچنا ، يغرم (س) غرما تاوان دینا ، مقلوع اکھڑا ہوا،قلع اکھاڑ نا مرطب سپست ۔ ترجمہ جائز ہے تیر زمین کو کرایہ پر لینا عمارت بنانے یا درخت خرما پھلدار درخت لگانے کے لئے کیونکہ یہ بھی ایسی منفعت ہے جو آراضی سے مقصود ہوتی ہے۔ پھر جب اجارہ کی مدت گزر جائے تو ضروری ہوگا مستاجر کے لئے یہ کہ اکھاڑ لے عمارت اور درخت اور حوالے کر دے زمین خالی۔ کیونکہ عمارت اور درخت کی کوئی انتہا نہیں تو اجارہ باقی رکھنے میں مالک زمین کو ضرر رسانی ہے بخلاف اس کے جب مدت گزرگئی اور حال یہ کہ کھیتی کچی سبز ہے کہ وہ پختہ ہونے تک اجر مثل پر چھوڑ دی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ کھیتی پکنے کی ایک انتہا معلوم ہے تو جانبین کی رعایت ممکن ہوئی۔ مگر یہ کہ اختیار کرے زمین والا اکھڑے ہوئے کی قیمت دے کر مالک ہو جاتا تو اس کو یہ اختیار ہے۔ اور یہ پودے اور درخت والے کی رضامندی سے ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ زمین ناقص ہو جاتی ہو اس کے اکھاڑنے سے کہ اس وقت زمین والا اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ مستاجر کی رضامندی کے بغیر ، یا راضی ہو جائے اس کو علی حالہ چھوڑنے پر ۔ پس عمارت اس کی ہوگی اور زمین اسکی ۔ کیونکہ حق تو مالک زمین کا ہے تو اس کو اختیار ہے کہ اپنا حق حاصل نہ کرے۔ اور جامع صغیر میں ہے کہ جب مدت اجارہ گزرگئی اور حال یہ کہ زمین
میں رطبہ ہے تو اس کو اکھاڑ لیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ رطاب کی کوئی انتہانہیں پس وہ درخت کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ تشريح قوله ويجوزان يستاجر ... الخ - اگر عمارت بنانے یا درخت لگانے کے لئے زمین کرائے پر لے تو درست ہے۔ اب مدت اجارہ تمام ہو جانے کے بعد مستاجر اپنی عمارت تو ڑ کر اور درخت اکھاڑ کر خالی زمین مالک کے حوالے کرے گا۔ یعنی اس کو اس پر مجبور کیا جائے گا اور زمین کا مالک نقصان کا ضامن بھی نہ ہوگا ۔ امام مالک اور امام مزنی شافعی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ امام شافعی اور امام احمد فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر انقضاء مدت پر اکھاڑنا شرط ہو تب تو یہی حکم ہے اور اگر عقد مطلق ہو تو اکھاڑنے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ الا یہ کہ مالک نقصان کا ضامن ہو ۔ ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ عمارت اور درخت کے لئے کوئی انتہا معلوم نہیں تو اجارہ باقی رکھنے میں مالک زمین کا ضرر ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے اگر زمین میں کھیتی کھڑی ہو اور مدت اجارہ گزرگئی ہو کہ وہ پختہ ہونے تک اجر مثل پر چھوڑ دی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اس کے پکنے
کی ایک انتہا معلوم ہے تو جانین کی رعایت ممکن ہے کہ مالک زمین کو کرائیل جائے گا اور مستاجر کو کھیتی پخت مل جائے گی ۔
كتاب الاجارات
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ قوله وفي الارض رطبة .... الخ - رطبہ ایک قسم کا نزم چارہ ہے جس کو فارسی میں سپست کہتے ہیں اور بعض نے اس کا ترجمہ گند نا کیا ہے اور شامی میں منقول ہے کہ کھیرے، لکڑی بینگن وغیرہ کو رطبہ کہتے ہیں۔ یہ ایک دفعہ کا بویا ہوا بہت دنوں تک رہتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کی جڑیں زمین میں عرصہ تک رہتی ہیں۔ سو اس کا حکم درخت کا سا ہے۔ یعنی مستاجر کے لئے اس کو اکھاڑ کر خالی زمین مالک کے حوالے کرنا لازم ہے۔ اس واسطے کہ جب رطبہ کی کوئی انتہاء نہ ہوئی اور وہ درخت کی مثل ہوگئی تو مدت اجارہ کے بعد اس کو اکھاڑ نا ضروری ہے بخلاف کھیتی کے کہ اگر مدت اجارہ ختم ہو جائے اور کھیتی کٹنے کا وقت نہ آئے تو مستاجر کو کھیتی کاٹنے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ بلکہ کٹنے کے وقت تک مہلت دی جائے گی اور زمین والے کو اجرت مثل دلائی جائے گی۔
قوله الان يختار .... الخ - اور اگر مالک زمین ٹوٹی ہوئی عمارت اور اکھڑے ہوئے درختوں کی قیمت دینے پر راضی ہو جائے تو یہ بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ پس قیمت دینے کے بعد وہ عمارت اور درختوں کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر مالک عمارت اور درختوں کو اپنی زمین پر رہنے دے تو یہ بھی جائز ہے۔ اس صورت میں زمین مالک کی رہے گی اور عمارت اور درخت مستاجر کے رہیں گے۔
Book of Ijarat. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu Sharh of Hidaya Volume 11. Ruling on leasing land for building or planting trees. It is permissible to lease an open space to build in it or to plant date palms or trees therein, because this is a benefit sought from lands. Then when the lease term expires, it is obligatory for him to remove the building and the plantation and surrender it empty, because they have no end; keeping them harms the landowner, unlike when the term expires and the crop is green, where it is left for an equivalent rent until harvest time because it has a known end, so it is possible to consider both sides. He said: Unless the landowner chooses to pay him the value of that removed and take ownership, then he has that right, but this is with the consent of the owner of the plantation and trees; unless the land is diminished by their removal, then he takes ownership without his consent. He said: Or he agrees to leave it as it is, then the building belongs to this one and the land to that one, because the right is his, so he may not enforce it. He said: In al-Jami' al-Saghir: When the lease term expires and there is moist fodder (ratbah) on the land, it is removed because moist fodder has no end, so it resembles trees. [Then Urdu vocabulary and translation follow: explanation of words and translation of the Arabic into Urdu.] Commentary on his statement: 'and it is permissible to lease...' - If one leases land for building or planting trees, it is valid. Now after the lease period ends, the lessee must demolish his building and uproot the trees and hand over the empty land to the owner; i.e., he will be compelled to do so and the landowner will not be liable for the loss. Imam Malik and Imam al-Muzani (Shafi'i) also hold this view. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad say that if removal upon expiry is a condition, then the same ruling applies; but if the contract is absolute, he will not be compelled to remove unless the owner guarantees the loss. We say that buildings and trees have no known end, so keeping them harms the landowner, unlike crops standing in the land when the lease expires; they are left for an equivalent rent until ripening because their ripening has a known end, so consideration of both sides is possible: the landowner will get rent and the lessee will get the ripe crop. [Page 42] Book of Ijarat. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu Sharh of Hidaya Volume 12. His statement: 'and on the land there is moist fodder (ratbah)...' - Ratbah is a type of fodder called 'sipist' in Persian; some translate it as 'gandana'; and in al-Shami it is reported that cucumber, wood, eggplant, etc. are called ratbah. It is sown once and remains for many days because its roots stay in the ground for a long time. So its ruling is like that of a tree: the lessee must uproot it and hand over the land empty. The reason is that ratbah has no end and it has become like a tree, so after the lease period, its removal is necessary, unlike crops: if the lease term ends and the crop is not yet ready for harvest, the lessee cannot be compelled to harvest it; rather, he will be given time until harvest and the landowner will be given the equivalent rent. His statement: 'unless he chooses...' - If the landowner agrees to pay the value of the demolished building and uprooted trees, that is possible. After paying the value, he becomes the owner of the building and trees. And if the owner allows the building and trees to remain on his land, that is also permissible. In that case, the land remains the owner's and the building and trees remain the lessee's.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the ruling on leasing land for building or planting trees. The Hanafi position (supported by Imam Malik and al-Muzani) is that it is permissible to lease land for such purposes, but upon expiry of the lease, the lessee must remove all structures and trees and return the land empty. The reason given is that buildings and trees have no fixed end (nihaayah), so allowing them to remain would cause continuous harm to the landowner. This is contrasted with crops (zar' baaqil), which have a known harvest time; for crops, the lessee is allowed to leave them until harvest with payment of the equivalent rent (ujrat al-mithl). The text then discusses three options for the landowner: (1) He may pay the value of the removed items and take ownership, but if the land is damaged by removal, he can take ownership without the lessee's consent. (2) He may agree to leave them as they are, in which case each party retains ownership of their respective property (land and building/trees). (3) The ruling from al-Jami' al-Saghir is that moist fodder (ratbah) is treated like trees because it has no fixed end. The commentary then clarifies that the Hanafi position is that the lessee is compelled to remove, while Shafi'i and Hanbali hold that compulsion only applies if removal was a condition in the contract. The Hanafi response is based on harm prevention (darrar) and the lack of a fixed end for buildings and trees.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijaarah): Lease contract for usufruct, permissible for known benefits like building on land.
قلع (qal'): Removal (uprooting) of buildings or trees from the land after lease expiry.
رطبہ (ratbah): Moist fodder or perennial plants like cucumber, eggplant that regrow from roots.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why must the lessee remove buildings and trees at the end of the lease, while crops may remain until harvest?
A) Because buildings and trees have no fixed end, causing continuous harm to the landowner.
B) Because the Shafi'i school requires removal of all structures.
C) Because the lease contract is invalid otherwise.
D) Because crops are less valuable than trees.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates removal of buildings and trees at lease end because they have no fixed end, while crops may remain until harvest because they do.

Leasing Animals for Riding or Carrying Loads
Ruling on leasing animals for riding or burden, with specifications on who may ride.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leasing animals for riding or carrying, explain the effect of an absolute vs specified contract, and distinguish the rule for real estate.

Core Idea
In leasing animals, the user becomes fixed once the lessee rides or designates one person; changing the user may incur liability.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents the Hanafi ruling on leasing quadrupeds (dawabb) for riding or carrying loads. The key principle is that the benefit (manfa'ah) is known and customary, making the contract permissible. However, the lessee's freedom to choose any rider is limited once he takes an action that specifies a particular user. This lesson unpacks the distinction between absolute and specified contracts, and how it applies to movable property versus real estate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what is being ruled upon and the basic hukm (permissible/ja'iz). Why is it permissible? Because the benefit is known and customary (manfa'ah ma'lumah ma'hudah).
The ruling is straightforward: leasing animals for riding or carrying is valid.
2
Understand the absolute contract (itlaq)
If the contract does not specify a rider (itlaq), the lessee may allow anyone to ride. But once he rides himself or allows one person, that user becomes specified (ta'ayyun) and cannot be changed later, because people differ in riding style and weight, affecting liability.
The same applies to leasing a garment for wearing.
3
Contrast with a specified contract
If the contract explicitly names a rider (e.g., 'on condition that Zayd rides'), the lessee must adhere to that. If he allows someone else and damage occurs, he is liable (daman). The specification is valid because the benefit varies with the user (yakhtalifu bikhtilaf al-musta'mil).
Liability arises from the violation of the condition.
4
Note the exception for real estate (aqaar)
For real estate (e.g., a house for residence), people do not differ significantly in use. Therefore, if the contract stipulates a specific resident, the lessee may still allow another resident because the restriction provides no real benefit. However, if the structure could be harmed (e.g., by heavy loads), that is treated separately.
This distinction is based on the variation (ikhtilaf) of the user.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
چوپاؤں کو سواری اور بوجھ لادنے کے لئے کرایہ پر لینے کا حکم
قال يجوز استيجار الدواب للركوب والحمل لانه منفعة معلومة معهودة فان اطلق الركوب جاز له ان يُركب من شاء عملا بالاطلاق ولكن اذا ركب بنفسه او اركب واحدا ليس له ان يركب غيره لانه تعين مرادا من الأصل والناس متفاوتون في الركوب فصار كانه نصّ على ركوبه و کذالک اذا استاجر ثوبا للبس واطلق فيما ذكرنا لاطلاق اللفظ وتفاوت الناس فى اللبس وان قال على ان يركبها فلان او يلبس الثوب فلان فاركبها غيره او البسه غيره فعطب كان ضامنا لان الناس يتفاوتون فى الركوب واللبس فصح التعيين وليس له ان يتعداه وكذالك كل ما يختلف باختلاف المستعمل لما ذكرنا فاما العقار وما لا يختلف باختلاف المستعمل اذا شرط سكنى واحد فله ان يُسكن غيره لان التقييد غير مفيد لعدم التفاوت والذى يضر بالبناء خارج على ما ذكرناه .
توضیح اللغـ اللغة ..... دواب جمع را به چوپایه، بر کب ارکاباً سوار کرنا ، ركب (ض) ركوباً - سوار بنا، لبس پہننا، عطب (س) عطباً ہلاک ہونا ، يتعداه تعدیا تجاوز کرنا عقار جائداد۔
ترجمہ اور جائز ہے جو پاؤں کو کرایہ پر لینا سوار ہونے اور بوجھ لادنے کے لئے ۔ کیونکہ یہ منفعت معلومہ معہودہ ہے۔ پس اگر مطلق رکھا سوار ہونے کو تو جائز ہے اس کے لئے یہ کہ سوار کرے جس کو چاہے۔ اطلاق پر عمل کرتے ہوئے لیکن جب وہ خود سوار ہو گیا یا اس نے کسی دوسرے کو سوار کیا تو اب کسی اور کو سوار نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ اصل اطلاق سے یہی مراد متعین ہوگئی اور لوگ چونکہ سواری میں متفاوت ہوتے ہیں تو گویا اس نے اس کی سواری کی تصریح کی تھی۔ اسی طرح اگر کپڑا اجرت پر لیا پہنے کے لئے اور پہنا مطلق رکھا۔ اطلاق لفظ اور پہنے میں لوگوں کے تفاوت کی وجہ سے اور اگر کہا کہ اس شرط پر کہ فلاں سوار ہو گا یا کپڑ افلاں شخص پہنے گا۔ پھر کسی اور کو سوار کیا یا کپڑا کسی اور کو
Ruling on leasing quadrupeds for riding and carrying loads. He said: It is permissible to lease animals for riding and carrying because it is a known customary benefit. If the riding is left absolute, it is permissible for him to have whomever he wishes ride, acting on the absolute wording. But when he rides himself or has one person ride, he may not let another ride, because it becomes specified as intended from the beginning, and people differ in riding, so it is as if he specified his own riding. Similarly, if he leases a garment for wearing and leaves it absolute, as we mentioned due to the absolute wording and people's variation in wearing. And if he says: 'On condition that so-and-so rides it' or 'so-and-so wears the garment,' then he has someone else ride it or wears it on someone else, and it is damaged, he is liable because people vary in riding and wearing, so the specification is valid, and he may not go beyond it. Similarly, everything that differs with the difference of the user, for the reason we mentioned. As for real estate (aqaar) and what does not differ with the difference of the user, if he stipulates the residence of one person, he may let another reside because the restriction is not beneficial due to lack of variation. And what harms the structure is excluded as we mentioned. [Then Urdu vocabulary and translation follow.]
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on leasing animals for riding or carrying loads. The Hanafi school deems it permissible because the benefit is known and customary. The key principle is that if the lease contract specifies riding in absolute terms (without naming a rider), the lessee may let anyone ride. However, once the lessee rides himself or lets one specific person ride, that person becomes the intended rider, and the lessee cannot change to another person because people vary in weight and riding style, making the user relevant. The same applies to leasing a garment for wearing. If the contract specifies a particular person (e.g., 'on condition that Zayd rides'), then the lessee must adhere to that specification; if he allows another person and damage occurs, he is liable. The reasoning is that the benefit varies with the user (yakhtalifu bikhtilaaf al-musta'mil), so specification matters. However, for real estate (like a house for residence), people do not differ significantly in use, so if a specific resident is named, the lessee may still allow another resident because the restriction is not meaningful. This distinction is important in Hanafi fiqh for determining liability.

Key Terms
دو اب (dawabb): Quadrupeds (animals) used for riding or carrying loads.
اطلاق (itlaq): Absolute or unrestricted contract without specifying the user.
تعين (ta'ayyun): Specification of the user by the lessee's action (riding himself or allowing one person).
عقار (aqaar): Real estate (e.g., house, land).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person leases a horse for riding with the explicit condition that 'only Ahmad rides it.' If the lessee allows Bakr to ride and the horse is injured, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The lessee is not liable because the contract is still valid.
B) The lessee is liable because he violated the specification.
C) The lessee may substitute riders freely; the condition is not effective.
D) The lessee is liable only if Ahmad was a lighter rider.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the user of a leased animal or garment becomes fixed once the lessee takes action, and violating a specified user leads to liability; however, for real estate, user specification is generally ineffective.

Ruling on Rutbah at the End of a Lease
Defines rutbah and states obligation to uproot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on rutbah at lease end and distinguish it from the ruling on annual crops.

Core Idea
Rutbah is like a tree: the lessee must uproot it; crops get a grace period until harvest.

This passage clarifies the obligations of a lessee when the lease ends and the land contains perennial vegetation (rutbah). Understanding this ruling helps you apply the correct fiqh rule to different types of plants, avoiding confusion with annual crops.

Guided Path
1
Define Rutbah
Identify what rutbah is: a perennial fodder that remains for years because its roots persist. Examples include cucumbers, gourds, and eggplants.
Rutbah is not a tree, but its legal status is likened to a tree due to its permanence.
2
State the Ruling
The lessee must uproot rutbah at lease end and hand over the land empty. This is because rutbah has no fixed harvest and its roots remain.
The obligation is to remove it entirely.
3
Compare with Crops
If the lease ends before crops are ready for harvest, the lessee is not forced to harvest. He is given time until harvest and pays ujrat al-mithl (market rent) for the extra period.
Crops have a natural harvest time; rutbah does not.
4
Apply the Distinction
Apply the rule: any perennial plant with no defined harvest is treated like rutbah; any annual crop with a harvest season is treated like crops.
Other perennial plants like trees follow similar logic (uproot or pay value).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الاجارات
قوله وفي الارض رطبة .... الخ - رطبہ ایک قسم کا نزم چارہ ہے جس کو فارسی میں سپست کہتے ہیں اور بعض نے اس کا ترجمہ گند نا کیا ہے اور شامی میں منقول ہے کہ کھیرے، لکڑی بینگن وغیرہ کو رطبہ کہتے ہیں۔ یہ ایک دفعہ کا بویا ہوا بہت دنوں تک رہتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کی جڑیں زمین میں عرصہ تک رہتی ہیں۔ سو اس کا حکم درخت کا سا ہے۔ یعنی مستاجر کے لئے اس کو اکھاڑ کر خالی زمین مالک کے حوالے کرنا لازم ہے۔ اس واسطے کہ جب رطبہ کی کوئی انتہاء نہ ہوئی اور وہ درخت کی مثل ہوگئی تو مدت اجارہ کے بعد اس کو اکھاڑ نا ضروری ہے بخلاف کھیتی کے کہ اگر مدت اجارہ ختم ہو جائے اور کھیتی کٹنے کا وقت نہ آئے تو مستاجر کو کھیتی کاٹنے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جا سکتا۔ بلکہ کٹنے کے وقت تک مہلت دی جائے گی اور زمین والے کو اجرت مثل دلائی جائے گی۔
قوله الان يختار .... الخ - اور اگر مالک زمین ٹوٹی ہوئی عمارت اور اکھڑے ہوئے درختوں کی قیمت دینے پر راضی ہو جائے تو یہ بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ پس قیمت دینے کے بعد وہ عمارت اور درختوں کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر مالک عمارت اور درختوں کو اپنی زمین پر رہنے دے تو یہ بھی جائز ہے۔ اس صورت میں زمین مالک کی رہے گی اور عمارت اور درخت مستاجر کے رہیں گے۔
And for land (that is) rutbah ... rutbah is a type of fodder, called 'sipast' in Persian, some translated as 'gandana'. In al-Shami it is transmitted that cucumbers, gourds, eggplants etc. are called rutbah. It is planted once and remains for many days because its roots remain in the ground. So its ruling is like that of a tree: the lessee must uproot it and hand over empty land to the owner. Because when rutbah has no end and became like a tree, after the lease period it is necessary to uproot it, unlike crops: if lease ends and harvest time not come, lessee cannot be forced to harvest; rather he is given time until harvest and landowner gets ujrat al-mithl. His statement: 'now he chooses...' - And if landowner agrees to pay value of broken building and uprooted trees, that is possible; after paying he becomes owner. And if he allows them to remain on his land, that is permissible; land remains his, building and trees remain lessee's.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a line from al-Hidayah. It defines 'rutbah' (perennial grass) and distinguishes it from annual crops. The ruling: the lessee must uproot rutbah at lease end because it has no fixed harvest and resembles a tree. For crops, if lease ends before harvest, lessee is given time until harvest and pays ujrat al-mithl. Then it covers landowner's options regarding structures/trees: he may pay value and own them, or allow them to remain while lessee retains ownership.

Key Terms
رطبة (rutbah): A type of perennial fodder/grass that remains for years, including cucumbers, gourds, eggplants etc.
اجرت مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The prevailing market rent for similar property when contractual rent is not applicable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on rutbah at the end of a lease?
A) The lessee must uproot it.
B) The lessee may leave it for the owner.
C) The lessee must pay its value.
D) The owner must uproot it.

Key Takeaway
Rutbah is treated like a tree: the lessee must uproot it at lease end; annual crops receive a grace period until harvest with ujrat al-mithl.

Hiring Animals: The Effect of Specifying the Rider
Explains rules for hiring animals and effect of specifying rider

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on hiring animals for riding/carrying and apply the rule that the first use specifies the intended user.

Core Idea
In a general hire contract, the first use specifies the user — substitution incurs liability.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains that hiring animals for riding or carrying is permissible because it is a known benefit. If the contract is absolute, the lessee may choose any rider. However, once he rides himself or assigns a specific rider, that rider becomes fixed, and he cannot substitute without liability. This principle also applies to hiring garments, while real estate is treated differently because use does not vary by user.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its permissibility
Hiring animals for riding or carrying is a valid lease because the benefit (manfa'ah) is known and customary. This is a condition for a valid ijara.
Know that a known benefit is essential to avoid gharar.
2
Analyze the absolute contract
If the contract does not specify a particular rider (itlaq), the lessee may let any person ride, acting on the absolute wording.
Absolute contract gives broad initial choice.
3
Determine the effect of first use
Once the lessee rides himself or lets one person ride, that person becomes the intended rider because people differ (tafawut) in riding style. He cannot then let another ride.
First use implicitly specifies the user for variable benefits.
4
Distinguish variable vs non-variable benefits
For real estate and things where use does not vary by user, specifying a particular tenant is ineffective, so the lessee may sublet. This is because the restriction is useless.
The key factor is whether the benefit is affected by who uses it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قال يجوز استيجار الدواب للركوب والحمل لانه منفعة معلومة معهودة فان اطلق الركوب جاز له ان يُركب من شاء عملا بالاطلاق ولكن اذا ركب بنفسه او اركب واحدا ليس له ان يركب غيره لانه تعين مرادا من الأصل والناس متفاوتون في الركوب فصار كانه نصّ على ركوبه و کذالک اذا استاجر ثوبا للبس واطلق فيما ذكرنا لاطلاق اللفظ وتفاوت الناس فى اللبس وان قال على ان يركبها فلان او يلبس الثوب فلان فاركبها غيره او البسه غيره فعطب كان ضامنا لان الناس يتفاوتون فى الركوب واللبس فصح التعيين وليس له ان يتعداه وكذالك كل ما يختلف باختلاف المستعمل لما ذكرنا فاما العقار وما لا يختلف باختلاف المستعمل اذا شرط سكنى واحد فله ان يُسكن غيره لان التقييد غير مفيد لعدم التفاوت والذى يضر بالبناء خارج على ما ذكرناه .

تشريح قوله استيجار الدواب ..... الخ - جانوروں کو سواری یا بار برداری کے لئے اجارہ پر لینا جائز ہے۔ اب اگر عقد مطلق ہو تو مستاجر جس کو چاہے سوار کر سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اگر وہ خود سوار ہو گیا یا اس نے دوسرے کو سوار کیا تو اس کے بعد دوسرے کو سوار نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ اصل اطلاق سے یہی مراد تعین ہو چکی اور سواری میں چونکہ لوگوں کا حال متفاوت ہوتا ہے۔ تو گویا اس نے سواری میں اسی شخص کو صریحا بیان کیا تھا۔ یہی حکم اجارہ ثوب کا ہے۔
Ruling on hiring animals for riding and carrying loads. He said: It is permissible to hire animals for riding and carrying because it is a known customary benefit. If he makes riding absolute, it is permissible for him to let ride whomever he wishes, acting on the absolute wording. But if he rides himself or lets one person ride, he cannot let another ride because that one became the intended person from the origin, and people differ in riding, so it is as if he specified his riding. Similarly, if he hires a garment for wearing and makes it absolute, due to the absolute wording and people's difference in wearing. And if he says 'on condition that so-and-so rides it' or 'so-and-so wears the garment', then he lets another ride or another wear it and it is destroyed, he is liable because people differ in riding and wearing, so the specification is valid and he cannot exceed it. And similarly everything that differs with difference of user. As for real estate and what does not differ with difference of user, if he stipulates one person's dwelling, he may let another dwell because the restriction is useless due to lack of difference. And what harms the building is excluded. Vocabulary: dawabb (animals), rakiba (to ride), labisa (to wear), atiba (to perish), yata'addahu (to exceed), 'iqar (real estate). Translation: It is permissible to hire animals for riding and carrying. If the contract is absolute, the lessee may let ride whomever he wishes. But if he rides himself or lets another ride, he cannot let another thereafter because the intended rider is determined by the initial action. Same for garment hire. Explanation: It is permissible to hire animals for riding or carrying. If absolute, lessee can choose rider. But if he rides himself or lets another, he cannot change because the intention is fixed. Same for garment.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the ruling on hiring animals for riding or carrying. The lease is valid because riding/carrying is a known benefit. If the contract is absolute (unrestricted), the lessee may choose any rider. However, once he rides himself or assigns someone, he cannot change to another because people vary in riding style, so the specified rider is effectively designated. Similarly for hiring a garment for wearing. If the lessee specifies a particular person and then substitutes, he is liable for damage. For real estate or things that don't vary with use, specifying a person is ineffective, so the lessee may sublet.

Key Terms
منفعة معلومة (manfa'ah ma'lumah): A known and specified benefit, a condition for valid lease.
اطلاق (itlaq): Absolute/unrestricted contract without specification of user.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Yes, with the owner's permission.
D) No, never.

Key Takeaway
In a hire contract for things that vary by user, the first use specifies the user, and substitution incurs liability.

Ruling on Specifying Load: Permissible and Prohibited Loads
ruling on permissible loads

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for what a hirer may load when the load type and quantity are specified.

Core Idea
You may load what is equal or less harmful, but not more harmful.

When you hire an animal to carry a specified load, the contract implies consent to the specified load. However, there is flexibility: you may substitute a load of equal or lesser harm, but not a more harmful one. This ruling protects the animal from excessive harm.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specified load
Look at what was agreed upon in terms of type and quantity, e.g., five qafiz of wheat.
2
Assess the proposed load's harm
Compare the harm of the proposed load to the specified load. Consider factors like weight, density, and distribution.
Example: iron is denser and harmful than cotton even at same weight.
3
Apply the ruling
If the proposed load is equally or less harmful, it is permissible. If more harmful, it is not permissible.
This applies even if the weight is the same, as harm can vary by type.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بوجھ کی نوعیت اور مقدار معلوم ہونا ضروری ہے یا نہیں
قال وان سمى نوعا وقدرا معلوما يحمله على الدابة مثل ان يقول خمسة اقفزة حنطة فله ان يحمل ما هو مثل الحنطة في الضرر او اقل كالشعير والسمسم لأنه دخل تحت الاذن لعدم التفاوت او لكونه خيرا من الأول وليس له ان يحمل ما هو اضر من الحنطة كالملح والحديد لانعدام الرضاء به وان استاجرها ليحمل عليها قطنا سماه فليس له ان يحمل عليها مثل وزنه حديدا لأنه ربما يكون اضر بالدابة فان الحديد يجتمع فى موضع من ظهره والقطن ينبسط على ظهره قال وان استاجرها ليركبها فاردف معه رجلا فعطبت ضمن نصف قیمتها ولا معتبر بالثقل لان الدابة قد يعقرها جهل الراكب الخفيف ويخف عليها ركوب الثقيل لعلمه بالفروسية ولان الآدمى غير موزون فلا يمكن معرفة الوزن فاعتبر عدد الراكب كعدد الجناة في الجنايات وان استاجرها ليحمل عليها مقدارا من الحنطة فحمل عليها اكثر منه فعطبت ضمن ما زاد الثقل لانها عطبت بما هو ماذون فيه ماهو غير ماذون فيه والسبب الثقل فانقسم عليهما الا اذا كان حملا لا يطيقه مثل تلك الدابة فحينئذ يضمن كل قيمتها لعدم الاذن فيها اصلا لخروجه عن العادة وان كبح الدابة بلجامها او ضربها فعطبت ضمن عند ابي حنيفة وقالا لا يضمن اذا فعل فعلا متعارفا لان المتعارف مما يدخل تحت مطلق العقد فكان حاصلا باذنه فلا يضمنه ولابي حنيفة ان الاذن مقيد بشرط السلامة اذ يتحقق السوق بدونهما وهما للمبالغة فيقيد بوصف السلامة كالمرور في الطريق
توضیح اللغة القفز جمع قفين ، حنطة گیہوں، ضرر نقصان، شعیر، جو سمسم تل ، ملح ،نمک ، حدید لوہا، قطن روئی ، ظهر پیٹھ، ينبسط انبساط پھیلنا ، اردف اردافا اپنے پیچھے سوار کرنا ، عطبت (س) عطباً بلاک ہونا ، ثقل لا يعقر (ض) عقراً زخمی کرنا ، فروسية شہسواری میں ماہر ہونا ، جناة جمع جانی بمعنی جنایت کرنے والا یسطیقه اطاقہ طاقت رکھنا کج (ف) کبحا چوپائے کولگام کھینچ کر ٹھہرانا، لجام گام ، سوق چلانا ۔
ترجمہ . اگر بیان کر دی نوع اور مقدار معلوم جولا دے گا چوپائے پر مثلاً کہا گیہوں کے پانچ قفیز تو وہ لا سکتا ہے ایسی چیز جو گیہوں
Is it necessary for the type and quantity of load to be known? He said: And if he specifies a known type and quantity to be loaded on the animal, such as saying five qafiz of wheat, then he may load what is like wheat in harm or less, like barley and sesame, because it falls under permission due to lack of difference or because it is better than the first. And he may not load what is more harmful than wheat, like salt and iron, due to lack of consent. And if he hires it to load cotton on it, specifying it, he may not load on it the equivalent weight of iron because perhaps it is more harmful to the animal: iron gathers in one spot of its back while cotton spreads out. He said: And if he hires it to ride, and he makes a man ride behind him, and it is injured, he is liable for half its price, with no consideration to weight because the animal may be injured by the ignorance of a light rider and may be light for a heavy rider due to his horsemanship, and because a human is not weighed so weight cannot be known; thus the number of riders is considered like the number of offenders in criminal cases. And if he hires it to load a quantity of wheat, and he loads more than that on it, and it is injured, he is liable for the excess weight because it was injured by what is permitted and by what is not permitted, and the cause is weight, so it is divided between them. Unless it is a load that such an animal cannot bear, then he is liable for its full price due to complete lack of permission because it is beyond custom. And if he restrains the animal by its bridle or hits it and it is injured, he is liable according to Abu Hanifa, and the two said: he is not liable if he does a customary action because the customary is included under the absolute contract, so it occurs with his permission and he is not liable. And for Abu Hanifa, permission is restricted by the condition of safety, since driving can be achieved without them, and they are for emphasis, so it is restricted by the condition of safety, like passing on the road. Vocabulary: qafaz (plural of qafiz), wheat, harm, barley, sesame, salt, iron, cotton, back, spreads, made ride behind, injured, weight, injure, horsemanship, offenders, can bear, bridle, rein, driving. Translation: If he specifies a known type and quantity to load on the animal, e.g., five qafiz of wheat, he may load what is like wheat in harm or less, such as... (cut off).
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage details rules when hiring an animal for loading. If load type and quantity are specified, the hirer cannot load something more harmful, but may load something equal or less harmful. If a rider brings a second person and animal is harmed, liability is half the price, regardless of weight, because riders vary in skill. For exceeding specified weight, liability is proportional; if beyond animal's capacity, full liability. Then a dispute: If hirer pulls bridle or hits animal customarily, Abu Hanifa says liable because permission conditional on safety; Sahibayn say not liable because customary actions are included in contract. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
قفز (qafaz): A measure of volume for grain, e.g., wheat.
حنطة (hintah): Wheat.
شعير (sha'ir): Barley.
سمسم (simsim): Sesame.
ملح (milh): Salt.
حديد (hadid): Iron.
قطن (qutn): Cotton.
ضرر (darar): Harm, damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A hirer specifies a load of five qafiz of wheat. Which of the following loads is NOT permissible?
A) Five qafiz of barley
B) Four qafiz of wheat and one qafiz of sesame
C) Five qafiz of salt
D) Five qafiz of rice (assuming rice is similar harm)

Key Takeaway
When hiring an animal for a specified load, you may substitute a load of equal or lesser harm, but not a more harmful one.

Liability for Extra Rider and Excess Weight
liability rules for exceeding hire terms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine liability when a hirer exceeds the agreed terms of hire for an animal.

Core Idea
Extra rider triggers half liability; excess weight triggers proportional liability; overload beyond capacity triggers full liability.

In addition to restrictions on load type, a hirer must not exceed the agreed number of riders or weight. This lesson covers the specific liability rules for such breaches, including the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the breach
Determine whether the hirer added an extra rider or exceeded the agreed weight.
2
Assess the liability
For extra rider: liability is half the animal's value. For excess weight: liability is proportional to the excess contribution to harm.
If the overload is beyond the animal's capacity, full liability applies.
3
Apply the rule
Calculate liability accordingly.

Source Text

بوجھ کی نوعیت اور مقدار معلوم ہونا ضروری ہے یا نہیں
قال وان سمى نوعا وقدرا معلوما يحمله على الدابة مثل ان يقول خمسة اقفزة حنطة فله ان يحمل ما هو مثل الحنطة في الضرر او اقل كالشعير والسمسم لأنه دخل تحت الاذن لعدم التفاوت او لكونه خيرا من الأول وليس له ان يحمل ما هو اضر من الحنطة كالملح والحديد لانعدام الرضاء به وان استاجرها ليحمل عليها قطنا سماه فليس له ان يحمل عليها مثل وزنه حديدا لأنه ربما يكون اضر بالدابة فان الحديد يجتمع فى موضع من ظهره والقطن ينبسط على ظهره قال وان استاجرها ليركبها فاردف معه رجلا فعطبت ضمن نصف قیمتها ولا معتبر بالثقل لان الدابة قد يعقرها جهل الراكب الخفيف ويخف عليها ركوب الثقيل لعلمه بالفروسية ولان الآدمى غير موزون فلا يمكن معرفة الوزن فاعتبر عدد الراكب كعدد الجناة في الجنايات وان استاجرها ليحمل عليها مقدارا من الحنطة فحمل عليها اكثر منه فعطبت ضمن ما زاد الثقل لانها عطبت بما هو ماذون فيه ماهو غير ماذون فيه والسبب الثقل فانقسم عليهما الا اذا كان حملا لا يطيقه مثل تلك الدابة فحينئذ يضمن كل قيمتها لعدم الاذن فيها اصلا لخروجه عن العادة وان كبح الدابة بلجامها او ضربها فعطبت ضمن عند ابي حنيفة وقالا لا يضمن اذا فعل فعلا متعارفا لان المتعارف مما يدخل تحت مطلق العقد فكان حاصلا باذنه فلا يضمنه ولابي حنيفة ان الاذن مقيد بشرط السلامة اذ يتحقق السوق بدونهما وهما للمبالغة فيقيد بوصف السلامة كالمرور في الطريق
توضیح اللغة القفز جمع قفين ، حنطة گیہوں، ضرر نقصان، شعیر، جو سمسم تل ، ملح ،نمک ، حدید لوہا، قطن روئی ، ظهر پیٹھ، ينبسط انبساط پھیلنا ، اردف اردافا اپنے پیچھے سوار کرنا ، عطبت (س) عطباً بلاک ہونا ، ثقل لا يعقر (ض) عقراً زخمی کرنا ، فروسية شہسواری میں ماہر ہونا ، جناة جمع جانی بمعنی جنایت کرنے والا یسطیقه اطاقہ طاقت رکھنا کج (ف) کبحا چوپائے کولگام کھینچ کر ٹھہرانا، لجام گام ، سوق چلانا ۔
ترجمہ . اگر بیان کر دی نوع اور مقدار معلوم جولا دے گا چوپائے پر مثلاً کہا گیہوں کے پانچ قفیز تو وہ لا سکتا ہے ایسی چیز جو گیہوں
Is it necessary for the type and quantity of load to be known? He said: And if he specifies a known type and quantity to be loaded on the animal, such as saying five qafiz of wheat, then he may load what is like wheat in harm or less, like barley and sesame, because it falls under permission due to lack of difference or because it is better than the first. And he may not load what is more harmful than wheat, like salt and iron, due to lack of consent. And if he hires it to load cotton on it, specifying it, he may not load on it the equivalent weight of iron because perhaps it is more harmful to the animal: iron gathers in one spot of its back while cotton spreads out. He said: And if he hires it to ride, and he makes a man ride behind him, and it is injured, he is liable for half its price, with no consideration to weight because the animal may be injured by the ignorance of a light rider and may be light for a heavy rider due to his horsemanship, and because a human is not weighed so weight cannot be known; thus the number of riders is considered like the number of offenders in criminal cases. And if he hires it to load a quantity of wheat, and he loads more than that on it, and it is injured, he is liable for the excess weight because it was injured by what is permitted and by what is not permitted, and the cause is weight, so it is divided between them. Unless it is a load that such an animal cannot bear, then he is liable for its full price due to complete lack of permission because it is beyond custom. And if he restrains the animal by its bridle or hits it and it is injured, he is liable according to Abu Hanifa, and the two said: he is not liable if he does a customary action because the customary is included under the absolute contract, so it occurs with his permission and he is not liable. And for Abu Hanifa, permission is restricted by the condition of safety, since driving can be achieved without them, and they are for emphasis, so it is restricted by the condition of safety, like passing on the road. Vocabulary: qafaz (plural of qafiz), wheat, harm, barley, sesame, salt, iron, cotton, back, spreads, made ride behind, injured, weight, injure, horsemanship, offenders, can bear, bridle, rein, driving. Translation: If he specifies a known type and quantity to load on the animal, e.g., five qafiz of wheat, he may load what is like wheat in harm or less, such as... (cut off).
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage details rules when hiring an animal for loading. If load type and quantity are specified, the hirer cannot load something more harmful, but may load something equal or less harmful. If a rider brings a second person and animal is harmed, liability is half the price, regardless of weight, because riders vary in skill. For exceeding specified weight, liability is proportional; if beyond animal's capacity, full liability. Then a dispute: If hirer pulls bridle or hits animal customarily, Abu Hanifa says liable because permission conditional on safety; Sahibayn say not liable because customary actions are included in contract. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
عطب (atab): Injury or destruction of the animal.
ثقل (thiqal): Weight.
فروسية (furusiyyah): Horsemanship, skill in riding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hirer loads an extra 10% weight on a hired camel (within its capacity) and the camel is injured, what is the liability?
A) Full value
B) Half value
C) Proportional to the excess weight's contribution
D) No liability if the camel would have been injured anyway

Key Takeaway
Liability for exceeding hire terms depends on the nature of the breach: extra rider = half value; excess cargo = proportional; overload beyond capacity = full value.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Liability for Customary Hitting and Pulling
intra-Hanafi dispute on liability for customary actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding liability for customary actions on a hired animal.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa says hitting/pulling triggers liability; the Sahibayn say no if customary.

Even within the Hanafi school, there is a notable disagreement on whether a hirer who performs customary actions like pulling the bridle or hitting the animal is liable if the animal is injured. This dispute hinges on the nature of permission in the contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the action
The hirer pulls the bridle or hits the animal in a customary manner.
Customary means the usual way of handling animals.
2
State Abu Hanifa's view
He holds the hirer liable because permission is conditional on safety. Such actions are not necessary for driving, so they are restricted by the safety condition.
3
State the Sahibayn's view
They hold no liability because customary actions are included under the absolute contract and occur with permission.
4
Analyze the evidence
Abu Hanifa argues that driving can be done without hitting, so hitting is for emphasis and thus subject to the safety condition. The Sahibayn argue that customary actions are part of the contract.
5
Note the practical consequence
According to Abu Hanifa, if the animal dies, the hirer pays full price. According to the Sahibayn, no compensation if the action is customary.

Hiring Animals: Permissibility and Binding Specification
Commentary on the ruling of hiring animals and binding effect of specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on hiring animals for riding or carrying loads, and explain why specification of the rider or load becomes binding after designation.

Core Idea
Once the hirer rides or assigns a rider, the specification is set; he cannot change it later.

This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah clarifies a practical issue in ijarah: when you hire an animal without specifying who rides, you may choose initially. But as soon as you yourself ride or designate someone, that choice becomes binding. The same principle applies to hiring a garment. Understanding this ruling prevents disputes between the hirer and the owner.

Guided Path
1
Name the act and its category
Identify the act: hiring an animal (istījār al-dawābb) is a contract of ijarah. The passage first states the permissibility of this contract.
It is a mu'amalah contract, not an ibadah.
2
Identify the hukm level
The default ruling for hiring animals is mubah (permissible). There is no obligation; it is allowed by default.
This is the strong default in Hanafi fiqh for mu'amalat.
3
Understand the effect of absolute contract
If the contract is absolute (without specifying the rider or load), the hirer may choose any rider or load initially. This is a right given to the hirer.
'Absolute' means the usufruct is not restricted to a particular person or thing.
4
Recognize when specification becomes binding
Once the hirer himself rides or assigns a specific rider and that rider rides, the specification becomes fixed. After that, the hirer cannot change to another rider. The same applies to loads and garments.
The rationale: people's conditions differ, so the value of the usufruct varies with the user.
5
Apply the analogy to garments
The passage explicitly extends the same ruling to hiring a garment (ijārat al-thawb): once worn by a specific person, it cannot be given to another to wear without a new agreement.
This shows the principle is general for usufructs that vary with users.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشريح قوله استيجار الدواب ..... الخ - جانوروں کو سواری یا بار برداری کے لئے اجارہ پر لینا جائز ہے۔ اب اگر عقد مطلق ہو تو مستاجر جس کو چاہے سوار کر سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اگر وہ خود سوار ہو گیا یا اس نے دوسرے کو سوار کیا تو اس کے بعد دوسرے کو سوار نہیں کر سکتا۔ کیونکہ اصل اطلاق سے یہی مراد تعین ہو چکی اور سواری میں چونکہ لوگوں کا حال متفاوت ہوتا ہے۔ تو گویا اس نے سواری میں اسی شخص کو صریحا بیان کیا تھا۔ یہی حکم اجارہ ثوب کا ہے۔
Explanation of his statement: 'Hiring animals ... etc' - It is permissible to hire animals for riding or carrying loads. Now if the contract is absolute, the hirer may have whoever he wants ride. But if he himself rode or had someone else ride, then after that he cannot have another ride. Because from the absolute wording, this designation is intended, and since people's conditions differ in riding, it is as if he explicitly stated that person for riding. The same ruling applies to the hire of a garment.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a matn statement about hiring animals. It states the basic ruling: hiring animals for riding or carrying loads is permissible. If the contract is absolute (without specifying who rides or what load), the hirer can choose. However, once the hirer himself rides or assigns a rider, the specification is set, and he cannot change to someone else because riding conditions vary with different people. Similarly, for garments, once specified, it cannot be changed.

Key Terms
استيجار الدواب (istījār al-dawābb): Hiring of animals for riding or carrying loads.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hires an animal for riding without specifying who will ride, and then he rides it himself, can he later let another person ride it?
A) Yes, because the contract is absolute.
B) No, because he has specified himself as the rider.
C) Yes, if the animal is not harmed.
D) No, but only if he pays extra.

Key Takeaway
In an absolute hire contract for an animal or garment, specification of the user becomes binding after the first use, and cannot be changed unilaterally.

Liability for Overloading and Striking Hired Animals
Details rulings on load specification, overloading, and liability for striking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on load specification, overloading, and liability for striking a hired animal, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on customary actions.

Core Idea
A hirer's liability depends on whether the action is within the agreed permission or customary usage; overloading beyond capacity and non-customary striking incur full compensation.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses common disputes in ijarah contracts for animals: what loads are permissible, what happens if the hirer overloads or gives a pillion ride, and whether striking or pulling reins triggers liability. The text presents the Hanafi position with a key dispute between Abu Hanifa and his disciples, the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
List the different scenarios: load specification, pillion ride, overloading, striking/pulling. Note the hukm for each: permissible/similar loads, half-value liability, proportional compensation, and liability dispute.
2
Analyze load specification
Understand that if type and weight are specified, the hirer may only carry loads of equal or lesser harm. Cotton vs iron example illustrates that distribution of weight matters.
3
Analyze pillion ride and overloading
For pillion ride: liability is half-value regardless of weight. For overloading: liability is proportional to excess weight unless load is beyond animal's capacity; then full liability.
The rationale: number of riders is considered like number of criminals; weight not measurable.
4
Examine the striking dispute
Abu Hanifa: hirer is liable even for customary striking because permission is conditioned on safety. Sahibayn: customary actions are included in the contract, so no liability.
The textual operation is expansion_probe: the jussive 'let him not' implies restriction.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
According to Durr al-Mukhtar, the fatwa is on the view of the Sahibayn (no liability for customary actions). This is the operative ruling for practice.
The ijtihad here is based on custom and the principle of inclusion under absolute contract.

Source Text

بوجھ کی نوعیت اور مقدار معلوم ہونا ضروری ہے یا نہیں

قال وان سمى نوعا وقدرا معلوما يحمله على الدابة مثل ان يقول خمسة اقفزة حنطة فله ان يحمل ما هو مثل الحنطة في الضرر او اقل كالشعير والسمسم لأنه دخل تحت الاذن لعدم التفاوت او لكونه خيرا من الأول وليس له ان يحمل ما هو اضر من الحنطة كالملح والحديد لانعدام الرضاء به وان استاجرها ليحمل عليها قطنا سماه فليس له ان يحمل عليها مثل وزنه حديدا لأنه ربما يكون اضر بالدابة فان الحديد يجتمع فى موضع من ظهره والقطن ينبسط على ظهره قال وان استاجرها ليركبها فاردف معه رجلا فعطبت ضمن نصف قیمتها ولا معتبر بالثقل لان الدابة قد يعقرها جهل الراكب الخفيف ويخف عليها ركوب الثقيل لعلمه بالفروسية ولان الآدمى غير موزون فلا يمكن معرفة الوزن فاعتبر عدد الراكب كعدد الجناة في الجنايات وان استاجرها ليحمل عليها مقدارا من الحنطة فحمل عليها اكثر منه فعطبت ضمن ما زاد الثقل لانها عطبت بما هو ماذون فيه ماهو غير ماذون فيه والسبب الثقل فانقسم عليهما الا اذا كان حملا لا يطيقه مثل تلك الدابة فحينئذ يضمن كل قيمتها لعدم الاذن فيها اصلا لخروجه عن العادة وان كبح الدابة بلجامها او ضربها فعطبت ضمن عند ابي حنيفة وقالا لا يضمن اذا فعل فعلا متعارفا لان المتعارف مما يدخل تحت مطلق العقد فكان حاصلا باذنه فلا يضمنه ولابي حنيفة ان الاذن مقيد بشرط السلامة اذ يتحقق السوق بدونهما وهما للمبالغة فيقيد بوصف السلامة كالمرور في الطريق

توضیح اللغة القفز جمع قفين ، حنطة گیہوں، ضرر نقصان، شعیر، جو سمسم تل ، ملح ،نمک ، حدید لوہا، قطن روئی ، ظهر پیٹھ، ينبسط انبساط پھیلنا ، اردف اردافا اپنے پیچھے سوار کرنا ، عطبت (س) عطباً بلاک ہونا ، ثقل لا يعقر (ض) عقراً زخمی کرنا ، فروسية شہسواری میں ماہر ہونا ، جناة جمع جانی بمعنی جنایت کرنے والا یسطیقه اطاقہ طاقت رکھنا کج (ف) کبحا چوپائے کولگام کھینچ کر ٹھہرانا، لجام گام ، سوق چلانا ۔

ترجمہ . اگر بیان کر دی نوع اور مقدار معلوم جولا دے گا چوپائے پر مثلاً کہا گیہوں کے پانچ قفیز تو وہ لا سکتا ہے ایسی چیز جو گیہوں

۴۳
كتاب الاجارات
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ جیسی ہو ضرر میں اس سے کم ہو۔ جیسے جو اور تل ، کیونکہ یہ اجازت کے تحت میں داخل ہے تفاوت نہ ہونے یا اول سے بہتر ہونے کی وجہ سے اور اس کو یہ اختیار نہیں کہ لادے ایسی چیز جو گیہوں سے زیادہ مضر ہو۔ جیسے نمک اور لوہا، ان کی رضا مندی نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اگر کرایہ پر لیا جانور اس لئے کہ اس پر روئی لا دے گا جس کا وزن بیان کر دیا تو اس کو یہ اختیار نہیں کہ اس کے ہم وزن لوہا لا د لے ۔ کیونکہ بسا اوقات لو ہا اس کو زیادہ مضر ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ لوہا مجمع ہو جاتا ہے اس کی پیٹھ پر ایک ہی جگہ اور روئی اس کی پیٹھ پر پھیل جاتی ہے۔ اگر کرایہ پر لیا چوپایہ سواری کے لئے اور اپنے پیچھے دوسرے کو سوار کر لیا اور وہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو اس کی نصف قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا اور بوجھ کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ کبھی ہلکے سوار کی نادانی چوپایہ کو خستہ کر دیتی ہے اور کبھی بھاری آدمی کی سواری اس پر خفیف ہوتی ہے اس کی شہسواری جانے کی وجہ سے اور اس لئے کہ آدمی وزنی چیز نہیں ہے تو اس کا وزن پہنچانا غیر ممکن ہے تو سواروں کی گنتی معتبر ہوئی جیسے جنایات میں مجرموں کی گفتی، اگر کرایہ پر لیا گیہوں کی ایک مقدار لادنے کے لئے پھر اس سے زیادہ لادا اور وہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو زائدہ بوجھ کے بقدر ضامن ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ ایسے بوجھ سے تلف ہوا جس میں وہ ماذون ہے اور جس میں ماذون نہیں ہے اور سبب یہی بوجھ ہے تو وہ ان دونوں پر تقسیم ہو گا۔ مگر جب کہ اتنا بوجھ ہو کہ اس کو ایسا جانور نہیں اٹھا سکتا تو اس وقت ضامن ہو گا کل قیمت کا کیونکہ اس کی اجازت بالکل نہیں عادت سے باہر ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ اگر کھینچا چوپایہ اس کی لگام سے بار اس کو مارا اور وہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو ضامن ہوگا امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ ضامن نہ ہو گا جب کہ اس نے متعارف فعل کیا ہو۔ کیونکہ متعارف فعل مطلق عقد کے تحت میں داخل ہوتا ہے تو اس کی اجازت سے ہو۔ لہذا اس کا ضامن نہ ہوگا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اجازت شرط سلامتی کے ساتھ مقید ہے کیونکہ چلانا ان کے بغیر بھی ہو سکتا ہے اور مارنا یا باگ کھینچنا تو تیز چلانے کے لئے ہوتا ہے۔ پس اجازت وصف سلامتی کے ساتھ مقید ہوگی جیسے راہ گزرنے میں ہے۔

تشریح قوله وان سمى نوعاً ... الخ - ایک شخص نے کوئی جانور کرایہ پر لیا اور اس پر جو بو جھلا دے گا اس کی نوع اور مقدار بیان کر دی۔ مثلاً یہ کہ دومن گیہوں لا دے گا۔ تو وہ اس پر گیہوں جیسی اور کوئی چیز مثلاً دو من جو بھی لا دسکتا ہے۔ اسی طرح جو اس سے ہلکی ہو جیسے قتل وغیرہ وہ بھی لا سکتا ہے دومن ، لیکن جو چیز گیہوں سے زیادہ نقصان دہ ہو وہ نہیں لا سکتا جیسے لوہا اور نمک وغیرہ کیونکہ موجر اس سے راضی نہیں ہے۔
قوله وان كبح الداية ... الخ - اگر متاجر کے مارنے یا لگام کھینچنے سے سواری ہلاک ہوگئی تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک مستاجر پر کل قیمت کا تاوان آئے گا۔ صاحبین اور ائمہ ثلاثہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر اس نے ایسی مار ماری یا اس طرح لگام کھینچی جو دستور عرف کے خلاف ہے تو تا وان لا زم ہوگا ورنہ نہیں۔ کیونکہ جو کام متعارف ہو وہ مطلق عقد کے تحت میں داخل ہوتا ہے تو یہ فعل اس کی اجازت سے پایا گیا لہذا ضامن نہ ہو گا۔
قوله ولابي حنيفة .... الخ - امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مالک کی طرف سے اجازت مقید بشرط سلامتی ہے اور اس نے اس کے خلف کیا ہے کیونکہ ایسی مار مارنے اور لگام کھینچنے کے بغیر چلانا ممکن تھا۔ مارنا اور باگ کھینچا تو تیز دوڑانے کے لئے ہوتا ہے۔ پس اس میں اجازت شرط سلامتی کے ساتھ مقید ہے جیسے عام راستہ میں چلانا جائز ہے بشرطیکہ سلامتی کے ساتھ ہو۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر کسی کا نقصان کرے تو ضامن ہوگا۔ درمختار میں ہے کہ فتوی صاحبین کے قول پر ہے اور غالیہ البیان میں تمہ کے حوالہ سے منقول ہے کہ امام ابو
Whether it is necessary to know the type and amount of load. He said: If he specified a type and known amount to be carried on the animal, for example he said five qafiz of wheat, then he may carry something similar to wheat in harm or less, like barley and sesame, because it falls under the permission due to lack of difference or because it is better than the first. He may not carry something more harmful than wheat, like salt and iron, because of lack of consent. If he hired it to carry cotton which he specified, he may not carry iron of similar weight, because it may be more harmful to the animal; iron concentrates in one spot on its back while cotton spreads out. He said: If he hired it to ride and he gave a man a pillion ride and it perished, he is liable for half its value, and weight is not considered because the animal may be injured by the ignorance of a light rider, while a heavy rider may be easy on it due to his knowledge of horsemanship, and because a person is not weighed so weight cannot be known; so the number of riders is considered like the number of criminals in crimes. And if he hired it to carry a quantity of wheat and he carried more than that on it and it perished, he is liable for the excess weight because it perished by something permitted and something not permitted, and the cause is weight, so it is apportioned between them, unless the load is such that such an animal cannot bear it, in which case he is liable for full value because there is no permission at all due to it being beyond custom. And if he pulled the animal's reins or struck it and it perished, he is liable according to Abu Hanifa. Both said: He is not liable if he did a customary act, because the customary is included under the absolute contract, so it occurred with his permission, thus he is not liable. Abu Hanifa's proof: Permission is conditioned upon safety, because driving can be achieved without these, and they are for intensification, so it is conditioned upon safety like passing through the road. Vocabulary explanation. Translation: ... (continues with Urdu translation and commentary).
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rulings on the liability of a hirer who causes destruction of a hired animal through overloading or physical actions like striking or pulling reins. It first discusses specification of load: if the type and weight are specified, the hirer may only carry loads similar or lighter in harm, not heavier. It then addresses the case of giving a pillion ride: if the hirer gives a pillion ride without permission and the animal dies, he is liable for half the value regardless of weight, because the skilfulness of the rider matters. For overloading: if the hirer loads more than agreed and the animal dies, he is liable for the portion attributed to the excess weight; but if the load is beyond the animal's capacity, he is fully liable. Finally, there is a dispute: Abu Hanifa holds the hirer liable for striking or pulling reins even if customary, while the Sahibayn hold no liability if the act is customary. The text notes that the fatwa according to Durr al-Mukhtar is on the view of the Sahibayn.

Key Terms
متعارف (muta'ārif): Customary; action that is conventionally done.
ضامن (ḍāmin): Liable; responsible for compensation.
اذن (idhn): Permission; consent of the owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, if a hirer pulls the reins of a hired mule in a customary manner and the mule dies, what is the ruling?
A) The hirer must pay full compensation.
B) The hirer must pay half the value.
C) The hirer is not liable.
D) The hirer must pay only if the mule was weak.

Key Takeaway
The hirer of an animal is liable for damage caused by overloading or non-customary striking, but customary actions like light striking are included in the contract per the relied-upon view.
