Tailor's Liability for Sewing a Different Garment: Choice or Compensation?
Analysis of ruling when tailor sews a qabā' instead of requested qamīṣ

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah ruling when a tailor sews a qabā' instead of a qamīṣ, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the chosen position to similar cases.

Core Idea
The owner may choose to accept the altered garment with fair wage or demand compensation—a balance of benefit and contract specifics.

When a tailor fulfills an order in a different form, the law must balance the owner's interest with the tailor's effort. This passage from the Sharh al-Hidayah presents a dispute within the Hanafi school: does the owner have a choice to accept the garment with fair wage, or must he take compensation? The resolution hinges on the similarity of benefit and the nature of the contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the initial ruling
The owner gives cloth to a tailor to sew a qamīṣ (shirt) for a named wage of one dirham. The tailor sews a qabā' (cloak). The Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah states that the owner has a choice: either accept the qabā' and pay its fair wage (ujrat al-mithl) capped at the named wage, or demand compensation (tāwān) for the cloth's value.
The fair wage cannot exceed the agreed wage because the contract is void (ijārah fāsidah) and ujrat al-mithl is capped by the musammā.
2
Understand the opposing position
A narration from Imam Abu Hanifa (via Hasan ibn Ziyād) holds that the owner has no choice; he can only demand compensation. This is because the qabā' is of a different genre (jins) from the qamīṣ, making the tailor a usurper (ghāṣib).
This is a weaker narration (nawādir) and not the relied-upon position in the school.
3
Analyze the reasoning for the Ẓāhir's view
The Ẓāhir argues that the qabā' can be tied at the waist and used like a shirt, so there is partial conformity. The owner may incline to whichever side he wishes—acceptance or rejection—but since conformity is incomplete, he must pay the fair wage (not the named wage) if he accepts. The named wage acts as a cap.
The reasoning is based on similarity in benefit: both garments cover the body and have sleeves and a skirt.
4
Examine the analogy with the basin and pitcher
The text draws an analogy: if a person orders a brass basin (ṭast) to be made, but the craftsman makes a pitcher (kūz) instead, the owner has a choice. The common illa is that the material is the same and the benefit is similar (holding water). Similarly, the cloth is the same and both qamīṣ and qabā' serve to cover the upper body.
This qiyas shows that the Hanafi method uses similarity in benefit to grant choice.
5
Apply the ruling to a more extreme case (trousers)
If the tailor sews a sarāwīl (trousers) instead of a qabā', the majority opinion (al-aṣaḥḥ) still gives the owner a choice due to unity in the basic benefit (covering the body). The disparity is not enough to eliminate choice.
This extension demonstrates the principle's scope: as long as the basic benefit (covering) is present, choice remains.

تشریح قوله و من دفع ... الخ ۔ کسی نے درزی کو ایک کپڑا دیا۔ تا کہ وہ ایک درہم کے عوض میں اس کی قمیص سی دے ۔ پس الخ۔ درزی نے اس کپڑے کی قبا سی دی تو کپڑے کے مالک کو اختیار ہے چاہے درزی سے اپنے کپڑے کی قیمت کا تاوان لے (اس صورت میں درزی اس قباء کا مالک ہو جائے گا ) اور چاہے اس سے قباء لے کر اس کا اجر مثل دیدے۔ مگر اجر مثل ایک درہم سے زیادہ نہ ہوگا۔

فائدہ قباء میں صرف دو تہ ہوتی ہیں اور کبھی اس کے درمیان میں بھیراؤ بھی ہوتا ہے اور یہ بظاہر قمیص کے خلاف ہے جیسا کہ روایت نوادر میں ہے۔ لیکن ظاہر الروایہ میں قباء جنس قمیص کے خلاف نہیں ہے۔ ورنہ تاوان کے علاوہ دوسرا اختیار نہ ہوتا۔ اسی لئے بعض مشائخ نے قباء سے کرتا مراد لیا۔ کیونکہ اس کو اگر آگے سے چاک کر دیا جائے تو وہ قباء ہو جاتا ہے نیز بلحاظ منفعت بھی گویا دونوں ہم جنس ہیں کیونکہ قباء وقمیص میں سے ہر ایک میں آستینیں کھلی اور دامن ہوتا ہے۔ قوله و وجه الظاهر الخ - ظاہر الروایہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قباء ایک لحاظ سے قمیص کے خلاف ہے اور ایک اعتبار سے قمیص ہے
One gave cloth to a tailor to sew a shirt for him for a dirham, he sewed a qabā'. The owner has the option: if he wishes, he makes him liable for the value of the cloth; if he wishes, he takes the qabā' and gives him its fair wage, and it should not exceed a dirham. It is said its meaning is the qurṭaq which has one fold because it is used like a qabā'. And it is said it is applied generally because the two are close in benefit. From Abu Hanifa: he is liable without choice, because the qabā' is contrary to the genus of the shirt. The apparent position: it is a shirt in one respect, because one ties its middle and benefits from it like a shirt, so there is conformity and opposition; he may incline to whichever side he wishes, except that the fair wage is wajib due to deficiency in the conformity, and it does not exceed the named dirham, as is the rule in all void leases, as we will explain in its chapter, God willing. And if it was a pair of trousers while he had ordered a qabā', it is said he is liable without choice due to disparity in benefit; the more correct is that he has a choice due to unity in the basis of benefit, and it becomes like the case when one orders a basin of brass to be beaten and he makes a pitcher; he has a choice. So is this. Explanation: the tailor's trade, to sew (ṣād ḍād), a garment. Qabā' is a garment worn over clothes, qurṭaq is a shirt, fold. Middle, between; sarāwīl is plural of sirwāl, trousers; ṭast is a copper vessel for washing hands, like a basin; kūz is a pitcher. Translation: Someone gave cloth to a tailor to sew a shirt for him for a dirham; he sewed a qabā'. So the owner has the option: either take the value of the cloth as compensation or take the qabā' and give its fair wage, which will not exceed a dirham. It is said that it is applied generally because qabā' and shirt are close in benefit. And from Imam Abu Hanifa there is a narration that the owner will take compensation without choice because qabā' is contrary to the genus of shirt. Because it is tied in the middle and benefit is derived like a shirt. So there is both conformity and opposition, so he may incline to whichever side he wishes, but the fair wage is wajib due to deficiency in the conformity, and it does not exceed the stated dirham. As is the ruling in other void leases, as we will explain in its chapter, God willing. And if he sewed a pair of trousers while he had ordered a qabā', it is said he takes compensation without choice due to disparity in benefit; the more correct is that he has a choice due to unity in the basis of benefit, and it is like the case where one orders a basin of brass to be beaten and he makes a pitcher; the owner has a choice. So here. Commentary on 'And whoever gives...': Someone gave cloth to a tailor to sew a shirt for him for a dirham. Then he sewed a qabā'. The cloth owner has the option: either take compensation for the cloth value (in which case the tailor becomes owner of the qabā'), or take the qabā' and give its fair wage, which will not exceed a dirham. Statement: 'It is said its meaning...' : Qabā' can be single-fold or double-fold. Some mashā'ikh said qabā' here means a shirt with one fold because it is used like a qabā'. And some said it is applied generally because qabā' and shirt are close in benefit (covering private parts, preventing loss). And each has sleeves and a skirt. Statement: 'And from Abu Hanifa...' : From Imam Abu Hanifa there is a narration that the owner has no option other than compensation because qabā' is contrary to the genus of shirt, so the tailor becomes a usurper. This is the narration of Hasan, and it is also the qiyās of the three Imams. Benefit: The qabā' has only two folds and sometimes has a slit in the middle; it is apparently contrary to the shirt, as in the Nawādir narration. But in the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, qabā' is not contrary to the genus of shirt; otherwise there would be no option other than compensation. Therefore some mashā'ikh took qabā' to mean a shirt, because if it is split at the front it becomes a qabā'; also in terms of benefit they are of the same genus because both have open sleeves and a skirt. Statement: 'And the aspect of the apparent...' : The reason for the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah is that qabā' in one aspect is contrary to the shirt, and in another aspect it is a shirt.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage from the Sharh of al-Hidayah discusses the case where a tailor is given cloth to sew a qamīṣ (shirt) for a fixed wage of one dirham, but instead sews a qabā' (a type of cloak). The Hanafi ruling from the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah gives the owner a choice: he may either demand the value of the cloth as compensation (making the tailor a guarantor) or accept the qabā' and pay its fair wage (ujrat al-mithl), capped at the agreed one dirham. This choice exists because the qabā' and qamīṣ share sufficient similarity in benefit (both cover the body, have sleeves, etc.) despite some differences. However, a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa (through Hasan ibn Ziyād) holds that the owner has no choice; he can only take compensation because the qabā' is of a different genre (jins) from the qamīṣ, making the tailor a usurper. The text clarifies that the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah's position is the relied-upon one, as it considers the qabā' to be a shirt in one respect (since it can be tied at the waist and used similarly). The same logic applies if the tailor sews a sarāwīl (trousers) instead of a qabā'; the more correct view gives the owner a choice due to unity in the basic benefit. An analogy is drawn with the case of ordering a brass basin (ṭast) but receiving a pitcher (kūz), where the owner also has a choice. This passage highlights the Hanafi method of balancing conformity and difference in benefits to determine liability in service contracts.

Key Terms
قباء (qabā'): A type of cloak or outer garment, often with two folds, tied at the waist.
قمیص (qamīṣ): A shirt; the garment originally ordered.
اجر مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair or standard wage for a similar service in the market.
تاوان (tāwān): Compensation or indemnity for the value of the cloth; damages.
ظاہر الروایہ (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The apparent or well-known narration; the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, as opposed to rare narrations (nawādir).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah in the Hanafi school, if a tailor sews a qabā' instead of the requested qamīṣ, what options does the cloth owner have?
A) He must take the qabā' and pay the agreed dirham.
B) He must demand compensation for the cloth value only.
C) He may either take the qabā' with ujrat al-mithl (capped at one dirham) or demand compensation for the cloth.
D) He may take the qabā' without any payment.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, the owner of cloth has a choice when the tailor makes a different but similar garment—either accept the altered garment with fair wage (capped at the named wage) or demand compensation for the cloth.

intermediate

Tailor Makes Qaba Instead of Qamis: Owner's Choice (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Ruling on tailor making different garment than ordered

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the owner's choice when a tailor substitutes a garment, explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and apply the ruling to similar cases.

Core Idea
When a tailor makes a different but similarly beneficial garment, the owner may choose compensation or acceptance with fair wage.

In hire contracts (ijara), the artisan must deliver exactly what was ordered. But what if the tailor sews a qaba (cloak) instead of a qamis (shirt)? The Hanafi school gives the owner a choice, though a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa himself restricts that choice. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Issue
Identify the fact pattern: a tailor is given cloth to sew a qamis for a named wage, but instead sews a qaba. What are the owner's legal options?
2
Identify the Two Hanafi Positions
The zahir al-riwaya (apparent ruling) gives the owner a choice between taking compensation for the cloth or accepting the qaba and paying a fair wage (ujrat al-mithl) not exceeding the named wage. A narration from Abu Hanifa (via Hasan ibn Ziyad) holds that the owner only gets compensation, because qaba is a different genus from qamis, making the tailor a usurper.
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree with the zahir al-riwaya.
3
Analyze the Opposing Proof
The opposing view argues that qaba and qamis are different in form (e.g., qaba may have a slit or be double-layered). Thus the tailor deviated entirely, analogous to a usurper (ghasib), so only compensation is due.
4
Understand the Majority Response
The majority (zahir al-riwaya) notes that both garments serve the same primary benefit (covering the body), and the qaba can be tied to function like a qamis. Since there is both similarity (in benefit) and difference (in cut), the owner may choose based on which aspect he prefers.
This reasoning justifies the option of paying a fair wage rather than forcing compensation.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: Under the majority view, the owner can keep the altered garment and pay a capped fair wage; under the minority narration, he must insist on compensation and cannot keep it. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is the majority view.
The fair wage cannot exceed the named wage, following general rules for fasid contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

قوله و وجه الظاهر الخ - ظاہر الروایہ کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ قباء ایک لحاظ سے قمیص کے خلاف ہے اور ایک اعتبار سے قمیص ہے بایں معنی کہ اس کے درمیان کو باندھ کر قمیص کی طرح نفع اٹھاتے ہیں تو قباء بنادینے میں موافقت و مخالفت دونوں پائی گئیں ۔ پس ما لک کو اختیار ہے کہ اگر وہ مخالفت سمجھے تو قیمت کا تاوان لے لے اور موافقت سمجھے تو قباء لے کر اجر مثل دے دے کیونکہ موافقت میں قدرے قصور ہے۔
Glossary: trousers, etc. Translation: Someone gave cloth to a tailor to sew a shirt for one dirham, and he sewed a qaba instead. The owner has the choice: either take the compensation of the cloth's value, or take the qaba and give its fair wage, which will not exceed one dirham. It has been said that it remains on its general application because qaba and shirt are close in benefit. And there is a narration from Abu Hanifa that the owner will take compensation without choice because qaba is contrary to the genus of shirt, because its middle is tied and benefit is taken like a shirt. So there is both agreement and opposition; he may incline toward either direction. But the fair wage is obligatory due to the fault in the aspect of agreement, and it will not exceed the named one dirham, just as in other invalid leases. Commentary on the statement: He gave, etc. Someone gave cloth to a tailor to sew a shirt for one dirham... The tailor sewed a qaba, so the owner has the choice: either take compensation (in which case the tailor becomes owner of the qaba) or take the qaba and give its fair wage, but the fair wage will not exceed one dirham. On the meaning of qaba: It can be single-layered or double. Some scholars say it means a shirt-like garment; others say it applies generally due to close benefit. On the narration from Abu Hanifa: He said the owner has no choice except compensation because qaba is contrary to the genus of shirt, making the tailor a usurper. This is the narration of Hasan and the qiyas of the three Imams. Benefit: Qaba has only two folds and sometimes has a slit, outwardly contrary to shirt as in Nawadir narrations, but in Zahir al-Riwaya it is not contrary; otherwise there would be no choice. So some scholars interpret qaba as a kurta; if slit in front it becomes a qaba. Both have open sleeves and hem. On the reason for the apparent view: Qaba is contrary in one respect and similar in another; the middle can be tied to use like a shirt, so both agreement and opposition exist. The owner may choose: if he considers the opposition, take compensation; if agreement, take the qaba and give fair wage due to slight fault.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a tailor who makes a qaba (cloak) when ordered to make a qamis (shirt). The author first states the ruling: the owner has the choice to either take the value of the cloth as compensation (making the tailor owner of the qaba) or accept the qaba and pay a fair wage (ujrat al-mithl) that cannot exceed the named wage of one dirham. The commentary then explores the meaning of qaba and the reasoning behind the ruling. Some scholars say qaba here refers to a long shirt, not a double-layered cloak, because it is similar in use. Others say the term is general because both garments serve the same benefit (covering the body). The dispute between the apparent ruling (zahir al-riwaya) and a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa (via Hasan ibn Ziyad) is highlighted: Abu Hanifa's narration gives the owner only the option of compensation, since qaba is a different genus from shirt, making the tailor a usurper. The commentator explains that the apparent ruling considers both similarity and difference: the qaba can be tied to function like a shirt, so the owner may choose based on benefit. The fair wage is obligatory but cannot exceed the named wage, as in other invalid hire contracts. This ruling is a precedent for similar cases.

Key Terms
قبا (qaba): A cloak or outer garment, possibly with two folds, worn similar to a shirt but may have a slit.
اجر مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market wage for the service, which cannot exceed the named wage in an invalid contract.
خیار (khiyar): Option or choice granted to a party in a contract; here the owner's right to choose between compensation and acceptance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The owner must take compensation only.
B) The owner must accept the qaba and pay fair wage.
C) The owner has a choice between compensation or paying fair wage and keeping the qaba.
D) The contract is void and no payment is due.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position gives the owner a choice between compensation and acceptance of the altered garment with fair wage, due to similarity of benefit.

Tailor makes trousers instead of qaba: similar ruling
Extension of ruling to another case of different garment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred Hanafi ruling when a tailor substitutes a different garment and explain the qiyas used to derive it.

Core Idea
The owner's choice remains even with different garment types because the essential benefit of clothing is shared.

In this passage, the author extends the earlier ruling on a tailor sewing a qaba to the case of trousers. Some scholars saw a greater difference, but the preferred view retains the owner's choice. We will examine the argument and the analogy to the coppersmith case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and differing opinions
State the facts: tailor ordered to sew a qaba but makes trousers. Two views: some say only compensation; the asahh says owner has a choice.
2
Examine the proof for the asahh view
The dalil is qiyas to the coppersmith case where ordering a basin (tust) but receiving a pitcher (kuzah) gives the owner a choice.
3
Identify the 'illa in the analogy
The effective cause is the shared essential benefit: both qaba and trousers are garments for covering the body.
4
Understand the opposition's reasoning
Some scholars argue that the difference in benefit is too great, so the owner should only get compensation.
5
Recognize the tarjih and its basis
The commentator declares the choice view as asahh, relying on the qiyas and the principle that essential benefit outweighs superficial differences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله ولو خاطه سراويل ..... الخ - اگر درزی نے اس کپڑے کا پائجامہ ہی دیا۔ حالانکہ مالک نے اسے قباء سینے کے لئے کہا تھا تو بقول بعض مالک اس سے صرف تاوان لے سکتا ہے۔ کپڑا لے کر مزدوری دینے کا اختیار نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ قباء اور پائجامہ کی منفعت میں تفاوت ہے۔ لیکن اصح یہ ہے کہ مالک کو دونوں اختیار میں چاہے منتخب لے چاہے کپڑا لے کر اجر مثل دے۔ اس لئے کہ اصل منفعت یعنی لباس ہونے اور ستر پوشی میں دونوں یکساں ہیں۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے کھیرے کو تانبے کا طشت بنانے کے لئے کہا اور اس نے کوزہ بنا دیا تو مالک کو دونوں اختیار ہوتے ہیں ایسے ہی اس مسئلہ میں ہوں گے۔
And if he sewed trousers... If the tailor sewed trousers for the cloth, while the owner had ordered him to sew a qaba, then according to some, the owner can only take compensation, because the benefit of qaba and trousers differs. But the more correct view is that the owner has both choices: either select the garment or take the cloth and give fair wage, because the essential benefit, i.e., being clothing and covering private parts, is the same in both. So this is like when someone orders a copper basin (tust) and the artisan makes a pitcher (kuzah); the owner has both choices. Similarly here.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling to a case where the tailor makes trousers (sirwal) instead of a qaba. Some scholars argue that the difference in benefit is greater, so the owner should only be entitled to compensation (the value of the cloth) without the option to accept the trousers. However, the preferred (asahh) view in the Hanafi school is that the owner still has the choice, because the essential shared benefit (being a garment for covering the body) unites them. The author provides a qiyas (analogy) to the case of a coppersmith: if someone orders a basin (tust) but receives a pitcher (kuzah), the owner can choose between compensation or acceptance with fair wage. Thus, even when the garment type differs significantly, as long as the core function (clothing) is the same, the owner retains the option. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle of considering the underlying purpose (maslahah) over mere form.

Key Terms
سراويل (sirwal): Trousers or pants; a lower garment.
اصح (asahh): The more correct or preferred view in the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred (asahh) ruling when a tailor makes trousers instead of the ordered qaba?
A) The owner must take compensation only.
B) The owner must accept the trousers and pay fair wage.
C) The owner has a choice between compensation or accepting the trousers with fair wage.
D) The contract is null and no payment is due.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, even when the garment type differs, the owner may choose between accepting the substitute with fair wage or taking compensation, provided the essential benefit of clothing is shared.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

8 min
Fair Wage in Invalid Hire: Hanafi Cap vs. Zufar/Shafi'i
General rule for invalid hire contracts with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fair wage in invalid hire contracts and explain the difference with Zufar and al-Shafi'i, including the rational proof for the cap.

Core Idea
In invalid hire, fair wage is capped at the named sum because benefits have no intrinsic value.

This lesson addresses a key dispute in the fiqh of hire (ijara) concerning compensation when the contract is invalid. While all schools agree that a fair wage is obligatory, the Hanafi school uniquely limits that wage to the amount named in the invalid contract. This ruling is based on the nature of benefits (manafi') and a careful distinction from the sale of tangible goods.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Determine the precise question: In an invalid hire contract (ijara fasida), what wage is due: the named wage or the market wage? And is there a cap?
The issue is about the upper limit of the fair wage.
2
State the two positions
Hanafi: Fair wage (ujrat al-mithl) is due but cannot exceed the named sum. Zufar and Shafi'i: Fair wage is due without any cap, by analogy to sale of commodities.
The practical difference arises when fair wage is higher than the named sum.
3
Analyze the proofs
Hanafi proof: Benefits (manafi') are not valuable in themselves; only the contract gives them value. Therefore, the invalid contract follows the valid one, which uses the named wage as a cap. Opposite proof: Analogy to sale where the commodity has intrinsic value, so market price is due regardless of named price.
The core reasoning is about the nature of benefits vs. tangible goods.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Consider a scenario: named wage $100, fair wage $150. Hanafi: worker gets $100 (capped). Shafi'i: worker gets $150 (uncapped). This shows the practical consequence of the dispute.
The cap protects the employer from unexpected high wages in invalid contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الاجارة الفاسدة
ترجمہ باب اجارہ فاسدہ کے بیان میں جن شروط سے اجارہ فاسد ہو جاتا ہے
قال الاجارة تفسدها الشروط كما تفسد البيع لانه بمنزلته الا ترى انه عقد يقال ويفسخ والواجب في الاجارة الفاسدة اجرة المثل لا يجاوز به المسمى وقال زفر والشافعى يجب بالغا ما بلغ اعتبارا ببيع الاعيان ولنا ان المنافع لا تتقوم بنفسها بل بالعقد لحاجة الناس فيكتفي بالضرورة فى الصحيح منها الا ان الفاسد تبع له فيعتبر ما يجعل بدلا في الصحيح عادة لكنهما اذا اتفقا على مقدار فى الفاسد فقد اسقطا الزيادة واذا نقص اجر المثل لم يجب زيادة المسمى لفساد التسمية بخلاف البيع لان العين متقوم في نفسه وهو الموجب الاصلى فان صحت التسمية انتقل عنه والافلا.
ترجمہ اجارہ کو شریں فاسد کر دیتی ہیں۔ جیسے بیع کو فاسد کر دیتی ہیں۔ کیونکہ اجارہ بمنزلہ بیع کے ہے کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ وہ بھی اقالہ اور فتح کیا جاتا ہے اور اجارہ فاسدہ میں اجر مثل واجب ہوتا ہے جو بیان کردہ مقدار سے نہیں بڑھتا۔ امام زفر ، امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ واجب ہوتا ہے۔ جہاں تک پہنچے بیچ اعیان پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ منافع بذات خود قیمتی نہیں ہوتے بلکہ بذریعہ عقد ہوتے ہیں۔ لوگوں کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے پس عقد صحیح میں ضرورت پر اکتفاء کیا جائے گا۔ اور فاسد چونکہ صحیح کے تابع ہے تو اجارہ صحیحہ میں جو چیز عادة بدل قرار دی جاتی ہے وہی فاسدہ میں معتبر ہوگی ۔ لیکن جب متعاقدین متفق ہو گئے۔ کسی مقدار پر اجارہ فاسدہ میں تو انہوں نے زیادہ کو ساقط کر دیا اور جب اجر مثل کم ہے تو بیان کردہ اجرت جو زائد ہے واجب نہ ہوگی قرارداد کے فساد کی وجہ سے بخلاف بیع کے کیونکہ عین بذات خود قیمتی ہے اور وہی اصل موجب ہے۔ پس اگر تسمیہ صحیح ہو تو شمن کی جانب منتقل ہوگا ورنہ نہیں ۔
Chapter of Invalid Hire. Translation: Conditions invalidate hire as they invalidate sale, because hire is like sale; do you not see that it can be cancelled (iqalah) and rescinded (faskh)? The obligatory in invalid hire is fair wage (ujrat al-mithl) that does not exceed the named sum. Zufar and Shafi'i said: It is obligatory whatever it reaches, by analogy to sale of commodities. Our proof: Benefits (manafi') are not valuable in themselves but by contract, due to people's need; in a valid contract we suffice with necessity, and the invalid follows it, so what is usually made the consideration in valid hire is considered. But when the parties agree on a sum in invalid hire, they have waived any excess; if the fair wage is less, the named sum is not due because the stipulation is void. Unlike sale because the commodity is valuable in itself and is the primary subject; if the naming is valid, [the price] transfers, otherwise not.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on invalid hire (ijara fasida). It lays down the general principle: invalid hire contracts are similar to invalid sales in that certain conditions render them void. The key ruling is that in an invalid hire, the worker is entitled to a fair wage (ujrat al-mithl), but this fair wage cannot exceed the wage mentioned in the invalid contract. This is contested by Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i, who argue by analogy to the sale of tangible goods (a'yan): in an invalid sale, the seller gets the full market price regardless of the agreed price. However, the Hanafi position is based on the nature of benefits (manafi'): benefits are not intrinsically valuable; they only become valuable through a valid contract due to public need. Therefore, in a valid contract, we suffice with the set wage, and in an invalid contract, we follow the valid contract's template but cap it at the named sum because the parties have implicitly agreed not to exceed that amount. If the fair wage is lower than the named wage, the named wage is not due because the agreement specifying it is void. This differs from the sale of commodities because commodities have intrinsic value, so the primary obligation is on the commodity itself, and the named price is considered if validly specified. This illustrates the Hanafi madhhab's distinctive theory of value in contracts.

Key Terms
اجرة المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market wage for similar work, due in invalid hire but capped at the named wage.
تسمية (tasmiyah): The naming of a price or wage in the contract; if void, the named sum is not binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the fair wage (ujrat al-mithl) in an invalid hire contract (ijara fasida) if the named wage is higher than the fair wage?
A) The named wage is due because the parties agreed to it.
B) The fair wage is due and it can exceed the named wage.
C) The fair wage is due but it cannot exceed the named wage.
D) No wage is due because the contract is void.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the fair wage in an invalid hire contract is capped at the named wage because benefits lack intrinsic value, distinguishing hire from sale.

Owner's Options When Tailor Makes Wrong Garment
Defines owner's option when tailor sews wrong garment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the owner's options when a tailor makes a garment different from what was ordered, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and identify the preferred (aṣaḥḥ) view with its proof.

Core Idea
When a tailor makes a wrong garment, the owner may accept it with equivalent wage or claim compensation, because the essential benefit is the same.

This lesson examines a specific case from Ijarah: a tailor sews a sarawil instead of the ordered qaba. Within the Hanafi school, there is a difference of opinion on whether the owner can only claim compensation or has the option to accept the garment. We will analyze the two views and the preferred position based on istihsān and analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The tailor made a sarawil instead of a qaba. The dispute is whether the owner can only take compensation or has both options: compensation or accepting the garment and paying the equivalent wage.
The dispute is intra-Hanafi; the text labels the preferred view as 'aṣaḥḥ'.
2
State the first view and its basis
Some Hanafis say the owner can only take compensation because the benefit of a qaba and sarawil differ (different forms).
This view focuses on the specific intended benefit.
3
State the preferred view and its proof
The aṣaḥḥ view gives both options: take the garment and pay ujrat al-mithl, or take compensation. The proof: the essential benefit (being clothing and covering) is the same. This is analogous to the case of a copper basin made into a pot.
Analogy (qiyas) to the copper basin case shows that when the core utility is unchanged, the owner has options.
4
Conclude the mufta bihi
The preferred view is operative; the owner has both options.
This is based on the text's declaration of 'aṣaḥḥ' and the absence of a contrary fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Meaning that if he ties its middle and benefits from it like a shirt, then in making a qaba both conformity and nonconformity are found. So the owner has the option: if he considers it nonconformity, he takes the price as compensation; if he considers it conformity, he takes the qaba and gives the equivalent wage because in conformity there is some shortcoming. His statement: 'And if he sews it as a sarawil...' - If the tailor made it into a sarawil, even though the owner told him to sew a qaba, then according to some, the owner can only take compensation, not take the cloth and give wages, because the benefit of a qaba and sarawil differ. But the correct view is that the owner has both options: either take the value, or take the cloth and give the equivalent wage, because the original benefit (being clothing and covering) is the same. This is like the case where someone says 'make a copper basin' and he makes a pot: the owner has both options. So it is in this case.

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a tailor makes a garment different from what the customer ordered. Two views exist within the Hanafi school: some say the owner can only claim compensation (the value of the cloth) because the new garment does not match the intended benefit. However, the preferred (aṣaḥḥ) position is that the owner has the choice to either accept the garment and pay the equivalent wage for it, or take compensation. This is based on istihsān (juristic preference), analogizing to the case of a copper basin being made into a pot—since both serve the same essential purpose (covering), the owner has both options. The passage emphasizes that the core benefit (clothing and covering) is identical between a qaba and sarawil.

Key Terms
قباء (qabā): A type of cloak or outer garment worn by people.
اجر مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The customary equivalent wage for similar work or benefit.

Checkpoint

B) He can take the sarawil and pay the equivalent wage, or take compensation.
C) He must accept the sarawil and pay the named wage.
D) He can force the tailor to remake the garment correctly.

Key Takeaway
The owner may accept the wrong garment and pay the equivalent wage, or claim compensation, because the core benefit of clothing is identical.

Ruling on Corrupt Ijarah: Ujrat al-Mithl Capped at Named Amount
States Hanafi ruling on corrupt ijarah and responds to Zufar and Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ujrat al-mithl in corrupt ijarah, explain the difference from the Zufar/Shafi'i position, and apply the cap rule to a given scenario.

Core Idea
In corrupt ijarah, ujrat al-mithl is wajib but capped at the named rent — benefits have no intrinsic value.

Rental contracts can be corrupted by invalid conditions or ignorance of key terms. When that happens, how much rent is due? The Hanafi school sets a clear rule: the market rate (ujrat al-mithl) is obligatory, but it cannot exceed the rent the parties agreed on. This lesson unpacks that ruling and the reasoning that distinguishes ijarah from sale, responding to the views of Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: in corrupt ijarah, ujrat al-mithl is wajib but not exceeding the musamma (named amount).
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing view
Zufar (within Hanafi) and al-Shafi'i hold that ujrat al-mithl is due without any upper limit, whatever the market rate.
They base this on an analogy to corrupt sale (bay' fasid).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the qiyas: in corrupt sale, the commodity has intrinsic value, so market price is always due. They analogize ijarah to sale.
The opposing dalil is qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school distinguishes: benefits (manafi') are not valuable in themselves but become valuable through contract; parties waived excess by agreeing on a named amount.
This is a qiyas khafi (subtle distinction) that breaks the analogy.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under Hanafi law, the landlord cannot claim more than the named rent even if market rates rise; under the opposing view, the landlord can claim the full market rate.
This difference affects real-world rental disputes.

Source Text

قال الاجارة تفسدها الشروط كما تفسد البيع لانه بمنزلته الا ترى انه عقد يقال ويفسخ والواجب في الاجارة الفاسدة اجرة المثل لا يجاوز به المسمى وقال زفر والشافعى يجب بالغا ما بلغ اعتبارا ببيع الاعيان ولنا ان المنافع لا تتقوم بنفسها بل بالعقد لحاجة الناس فيكتفي بالضرورة فى الصحيح منها الا ان الفاسد تبع له فيعتبر ما يجعل بدلا في الصحيح عادة لكنهما اذا اتفقا على مقدار فى الفاسد فقد اسقطا الزيادة واذا نقص اجر المثل لم يجب زيادة المسمى لفساد التسمية بخلاف البيع لان العين متقوم في نفسه وهو الموجب الاصلى فان صحت التسمية انتقل عنه والافلا.

امام زفر و امام شافعی نے جوا جارو کوچ پر قیاس کیا ہے اس کا جواب ہے کہ یہ میچ نہیں۔ کیونکہ بیچ و اجارہ میں فرق ہے اور وہ یہ کہ بیچ میں مال عین بیچ ہوتا ہے۔ اور مال عین بذات خود قیمتی چیز ہے۔ پس اصل مقتضائے بیچ یہ ہے کہ یہی قیمت واجب ہو۔ لیکن اگر متعاقدین نے قیمت کے علاوہ کسی مقدار یمن پر اتفاق کر لیا تو قیمت سے منتقل ہو کر ثمن واجب ہوگا۔ بشرطیکہ عقد صحیح ہو ۔ اگر فاسد ہو تو وہی اصلی قیمت واجب رہے گی۔ بخلاف اجارہ کے کہ اس میں منافع فروخت ہوتے ہیں جو بذات خود قیمتی نہیں بلکہ لوگوں کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے شرع نے ان کو قیمتی کر دیا۔ پس اگر متعاقدین نے کوئی صحیح قرارداد ہو تو وہی واجب ہوگی اور اگر قرار داد صحیح نہ ہو تو ان کی ٹھہرائی ہوئی مقدار معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ بلکہ جو قیمت ہوتی ہو وہ لازم ہوگی۔ پھر جس مقدار پر انہوں نے اتفاق کیا ہے اس پر رضامندی موجود ہے۔ پس اگر عقد صحیح ہوتا تو اس قدر ماتا اور فاسد اجارہ چونکہ صحیح پر قیاس ہے تو اس میں بھی ان کی رضا مندی سے زیادہ نہیں ملے گا۔ بہر کیف اگر اجر مثل کم ہو تو یہی ملے گا ور نہ قرارداد سے زیادہ نہیں ملے گا۔
Chapter of Corrupt Ijarah. Translation: Regarding the chapter on corrupt ijarah. Conditions that corrupt ijarah. He said: Ijarah is corrupted by conditions just as sale is corrupted, because it is like sale. Do you not see that it is a contract that can be terminated and rescinded? And in corrupt ijarah, the obligatory is ujrat al-mithl (equivalent wage) that does not exceed the named amount. Zufar and Shafi'i said: It is obligatory whatever it reaches, in consideration of the sale of goods. Our proof: Benefits are not valuable in themselves but become valuable by contract due to people's need. So in a valid contract, necessity suffices, and the corrupt [contract] is dependent on it; thus what is usually made a substitute in a valid contract is considered. But when both parties agree on an amount in the corrupt [contract], they have waived the excess. And if ujrat al-mithl is less, the named increase is not obligatory due to the corruption of the naming. Unlike sale, because the commodity is valuable in itself and is the original obligator. If the naming is valid, it shifts from it; otherwise not. Commentary on his statement: 'Ijarah is corrupted by conditions...' - Since ijarah is like sale, the conditions that corrupt sale also corrupt ijarah, such as stipulating that if the house collapses the rent is not waived, or if the mill's water stops the rent is still due. Similarly, ignorance of the wage, period, or work corrupts ijarah. And ujrat al-mithl is obligatory but not exceeding the named amount. According to Zufar and Shafi'i, ujrat al-mithl is given even if more than named; they analogize to corrupt sale where the price is obligatory however high. We say benefits are not valuable in themselves but become valuable through contract, and the parties waived excess by agreeing on a named amount, so the excess is disregarded. His statement: 'Unlike sale...' - The response to their analogy: Sale and ijarah differ. In sale, the commodity is valuable in itself, so the original requirement is that the price is obligatory. If the parties agree on another amount, it transfers to that if valid; if the contract is corrupt, the original price remains. In ijarah, benefits are sold; they are not valuable in themselves but made valuable by Shari'ah due to need. If the parties make a valid agreement, that amount is obligatory; if the agreement is corrupt, the agreed amount is not considered, rather the actual value is obligatory. But since they consented to that amount, it is not exceeded if ujrat al-mithl is less. In short, if ujrat al-mithl is less, that is given; if it is more, the named amount is not exceeded.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on corrupt ijarah (ijarah fasidah). The core ruling is that in a corrupt rental contract, the tenant must pay the ujrat al-mithl (equivalent market wage), but this amount is capped at the rent named in the contract (musamma). If the ujrat al-mithl is less than the named amount, only the ujrat al-mithl is paid; if it is more, the named amount is paid. This differs from the positions of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i, who hold that the ujrat al-mithl is due without any upper limit, analogizing to corrupt sale (bay' fasid) where the market price of the commodity is always paid. The Hanafi proof relies on the nature of benefits (manafi'): benefits are not intrinsically valuable but derive value through the contract due to societal need. In a valid ijarah, the agreed wage is the substitute; the corrupt contract follows the valid one in principle. Since the parties voluntarily agreed on a specific amount, they implicitly waived any excess. Therefore, even if the ujrat al-mithl is higher, the landlord cannot claim more than the named rent. The commentary further explains the distinction from sale: in sale, the commodity ('ayn) is an entity with inherent value, so if the named price is invalid, the market value becomes binding. In ijarah, benefits lack inherent value, so the agreement governs within the bounds of the named amount.

Key Terms
اجارة فاسدة (ijarah fasidah): A rental contract defective due to invalid conditions (e.g., ignorance of wage/period) or prohibited stipulations.
اجرة المثل (ujrat al-mithl): The customary equivalent wage for similar services or properties in the market.
مسمى (musamma): The amount of rent expressly named and agreed upon in the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a corrupt ijarah (ijarah fasidah), what is the Hanafi ruling regarding ujrat al-mithl?
A) Ujrat al-mithl is not obligatory; only the named rent is paid.
B) Ujrat al-mithl is obligatory and can be more than the named rent.
C) Ujrat al-mithl is obligatory but does not exceed the named rent.
D) Ujrat al-mithl is calculated as the average of market and named rent.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the ujrat al-mithl in corrupt ijarah is capped at the named rent because benefits derive value from contract, not intrinsically.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Ujrat al-Mithl in Fasid Ijarah: The Cap on Fair Rent
Ruling on compensation in fasid lease and refutation of analogy to fasid sale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation in a fasid ijarah, distinguish it from the ruling in a fasid sale, and evaluate the opposing analogy.

Core Idea
In a fasid lease, fair rent is owed but never exceeds the agreed amount—because usufructs have no intrinsic value.

When a lease contract is fasid (defective), the lessee must compensate the lessor for usage. The Hanafi school uniquely caps this compensation at the agreed rent, even if fair rent is higher. This ruling rests on a key distinction between usufructs and physical assets, and it directly challenges the analogy to fasid sale.

Guided Path
1
Identify causes of fasid ijarah
From the passage, list the conditions that render an ijarah contract fasid: invalid stipulations (e.g., rent due even if property collapses), uncertainty (jahalah) in the leased object, rent, duration, or work.
These conditions invalidate the contract in description while the essence remains.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The passage states: ujrat al-mithl (fair rent) is wajib but not given more than the agreed amount (musamma). Note the hukm level and the cap.
The cap is the distinctive element.
3
Present the opposing analogy
Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i analogize to fasid sale: in a fasid sale, the full market price of the object is due. They apply this to ijarah, arguing ujrat al-mithl is due without cap.
This is a qiyas: fasid sale → fasid ijarah.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi rebuttal distinguishes sale from lease: in sale, the object (al-ayn) is intrinsically valuable; in lease, usufructs (manafi') are not. Usufructs gain value through contract and consent. Therefore, the agreed amount limits liability.
Key: the nature of the subject matter differs.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: if fair rent > agreed rent, Hanafi: lessee pays agreed rent; opposing: lessee pays fair rent. If fair rent ≤ agreed rent, both pay fair rent.
The cap only matters when fair rent is higher.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اجارہ بھی فاسد ہو جائے گا۔ جیسے شرط لگانا کہ اگر مکان منہدم بھی ہو جائے تب بھی کرانیہ ساقط نہ ہوگا۔ یا پن چکی کا پانی بند ہو جائے تب بھی اجرت لازم ہو گی۔ اسی طرح شی اجور یا اجرت یا مدت یا عمل کا مجہول ہونا وغیرہ ان سب چیزوں سے اجارہ فاسد ہو جائے گا۔ اور اجرت مثل واجب ہوگی۔ لیکن مسٹمی سے زیادہ نہیں دی جائے گی۔
امام زفر اور امام شافعی کے یہاں اجرت مثل دی جائے گی گوشی سے زیادہ ہو۔ یہ حضرات اس کو بیع فاسد پر قیاس کرتے ہیں کہ اس میں مبیع کی قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے۔ خواہ کتنی ہو۔ ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ منافع فی نفسہ متقوم نہیں بلکہ عقد کی وجہ سے متقوم ہوتے ہیں۔ اور عقد میں خود متعاقدین نے اجر ستمی پر اتفاق کر کے زیادتی کو ساقط کر دیا۔ اس لئے زائد مقدار ساقط الاعتبار ہوگی۔
قوله بخلاف البيع الخ - امام زفر و امام شافعی نے جوا جارو کوچ پر قیاس کیا ہے اس کا جواب ہے کہ یہ میچ نہیں۔ کیونکہ بیچ و اجارہ میں فرق ہے اور وہ یہ کہ بیچ میں مال عین بیچ ہوتا ہے۔ اور مال عین بذات خود قیمتی چیز ہے۔ پس اصل مقتضائے بیچ یہ ہے کہ یہی قیمت واجب ہو۔ لیکن اگر متعاقدین نے قیمت کے علاوہ کسی مقدار یمن پر اتفاق کر لیا تو قیمت سے منتقل ہو کر ثمن واجب ہوگا۔ بشرطیکہ عقد صحیح ہو ۔ اگر فاسد ہو تو وہی اصلی قیمت واجب رہے گی۔ بخلاف اجارہ کے کہ اس میں منافع فروخت ہوتے ہیں جو بذات خود قیمتی نہیں بلکہ لوگوں کی ضرورت کی وجہ سے شرع نے ان کو قیمتی کر دیا۔ پس اگر متعاقدین نے کوئی صحیح قرارداد کی ہو تو وہی واجب ہوگی اور اگر قرار داد صحیح نہ ہو تو ان کی ٹھہرائی ہوئی مقدار معتبر نہ ہوگی۔ بلکہ جو قیمت ہوتی ہو وہ لازم ہوگی۔ پھر جس مقدار پر انہوں نے اتفاق کیا ہے اس پر رضامندی موجود ہے۔ پس اگر عقد صحیح ہوتا تو اس قدر ماتا اور فاسد اجارہ چونکہ صحیح پر قیاس ہے تو اس میں بھی ان کی رضا مندی سے زیادہ نہیں ملے گا۔ بہر کیف اگر اجر مثل کم ہو تو یہی ملے گا ور نہ قرارداد سے زیادہ نہیں ملے گا۔
The lease will also become invalid. Like stipulating that even if the house collapses, the rent will not be dropped. Or if the water of the watermill stops, the rent will still be obligatory. Similarly, the unknown nature of the leased object, rent, duration, or work etc., all these things will make the lease invalid. And the fair rent will be obligatory, but it will not be given more than the agreed amount.
According to Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i, fair rent will be given even if it is more than [the agreed amount]. These scholars analogize this to an invalid sale, where the price of the sold item is obligatory, no matter how much it is. We say that usufructs are not intrinsically valuable; rather, they become valuable due to the contract. And in the contract, the parties themselves agreed on the specified rent and eliminated the excess. Therefore, the excess amount is disregarded.
His statement 'contrary to sale, etc.' - The answer to the analogy of Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i is that it is not correct, because there is a difference between sale and lease. That is, in sale, a specific asset is sold, and a specific asset is inherently valuable. So the original requirement of sale is that this price is obligatory. But if the parties agreed on some other amount besides the price, then they transfer from the price and the agreed price becomes obligatory, provided the contract is valid. If it is invalid, then the original price remains obligatory. Unlike lease, where usufructs are sold, which are not intrinsically valuable; rather, due to people's need, the Law has made them valuable. So if the parties have made a valid agreement, that will be binding; if the agreement is not valid, then their agreed amount is not credible. Instead, whatever the [fair] price is, it will be binding. Then, they have consent on the amount they agreed upon. So if the contract were valid, this amount would be [binding]; and since an invalid lease is analogous to a valid one, they will not receive more than their consent. In any case, if the fair rent is less, this will be given; otherwise it will not exceed the agreement.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding compensation in a fasid (invalid) lease. It begins by listing conditions that render an ijarah fasid, such as stipulating that rent is due even if the house collapses or the watermill stops, or uncertainty (jahalah) in the leased object, rent, duration, or work. The ruling is that when the lease is fasid, the lessee must pay ujrat al-mithl (fair rent) but not exceeding the agreed amount (musamma).

Imam Zufar and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that ujrat al-mithl is payable without this cap, analogizing to a fasid sale (bay' fasid) where the full market price of the sold item is due. The Hanafi response distinguishes between the two contracts: in sale, the object (al-'ayn) is inherently valuable, so if the contract is fasid, the default market price applies. In ijarah, the subject matter is usufructs (manafi'), which are not intrinsically valuable; they derive value from the contract and people's needs. Since the parties voluntarily agreed on a specific amount, that agreement reflects their consent. A fasid lease is compared to a valid lease, and in a valid lease, the agreed rent is binding. Therefore, in a fasid lease, the fair rent is capped at the agreed amount because that is what the parties consented to. If the fair rent is lower, the lower amount is paid; if higher, it is not demanded.

The passage concludes by reaffirming the Hanafi position through a detailed logical reasoning: the essence of sale is the transfer of a valuable commodity, so its original ruling is the market price, while the essence of ijarah is the transfer of usufructs, which are not inherently valuable; thus the agreed price limits liability.

Key Terms
اجارہ فاسد (ijārah fāsid): A lease contract that is defective due to an invalid condition or uncertainty, but still requires compensation for usage.
اجرت مثل (ujrat al-mithl): The fair market rent for similar property or services in similar circumstances.
مال عین (māl ʿayn): A tangible, specific asset that has inherent value (as opposed to usufruct).
منافع (manāfiʿ): Usufructs or benefits derived from an asset, which are not intrinsically valuable but become valuable through contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a fasid ijarah, what is the Hanafi ruling regarding the amount of rent payable if the agreed rent is less than the fair market rent?
A) The lessee must pay the full fair market rent (ujrat al-mithl).
B) The lessee pays only the agreed rent, even if it is lower.
C) The lessee pays the average of the agreed rent and fair market rent.
D) The contract is void and no rent is payable.

Key Takeaway
In a fasid ijarah, the Hanafi school requires ujrat al-mithl but caps it at the agreed amount, rejecting the analogy to fasid sale because usufructs are not inherently valuable.

Leasing a House for a Year Without Specifying Monthly Rent
Ruling on fixed-term yearly lease without monthly breakdown of rent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a fixed-term lease with a total known rent even when monthly installments are unspecified and apply the condition of known duration and known rent to determine validity.

Core Idea
A lease is valid if total duration and total rent are known; unspecified monthly breakdown does not cause invalidity.

Contracts of lease (ijara) require certainty about the essential terms. This lesson examines a scenario where the duration and total rent are fixed, but the monthly allocation is left unstated. The Hanafi ruling provides a clear principle: as long as the overall framework is known, the contract stands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and its ruling
Recognize the act: leasing a house for a fixed term (one year) with a stated total rent (ten dirhams). The ruling is that the contract is valid (sahih).
The key is that both duration and total rent are specified.
2
Examine the condition that ensures validity
The condition is that the total duration and total rent are known. The lack of a monthly breakdown does not introduce fatal uncertainty (gharar).
Contrast with a case where the duration or total rent is unknown — then the contract would be fasid.
3
Understand the analogical reasoning
The ruling is analogous to a one-month lease where the daily rent is not specified. Since a month is known, the daily allocation is irrelevant. Similarly, a year is known, so the monthly allocation is irrelevant.
This reasoning is based on qiyas (analogy) within the same chapter of ijara.
4
Apply the principle to other fixed terms
The same rule applies to any lease where the term and total rent are fixed, e.g., six months, two years. The monthly or daily breakdown does not need to be stated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وان استاجر داراً سنة بعشرة دراهم جاز وان لم يبين قسط كل شهر من الاجرة لان المدة معلومة بدون التقسيم فصار كاجارة شهر واحد فانه جائز وان لم يبين قسط كل يوم
ترجمہ: اور اگر اس نے ایک مکان سال بھر کے لیے دس درہم میں کرایہ پر لیا تو یہ جائز ہے اگرچہ وہ ہر مہینے کے کرایہ کی قسط بیان نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ کل مدت تقسیم کے بغیر معلوم ہے، تو یہ ایک ماہ کے اجارہ کی طرح ہو گیا، کیونکہ وہ جائز ہے اگرچہ ہر روز کی قسط بیان نہ کی ہو۔
تشرح: اس طرح اگر سال بھر کے لئے مکان کرایہ پر لے اور سال بھر کا کرایہ ذکر کرے، نہر مہینہ کا کرایہ بیان نہ کرے تب بھی اجارہ صحیح ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ہر ماہ کی قسط بیان کئے بغیر بھی کل مدت معلوم ہو گئی تو یہ ایسا ہو گیا جیسے ایک ماہ کے لئے مکان کرایہ پر لیا اور ہر روز کا کرایہ بیان نہیں کیا کہ یہ جائز ہے۔
His statement: 'And if he rents a house for a year for ten dirhams, it is permissible even if he does not specify the installments of each month's rent, because the duration is known without division, so it becomes like a lease of one month, which is permissible even if he does not specify the installment of each day.'
Translation: And if he rents a house for a year for ten dirhams, it is permissible even if he does not state the monthly rent installment, because the total duration is known without division, so it becomes like a lease of one month, which is permissible even if he does not specify the daily installment.
Explanation: Similarly, if he rents a house for a year and mentions the total year's rent but does not mention the monthly rent, then too the lease is valid, because even without mentioning each month's installment, the total duration is known. So it becomes like renting a house for one month without specifying the daily rent, which is permissible.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This is a concise ruling stating that when a house is leased for a fixed term (e.g., one year) with a total rent mentioned (e.g., ten dirhams), the contract is valid even if the monthly or daily breakdown is not specified. The reason is that the total duration is known and definite. It is analogous to leasing a house for one month without specifying the daily rent — that is also valid. The key point is that uncertainty (jahalah) in the apportionment of rent over shorter periods within a fixed total duration does not invalidate the contract, as long as the overall duration and total rent are clear. This ruling applies to any fixed term where the total rent is known.

Key Terms
قسط (qiṣṭ): Installment; refers to the monthly portion of the rent in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Fasid (invalid) and requires ujrat al-mithl.
C) Sahih (valid) because the total duration is known.
D) Sahih only if the annual rent is divided equally.

Key Takeaway
A fixed-term lease with a known total rent is valid even without a monthly or daily breakdown of the rent.

Beginning of the Lease Term When Not Specified
Ruling on when the lease term begins if not explicitly stated

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the start of a lease term when no start date is mentioned and explain the reasoning using the analogy to oath and distinction from fasting.

Core Idea
If no lease start date is specified, the term begins immediately at contract because all times are equal for lease.

When parties enter into a lease (ijara), the term must be known. But what if they forget to specify a start date? This lesson clarifies the Hanafi default rule: the term begins at the moment the contract is made. The reasoning ties into the nature of lease – all times are interchangeable – and contrasts with acts like fasting, which have fixed temporal slots.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage covers two cases: when a start date is specified (ibtida' al-muddah mimma samma) and when it is not specified. Understand the rule for each.
2
Understand the default rule
When no start date is mentioned, the term begins from the time of contract (min al-waqt alladhi istajara). This is the default.
The phrase 'istajara' refers to the moment the lease is concluded.
3
Analyze the analogy to oath (yamin)
The text says 'fashbaha al-yamin' – it draws an analogy to an oath. An oath takes effect immediately upon utterance; similarly, a lease without a specified start takes effect immediately.
The 'illa (effective cause) is that all times are equally suitable for lease, just as all times are equally suitable for an oath to be binding.
4
Distinguish from fasting (sawm)
Fasting is different: nights are not a place for fasting, so an unspecified fast cannot begin at night. The start of a fast is tied to a specific time (dawn). Lease has no such restriction.
This distinction shows that the default rule is not universal – it depends on the nature of the act.
5
Apply to a concrete scenario
Take a real case: A leases a car to B on July 1st with no start date. According to the rule, the term begins immediately on July 1st. Check if the analogy to oath holds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يعتبر ابتداء المدة مما سمى وان لم يسم شيئا فهو من الوقت الذى استاجره لان الاوقات كلها في حق الاجارة على السواء فاشبه اليمين بخلاف الصوم لان الليالى ليست بمحل له ثم ان كان العقد حين يهل
Then, the beginning of the duration is considered from what [time] he mentioned. And if he did not mention anything, then it is from the time he leased it, because all times are equal with respect to lease, so it resembles an oath (yamin) as opposed to fasting, because nights are not a place for it. Then, if the contract [is made] when the new moon appears...
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage explains the commencement of the lease term. If the parties specify a start date, the term begins from that date. If no start date is mentioned, the term begins immediately from the time of the contract. The reasoning is that all times are equivalent for the purpose of lease — there is no specific preferred time like there is for fasting, which must begin at dawn. The analogy is drawn to an oath (yamin), which also takes effect from the moment it is sworn. The text ends abruptly, likely discussing the scenario where the contract is made at the beginning of the month (when the new moon appears). This fragment indicates that the start time is immediate unless a specific future date is agreed upon.

Key Terms
ابتداء المدة (ibtidā' al-muddah): The starting point of the lease term.
يمين (yamīn): An oath; here used as analogy for immediate effect from the time of utterance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) From the following Monday
B) From the next dawn (similar to fasting)
C) From the time of contract on Monday
D) The contract is invalid because the start date is uncertain

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a lease term begins immediately if no start date is stated, based on the principle that all times are equal for lease.

Ruling on Renting a House with Monthly Rent Without Specifying Total Duration
Explains ruling for monthly rent lease without total months specification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a monthly rent lease without total duration and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Uncertain total duration renders the lease for subsequent months fasid, not batil.

When someone rents a house for a monthly rent but does not specify how many months, is the contract valid? The Hanafi school distinguishes between the first month and subsequent months. This lesson walks through the reasoning behind this distinction, the internal Hanafi difference between qiyas and the relied-upon zahir al-riwayah, and how other madhahib rule on the same issue.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The lease is valid only for the first month; for remaining months it is fasid unless the total months are stated.
The first month is known because the word 'kull' when applied to indefinite items is restricted to a single unit.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i's stronger opinion holds the entire lease is batil; Imam Malik considers it ja'iz.
Imam Ahmad and Sheikh Istakhrī have a view similar to the Hanafi.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
The word 'kull' (كل) when applied to things without limit cannot be applied generally, so it is confined to a single instance. The first month is a known period, so the contract is valid for it.
For subsequent months, the period is unknown, so the contract is fasid.
4
Analyse the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf
According to qiyas, if the tenant stays even for a moment in the second month, the lease becomes valid for that entire month due to mutual consent. However, the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) holds that either party has the option to cancel at the start of the second month.
The reason for the option is that considering a moment as establishing consent is problematic (حرج).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Hanafi law, if the tenant stays for a moment in the second month, the lease becomes valid for that month (qiyas) or either party can cancel (zahir al-riwayah). Under Shafi'i, the entire lease is void.
The practical difference (thamarah) is crucial for eviction and rent payment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الاجارات
صرف ہوتا ہے عموم پر عمل کے متعد ر ہونے کی وجہ سے اور ایک مبینہ معلوم ہے تو اس میں عقد صیح ہو گیا۔ جب یہ مہینہ پورا ہو جائے تو ان میں سے ہر ایک کو اختیار ہوگا کہ اجارہ توڑ دے عقد صحیح کے پورا ہو جانے کی وجہ سے۔ پھر اگر اس نے سب مہینے معین کر کے بتا دیئے تو عقد جائز ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ کل مدت معلوم ہوگئی۔ پھر اگر ٹھہر گیا مستاجر دوسرے مہینہ میں بھی ایک گھڑی تو اس میں بھی عقد صحیح ہو جائے گا۔ اب موجہ اس کو نکال نہیں سکتا ۔ یہاں تک کہ مہینہ گذر جائے اسی طرح ہر اس مہینہ کا حکم ہے جس کے شروع میں مستاجر سکونت کرے۔ کیونکہ دوسرے مہینہ میں بھی سکونت پر دونوں کی رضا مندی سے عقد پورا ہو گیا۔ لیکن کتاب میں جو ذ کر کیا ہے۔ قیاس یہی ہے اور اس کی طرف بعض مشائخ نے میلان کیا ہے۔ اور ظاہر الروایہ یہ ہے کہ دوسرے ماہ کی اول رات اور اول دن میں ان میں سے ہر ایک کو شیخ کا اختیار رہیگا۔ کیونکہ ایک گھڑی کا اعتبار کرنے میں کچھ حرج ہے۔ جب کرایہ پر لیا مکان سال بھر کے لئے دس درہم میں تو یہ جائز ہے۔ اگر چہ ماہانہ اجرت کی قسط بیان نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ کل مدت تقسیم کے بغیر معلوم ہے۔ تو ایک ماہ کے اجارہ کی طرح ہو گیا کہ یہ جائز ہے اگر چہ ہر روز کی قسط بیان نہ کی ہو۔ تشرح قوله ومن استاجر داراً الخ ۔ کسی نے ایک مکان ایک درہم ماہوار کرایہ پر لیا تو بار صرف ایک ماہ میں صحیح ہوگا اور اجارہ باقی مہینوں میں فاسد ، ہاں اگر وہ کل مہینے بیان کر دے مثلا یوں کہے کہ دس ماہ کے لئے ہر ماہ ایک درہم کے عوض لے رہا ہوں تو سب میں صحیح ہو جائے گا کیونکہ کل مدت معلوم ہوگئی ۔ مدت کے بارے میں امام شافعی بھی یہی فرماتے ہیں اور شیخ اصطحر کی اور امام احمد نے بھی اس کو اختیار کیا ہے۔ لیکن امام شافعی کا اصح قول یہ ہے کہ اجارہ باطل ہے۔ امام مالک کے نزدیک اجارہ میچ ہے ہر ماہ گزرنے پر اجرت کا مستحق
قوله لان الاصل الخ ۔ صرف ایک ماہ میں اجارہ کے صحیح ہونے کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جب کلمہ کل ایسی چیزوں پر داخل ہو جن کی - کوئی انتہا نہ ہو تو اس کے عموم پر عمل متعذر ہونے کی وجہ سے فرد واحد کی طرف منصرف ہوتا ہے اور ایک مہینہ معلوم ہے تو اجارہ ایک ہی مبین میں صحیح ہوگا۔ پھر جس مہینہ کے شروع میں مستاجر تھوڑی دیر ٹھہرے گا۔ اس میں بھی اجارہ صحیح ہو جائے گا یہاں تک کہ مہینہ ختم ہونے سے
پہلے مو جر متاجر کو اس مکان سے نکال نہیں سکتا۔ وہ صحت یہ ہے کہ مظہر نے کی وجہ سے دونوں کی رضا مندی پائی گئی۔ قوله الا ان الذى الخ - امام قدوری نے جو مختصر میں لفظ ساعۃ ( ایک گھڑی ) ذکر کیا ہے یہی قیاس ہے اور بعض متاخرین مشائخ اس کی طرف مائل ہیں۔ ظاہر الروایہ یہ ہے کہ دوسرے مہینہ کے اول شب و روز میں متعاقدین میں سے ہر ایک کو فسخ اجارہ کا اختیار رہے گا۔ کیونکہ ایک گھڑی کا اعتبار کرنے میں کچھ حرج ہے۔

Book of Ijarat. It is restricted to a single unit because acting upon the generality is impossible, and one month is known, so the contract becomes valid in it. When this month is completed, each of them has the option to rescind the lease because the correct contract has been completed. Then if he specifies all the months and informs, the contract becomes permissible. Because the total period became known. Then if the lessee stays for a moment even in the second month, then in that too the contract becomes valid. Now the lessor cannot evict him until the month passes. Similarly is the ruling of every month in which the lessee resides at its beginning. Because in the second month too, the contract was completed with mutual consent upon residence. But what is mentioned in the book: this is the analogy (qiyas) and some later scholars inclined towards it. And the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) is that at the first night and first day of the second month, each of them (the contracting parties) has the option (to rescind). Because considering a moment is problematic. When a house is rented for a full year for ten dirhams, it is permissible even if the monthly rent installment is not stated. Because the total period is known without division. So it became like the lease of one month that it is permissible even if the daily rent installment is not stated. Explanation of his statement: 'Whoever rents a house...' Someone rented a house for one dirham per month, so the lease is valid only in one month, and the lease is fasid in the remaining months. Yes, if he states all the months, for example, says: 'I am taking it for ten months at one dirham per month,' then it is valid in all because the total period became known. Regarding the period, Imam Shafi'i also says this, and Sheikh Istakhrī and Imam Ahmad also chose this. But the more correct statement of Imam Shafi'i is that the lease is batil. According to Imam Malik, the lease is permissible, and rent is due upon each month passing. His statement: 'Because the principle...' The reason for the validity of the lease in only one month is that when the word 'kull' (all/every) enters upon things that have no end, acting upon its generality is impossible, so it is diverted to a single individual, and one month is known, so the lease is valid in one month. Then in whichever month the lessee stays for a short while at its beginning, the lease becomes valid in that too, such that before the month ends the lessor cannot evict the lessee from the house. Its validity is due to the finding of mutual consent through the apparent [action]. His statement: 'Except that which...' Imam al-Quduri mentioned the word 'hour' (one moment) in al-Mukhtasar; this is the analogy, and some later scholars incline towards it. The apparent narration is that at the first night and first day of the second month, each of the contracting parties has the option to rescind the lease. Because considering a moment is problematic. His statement: 'And if he rents a house...' In this manner, if he rents a house for a full year and mentions the full year's rent but does not state the monthly rent, even then the lease is valid. Because the total period became known without stating each month's installment. So it became like renting a house for one month without stating each day's rent, which is permissible.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the ruling of renting a house with a monthly rent but without specifying the total number of months. The Hanafi position is that the lease is valid only for the first month; for subsequent months it is fasid unless the total months are stated. If the total is stated, all months are valid. There is an internal Hanafi difference: qiyas (analogy) holds that if the lessee stays even for a moment in the second month, the lease becomes valid for that entire month due to mutual consent. However, the relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is that at the beginning of the second month, either party has the option to cancel the lease. The reason is that considering a moment as establishing consent is problematic. The passage also discusses the case where the house is rented for a full year with a lump sum rent; this is valid even without stating monthly installments, similar to renting for one month without daily installments. Other madhahib are mentioned: Imam Shafi'i's stronger opinion is that the lease is void (batil); Imam Malik considers it permissible; Imam Ahmad and Sheikh Istakhrī have a view similar to the Hanafi position. The Hanafi proof is based on the impossibility of applying the word 'kull' (all) to indefinite items, so it is restricted to a single known month.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijarah): A contract of lease or hire for a specified benefit or service in exchange for known compensation.
ظاہر الروایہ (zahir al-riwayah): The transmitted rulings from the six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.).
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to derive ruling for a new case from an original case due to shared effective cause.
فاسد (fasid): A defective contract that lacks an essential condition but can be rectified; the contract is not void but not fully valid.
کل (kull): The word 'all/every' in Arabic; in this context, applied to indefinite items it restricts to a single unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab (mufta bihi), what is the ruling at the beginning of the second month when renting a house for 1 dirham per month without specifying total months?
A) The lease becomes automatically valid for the entire second month if the tenant stays for a moment.
B) The lease is fasid and immediately void; the tenant must vacate.
C) Each party has the option to cancel the lease.
D) The lease becomes valid only if both parties sign a new agreement.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the first month (valid) and subsequent months (fasid) when total duration is unspecified, with the mufta bihi giving an option to cancel at the start of each new month.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
12 min
Lease Period Commencement and Month Calculation
Determines start of lease period and whether months counted by days or lunar months

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for commencement of the lease period and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad on calculating months when the contract starts mid-month.

Core Idea
When a lease contract starts mid-month, Abu Hanifa counts all months by days; Muhammad counts the first by days and the rest by lunar months.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses two connected issues in lease (ijara) contracts: when does the lease period begin if the start date is not specified, and if it is specified in months but the contract is made in the middle of a lunar month, how should those months be counted? The general rule is that the period starts from the time named, or if not named, from the time of contract, analogous to an oath. The second issue involves a significant intra-Hanafi dispute among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani, which we will analyze in detail.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule for commencement
The passage states that the lease period begins at the time specified by the parties; if not specified, it begins at the time the contract is made. This is reasoned by analogy to oaths, where the period starts immediately, unlike fasting which excludes nights.
This rule applies to all lease contracts in the Hanafi school.
2
Recognize the condition for month calculation
If the contract is made at the sighting of the lunar crescent, all months are counted by lunar months. If the contract is made in the middle of a month, a dispute arises on how to count the months.
The key distinction is whether the start aligns with the lunar month.
3
State the positions of the three Imams
Abu Hanifa holds that all months (i.e., the entire term) are counted by days (30 days per month). Abu Yusuf has two narrations: one agreeing with Abu Hanifa and one with Muhammad. Muhammad holds that only the first month is counted by days (out of necessity) and the remaining months by lunar crescents.
This is the core of the intra-Hanafi dispute.
4
Analyze the proofs (talil)
Muhammad's reasoning: recourse to days is only due to necessity, which exists only for the first month. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: once the first month is completed by days, the second month must also start by days by necessity, and so on until the end of the term. This is supported by analogy to the 'iddah (waiting period) calculation.
The analogy to 'iddah reinforces the idea that once days are used, they continue.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa's view, a one-year lease starting mid-month ends after exactly 360 days (12 months of 30 days). Under Muhammad's view, after the first 30 days, the remaining months follow the lunar calendar, so the end date aligns with the crescent after the last month.
This practical difference affects rent payment and contract end dates.
