تشریح قوله ثم يعتبر الخ- مدت اجارہ کی ابتداء اسی وقت سے شمار ہوگی جو وقت موجر و مستاجر نے بیان کیا ہے۔ اور اگر انہوں نے کوئی وقت بیان نہ کیا ہو تو ابتداء مدت اس وقت سے شمار ہوگی جب سے اجارہ پر لیا ہے۔ کیونکہ اجارہ کے حق میں کل اوقات یکساں ہیں تو یہ قسم کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ مثلا قسم کھائی کہ فلاں سے ایک ماہ کلام نہ کروں گا تو جس وقت سے قسم کھائی ہے مہینہ اسی وقت سے شمار ہوگا۔ بخلاف روزہ کے۔ کہ اگر کسی نے نذر کی کہ مجھ پر ایک ماہ کے روزے واجب ہیں تو علی الاتصال مہینہ ضروری نہیں ۔ کیونکہ روزہ کے حق میں تمام اوقات یکساں نہیں ہوتے ۔ چنانچہ راتیں روزہ کا حل نہیں ہیں۔
قوله ثم ان كان العقد ... الخ - پھر اگر عقد اجارہ چاند رات کو واقع ہوا تو سال کے کل مہینوں کا شمار چاند سے ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ شہور میں اہلہ ہی اصل ہیں قال الله تعالى يسألونك عن الاهلة قل هى مواقيت للناس الا ترى الى قوله عليه السلام صوموا لرؤيته وأفطروا لرؤيته فان غم عليكم الهلال فاكملو اعدة شعبان ثلاثين يوماً اور اگر عقد اجاره شروع چاند سے نہیں۔ بلکہ اثناء ماہ میں کسی تاریخ سے واقع ہوا ہو۔ مثلاً دسویں یا بارھویں تاریخ میں تو ہر ماہ کا اعتبار دنوں کے لحاظ سے ہوگا ۔ یعنی ہر تمیں روز کے بعد ایک مہینہ ہوا کرے گا۔ یہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک ہے۔ امام ابو یوسف اور امام احمد سے ایک روایت اور امام شافعی کا ایک قول بھی یہی ہے۔ امام محمد کے نزدیک پہلا مہینہ دونوں سے پورا کیا جائے گا اور باقی مہینے چاندوں سے، امام ابو یوسف و امام احمد سے دوسری روایت اور امام شافعی کا دوسرا قول یہی ہے۔ کیونکہ ایام کی طرف مراجعت بوجہ ضرورت ہے اور ضرورت صرف پہلے مہینے میں ہے۔ امام صاحب یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جب پہلا مہینہ ایام سے پورا ہوگا تو دوسرے مہینے کی ابتداء بھی ایام سے ہوگی۔ وهكذا الى آخر السنة.
Then the beginning of the period is considered from what they named, and if they did not name anything, then it is from the time he rented it, because all times are equal in respect of lease, so it resembles an oath, unlike fasting because nights are not a place for it. Then if the contract is at the time of the crescent's appearance, then all months of the year are by the crescents because they are the origin. And if it is in the middle of a month, then all are by days according to Abu Hanifa, and this is one narration from Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, and it is another narration from Abu Yusuf: the first month is by days and the rest by crescents, because recourse to days is out of necessity, and that is in the first of them. And his (Abu Hanifa's) argument is that when the first is completed by days, the second begins by days out of necessity, and so on till the end of the year. Its analogy is the 'iddah, which has passed in the book of talaq. Translation: Then the beginning of the period is considered from the time they named, and if they did not name anything, then from the time he rented it, because all times are equal in respect of lease, so it resembles an oath, unlike fasting because nights are not a place for it. Then if the contract is at the time of the crescent's appearance, all months of the year are counted by the crescents, because they are the origin. And if it is in the middle of a month, then all are counted by days according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and this is one narration from Abu Yusuf. According to Imam Muhammad, and it is the other narration from Abu Yusuf: the first month is by days and the rest by crescents, because recourse to days is out of necessity, and necessity is only in the first month. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is that when the first month is completed by days, the second month must also be by days, and so on until the end of the year. Its analogy is the 'iddah which has passed in the book of talaq. Explanation of his statement: 'Then it is considered...' The beginning of the lease period will be counted from the time that the lessor and lessee stated. If they did not state any time, then the beginning of the period is from the time the lease was taken. Because all times are equal in respect of lease, so it resembles an oath. For example, if someone swears that he will not speak to so-and-so for one month, the month is counted from the time of the oath. Unlike fasting, if someone vows to fast for one month, consecutive fasting is not necessary because not all times are equal for fasting; nights are not suitable for fasting. His statement: 'Then if the contract...' Then if the lease contract occurs on a crescent night, all months of the year are counted by crescents, because in months the crescents are the origin. Allah says: 'They ask you about the crescents; say they are appointed times for people.' Also consider the Prophet's saying: 'Fast at its sighting and break fast at its sighting, and if the crescent is hidden from you, complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty days.' And if the lease contract does not start from the crescent but from a date in the middle of the month, for example the 10th or 12th, then every month is counted by days—that is, every thirty days makes a month. This is according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Ahmad have one narration, and Imam Shafi'i has one saying to this effect. According to Imam Muhammad, the first month is completed by days and the remaining by crescents. This is the second narration from Abu Yusuf and Imam Ahmad, and the second saying of Imam Shafi'i. Because recourse to days is out of necessity, and necessity is only in the first month. Imam Abu Hanifa says that when the first month is completed by days, the beginning of the second month will also be by days, and so on until the end of the year.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage deals with the commencement of the lease period and how months are calculated. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam Muhammad, and two narrations from Abu Yusuf. The general rule is that the lease period begins at the time specified by the parties; if not specified, it begins at the time of the contract. This is analogous to an oath, where the period starts immediately, unlike fasting where nights interrupt. If the contract is made at the start of a lunar month (crescent sighting), the months are counted by lunar months according to all. However, if the contract is made in the middle of a month, there is a difference: Imam Abu Hanifa says all months are counted by days (30 days each). One narration from Abu Yusuf agrees. Imam Muhammad (and another narration from Abu Yusuf) says the first month is counted by days (out of necessity) and the remaining by lunar months. Abu Hanifa's proof is that once the first month is started by days, the second must also be by days by necessity, continuing to the end. The text draws an analogy to the 'iddah (waiting period) calculations. It also supports the lunar months as the origin with a Quranic verse and hadith about fasting.

Key Terms
ابتداء المدة (ibtida' al-mudda): The commencement point of the lease period; whether it starts from the time named in the contract or from the time of contract itself.
الأهلة (al-ahillah): The lunar crescents used to mark months; considered the original basis for counting months in lease contracts.
الأيام (al-ayyam): Days; used to count months by 30-day periods when the contract starts mid-month.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad (and one narration from Abu Yusuf), when a lease contract is made in the middle of a lunar month, how is the first month calculated?
A) By the lunar crescent (29 or 30 days)
B) By days (30 days)
C) By the number of days remaining in that lunar month
D) The contract is invalid until the next crescent

Key Takeaway
The lease period begins at the time named in the contract or at contract formation; months are counted by lunar months if the contract starts at a crescent; if mid-month, Abu Hanifa counts all months by 30-day periods, while Muhammad counts only the first month by days and the rest by lunar months.

Calculation of Months in Ijarah: Dispute Among Hanafi Imams
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ijarah month calculation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani on counting months in ijarah when the contract starts mid-month and APPLY the mufta bihi ruling to determine the end date of a lease.

Core Idea
When ijarah starts mid-month, Abu Hanifa counts all months by 30 days; Muhammad counts only the first month by days.

In Hanafi fiqh, the length of an ijarah lease is determined by months. But what happens if the contract begins in the middle of a lunar month? The three senior Hanafi imams disagreed on the method. This lesson unpacks their arguments and identifies the relied-upon position in the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the starting point of the ijarah period
The text states that if the parties specify a start date, it governs; otherwise, it begins from the contract date. This sets the baseline.
2
Distinguish two scenarios: contract at beginning vs. middle of month
If the contract occurs at the crescent, use lunar months; if mid-month, a dispute arises.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and his qiyas on 'iddah
He counts all months by 30-day periods (days), analogizing to the waiting period of divorce.
Abu Hanifa argues that once you start with days, you continue.
4
State Muhammad al-Shaybani's position and his necessity argument
He counts only the first month by days, then reverts to lunar months, because days are used only out of necessity.
Necessity (al-darura) is limited to the incomplete first month.
5
Note Abu Yusuf's two narrations and determine the mufta bihi
Abu Yusuf transmitted both views; the relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's, from Zahir al-Riwayah.
Al-Hidayah and later commentaries prefer Abu Hanifa's view.

تشریح قوله ثم يعتبر الخ- مدت اجارہ کی ابتداء اسی وقت سے شمار ہوگی جو وقت موجر و مستاجر نے بیان کیا ہے۔ اور اگر انہوں نے کوئی وقت بیان نہ کیا ہو تو ابتداء مدت اس وقت سے شمار ہوگی جب سے اجارہ پر لیا ہے۔ کیونکہ اجارہ کے حق میں کل اوقات یکساں ہیں تو یہ قسم کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ مثلا قسم کھائی کہ فلاں سے ایک ماہ کلام نہ کروں گا تو جس وقت سے قسم کھائی ہے مہینہ اسی وقت سے شمار ہوگا۔ بخلاف روزہ کے۔ کہ اگر کسی نے نذر کی کہ مجھ پر ایک ماہ کے روزے واجب ہیں تو علی الاتصال مہینہ ضروری نہیں ۔ کیونکہ روزہ کے حق میں تمام اوقات یکساں نہیں ہوتے ۔ چنانچہ راتیں روزہ کا حل نہیں ہیں۔

The crescent: all months of the year are determined by crescents because they are the basis. If it is in the middle of the month, then all are by days according to Abu Hanifa, and this is one narration from Abu Yusuf. According to Muhammad, and it is another narration from Abu Yusuf: the first month is by days and the rest by crescents because days are resorted to out of necessity, and necessity is only in the first. His proof: when the first month is completed by days, the second necessarily begins by days, and so on until the end of the year. Its analogy is the waiting period (iddah) which has passed in the book of divorce. Translation: Then the beginning of the period is considered from the time they stated; if they did not state anything, then from the time the ijarah was taken. Because all times are equal in the right of ijarah, so it resembles an oath, unlike fasting because nights are not a place for fasting. Then if the contract occurred when the moon had appeared, all months of the year are counted by moons because that is the basis. If it is in the middle of the month, then all are counted by days according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and this is one narration from Imam Abu Yusuf. According to Imam Muhammad, which is the other narration from Imam Abu Yusuf: the first month is by days and the rest by moons, because resorting to days is by necessity and necessity is only in the first month. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that when the first month is completed by days, the second month necessarily is by days, and so on until the end of the year. Its analogy is the waiting period which has passed in the book of divorce. Commentary: The saying 'then it is considered' - the beginning of the ijarah period is counted from the time that the lessor and lessee have stated. If they did not state any time, then the beginning of the period is counted from the time the ijarah was taken. Because all times are equal in the right of ijarah, so it resembles an oath. For example, if one swears that he will not speak to so-and-so for a month, the month counts from the time of the oath. Unlike fasting: if someone vows that a month of fasting is obligatory upon him, the month does not necessarily have to be consecutive, because all times are not equal in the right of fasting; indeed, nights are not a place for fasting. The saying 'then if the contract...' - then if the ijarah contract occurred on a moonlit night, all months of the year are counted by moons. Because in months, crescents are the basis. Allah says: 'They ask you about the crescents. Say: They are times appointed for mankind' and look at his saying (peace be upon him): Fast upon seeing it and break fast upon seeing it; if the crescent is concealed from you, then complete the number of Sha'ban as thirty days. And if the ijarah contract is not at the start of a moon but rather in the middle of a month, for example on the tenth or twelfth date, then each month is considered by days, i.e., after every thirty days a month passes. This is according to Imam Sahib. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Ahmad have one narration, and Imam Shafi'i also has one saying like this. According to Imam Muhammad, the first month is completed by days and the remaining months by crescents. Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Ahmad have a second narration, and Imam Shafi'i's second saying is this. Because resorting to days is due to necessity, and necessity is only in the first month. Imam Sahib says: When the first month is completed by days, the beginning of the second month will also be by days, and so on until the end of the year.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the calculation of months in an ijarah (lease/rental) contract when the contract's start date is not specified to coincide with the beginning of a lunar month. The ruling is divided into two scenarios: first, if the parties specify a start date, that date governs; if not, the start is the contract date. Then, if the contract occurs at the start of a lunar month, all months are counted by lunar months. If it occurs in the middle of a month, Abu Hanifa holds that all months are counted by 30-day periods (by days), analogizing to the waiting period ('iddah). Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that only the first month is counted by days, and subsequent months revert to lunar months, because resorting to days is a necessity only for the incomplete first month. Abu Yusuf has two narrations, one supporting each view. The text also notes that Imam Shafi'i and Imam Ahmad have similar differences. The proof for the general principle uses a verse about crescents and a hadith on moon sighting for fasting, but the specific analogy is with 'iddah, which in divorce law uses a similar method of counting months when the divorce occurs mid-month. The commentary explains the reasoning: all times are equal for ijarah (like a vow), unlike fasting where nights break continuity.

Key Terms
هلال (hilal): The crescent moon, used to determine lunar months
ايام (ayyam): Days, counted as 30-day periods for the purpose of ijarah when lunar alignment is absent
عدة (iddah): Waiting period after divorce, used as analogy for counting months in ijarah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if an ijarah contract is made on the 15th of a lunar month, how are the months of the contract counted?
A) All months by lunar months
B) All months by 30-day periods (days)
C) First month by days, then by lunar months
D) Only the first month is considered, others are ignored

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school resolves the ijarah month calculation dispute by following Abu Hanifa's view that all months are counted by 30 days when the contract starts mid-month, based on qiyas on 'iddah.

Permissibility of Wages for Hammam and Hijamah
Two rulings on permissibility of wages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wages for hammam and hijamah and identify the proofs used (custom, consensus, prophetic practice, and ijarah principles).

Core Idea
Wages for hammam and hijamah are permissible in Hanafi fiqh, supported by custom, consensus, and prophetic example.

In this passage, the author of the matn presents the Hanafi position that taking wages for public baths (hammam) and cupping (hijamah) is permissible. The proofs for hammam rely on customary practice and consensus, while for hijamah the proof is the Prophet's own action and the principles of ijarah. The commentary then addresses a dispute about the hammam, showing how the Hanafi school reconciles the conflicting evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage addresses two separate issues: wages for using a public bath (hammam) and wages for cupping (hijamah). Separate the proofs for each.
2
For hammam: locate the proof
The proof for hammam is customary practice (ta'aruf) and the consensus of Muslims, supported by the hadith 'What the Muslims consider good is good with Allah.' Ignorance (jihalah) about the exact compensation is overlooked due to consensus.
The dispute about hammam involves hadith condemning the bath itself; the Hanafi response is that those apply only to immodest use.
3
For hijamah: locate the proof
The proof for hijamah is the explicit practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who got cupped and paid the cupper. Additionally, it is a valid ijarah contract with known work and wage.
No significant dispute on hijamah wages.
4
Understand the dispute and Hanafi reconciliation
Some scholars prohibit hammam wages based on hadith like 'The hammam is the house of Shaitan.' The Hanafi response distinguishes between entering with covering vs. without. With proper covering, entry is permissible, and thus wages are permissible. The commentary cites supporting hadith.
The majority view permits hammam entry with covering, and wages follow permissibility.

اجرت حمام و حجام کی بحث
قال ويجوز اخذ اجرة الحمام والحجام فاما الحمام فلتعارف الناس ولم يعتبر الجهالة لاجماع المسلمين قال عليه السلام ما رآه المسلمون حسنا فهو عند الله حسن واما الحجام فلماروى انه عليه السلام احتجم واعطى الحجام الاجرة ولانه استيجار على عمل معلوم باجر معلوم فيقع جائزا .
ترجمہ جائز ہے تمام اور پچھنے لگانے کی اجرت لینا، حمام کی تو لوگوں کے تعارف کی وجہ سے اور جہالت معتبر نہیں اجماع مسلمین کی وجہ سے ، آپ کا ارشاد ہے کہ جس کو مسلمانوں نے بہتر جانا وہ اللہ کے نزدیک بہتر ہے اور لگانا تو اس دلیل سے جائز ہے کہ رسول اللہ یا سے مروی ہے کہ آپ نے خود پچھنا لگوایا اور حجام کو اس کی اجرت دی اور اس دلیل سے بھی کہ پچھنا لگانا ایک جانا پہچانا کام ہے اور اس کی اجرت بھی جانی پہچانی اور اجارہ ہے لہذا یہ کام جائز ہوگا۔
تشریح قوله ويجوز الخ - اس قول میں دو مسئلے ہیں۔ ایک اجرت تمام کا جواز اور پچھنے لگانے کی اجرت ہو اول یعنی حمام کے بارے میں علماء کا اختلاف ہے۔ کیونکہ حمام کی مذمت میں الحمام بيت الشيطان الحمام شربيت “ وغیرہ چندا حادیث وارد ہیں۔ اسی لئے بعض علماء نے حمام کی اجرت حرام قرار دی ہے۔ اور بعض علماء نے مردانہ وزنانہ تمام میں فرق کیا ہے۔ پس مردوں کے لئے دخول جائز رکھا ہے اور عورتوں کے لئے نا جائز۔
کیونکہ ابو داؤد ترمذی اور ابن ماجہ نے حضرت عائشہ سے روایت کی ہے
ان رسول الله نهى الرجال والنساء عن دخول الحمام ثم رخص للرجل ان يدخلوا في الميازر
آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مردوں اور عورتوں کو دخول حمام سے منع فرمایا پھر مردوں کو داخل ہونے کی اجازت دی تہبند باندھ کر ۔ دخل على عائشة نسوة من اهل الشام فقالت ممن انتن؟ قلن من اهل الشام قالت لعلكن من الكورة التى تدخل نسائها الحمامات، قلن : نعم قالت اما اني سمعت رسول الله يقول: ما من امرأة تخلع ثيابها فى غير بيتها الا هتكت ما بينهما وبين الله
حضرت عائشہ کے پاس ملک شام کی کچھ عورتیں آئیں ۔ حضرت عائشہ نے پوچھا۔ کہاں کی ہو؟ انہوں نے کہا۔ ملک شام کی ۔ حضرت عائشہ نے کہا۔ شاید تم وہاں کی ہو جہاں عورتیں حمام میں داخل ہوا کرتی ہیں۔ انہوں نے کہا۔ ہاں۔ عائشہ نے فرمایا۔ خبر دار، میں نے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کو یہ فرماتے سنا ہے کہ جو عورت اپنے کپڑے اپنے گھر کے سوا کہیں اور اتارتی ہے تو اپنے پردہ کو پھاڑتی ہے جو اس کے اور اللہ جل شانہ کے درمیان میں ہے۔
لیکن عام علماء کے نزدیک صحیح یہ ہے کہ دونوں قسم کے حماموں میں کچھ مضائقہ نہیں۔ کیونکہ عورتوں کو بھی حیض و نفاس وغیرہ سے نہانے کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے۔ رہی مذمت سو وہ اس بناء پر ہے کہ لگی نہائے۔ اگر پردہ کر لیا یانگ باندھ لی تو کچھ مضائقہ نہیں۔ چنانچہ حافظ بزار و طبرانی نے حضرت ابن عباس سے مرفوعا روایت کی ہے۔
احذروا بيتا يقال له الحمام، قالوا: يا رسول الله ) انه يذهب بالدرن و ينفع المريض قال. فاستتر بہر کیف مذکورہ روایات اس پر دال ہیں کہ پردہ کے ساتھ دخول حمام جائز ہے۔ اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ جب حمام میں داخل ہوگا تو اجرت دینی پڑے گی۔ پس یہ اجرت حمام کے نواز پر بھی دال ہوئیں اور یہ ثابت ہو گیا کہ مکان و دکان کی طرح اجرت حمام میں بھی
Discussion of wages for hammam and hijamah. He said: It is permissible to take wages for the hammam and the cupper. As for the hammam, due to the custom of the people, and ignorance (jihalah) is not considered due to the consensus of the Muslims. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'What the Muslims consider good is good with Allah.' As for the cupper, due to the narration that the Prophet (peace be upon him) got cupped and gave the cupper his wage, and because it is a hiring for a known work with a known wage, so it is permissible. Translation: It is permissible to take wages for the bath and cupping. For the hammam, due to the custom of people, and ignorance is not considered due to the consensus of Muslims. The Prophet said: 'What the Muslims consider good is good with Allah.' For cupping, it is permissible because it is narrated that the Prophet himself got cupped and gave the cupper his wage, and also because it is a hiring for a known work with a known wage, so this work is permissible. Commentary: His saying 'it is permissible' - in this statement there are two issues: the permissibility of wages for the hammam and for cupping. The first, regarding the hammam, there is disagreement among scholars because there are hadith condemning the hammam, such as 'The hammam is the house of Shaitan' etc. Therefore some scholars declared the wage for the hammam prohibited, and some made a distinction between male and female baths, deeming entry permissible for men and impermissible for women. Because Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah narrated from Aisha: 'The Prophet prohibited men and women from entering the hammam, then he permitted men to enter wearing waist-wrappers.' And Aisha said: Some women from Syria entered upon her; she asked, 'From where are you?' They said, 'From Syria.' She said, 'Perhaps you are from the town where women enter public baths?' They said, 'Yes.' She said, 'Indeed, I heard the Prophet say: No woman removes her clothes in other than her home except that she tears the veil between herself and Allah.' But according to the majority of scholars, the correct view is that there is no harm in both types of baths, because women also need to bathe for menstruation and postpartum bleeding. As for the condemnation, it is based on bathing without covering. If one covers or ties a waist-wrapper, there is no harm. Thus, Hafiz Bazzar and Tabarani narrated from Ibn Abbas marfu'an: 'Beware of a house called the hammam.' They said, 'O Messenger of Allah, it removes dirt and benefits the sick.' He said, 'Conceal yourself.' So these narrations indicate that entering the hammam with covering is permissible. And it is obvious that when one enters, he will have to pay a wage. So this also indicates the permissibility of the wage for the hammam, and it is established that like a house or shop, the wage for hammam is also permissible.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of taking wages for using a public bath (hammam) and for cupping (hijamah). The matn states that both are permissible. For the hammam, the proof is the customary practice (ta'aruf) of people and the consensus of Muslims; a hadith states that what Muslims deem good is good with Allah, so uncertainty (jihalah) about compensation is overlooked. For cupping, the proof is the explicit practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) who got cupped and paid the cupper, and also it is a valid ijarah contract with known work and wage. The commentary discusses a disagreement among scholars about the hammam: some consider it impermissible due to hadith condemning the hammam, and some differentiate between men and women, forbidding women entry. However, the majority view is that entering the hammam is permissible if one covers properly (with a waist-wrapper for men, proper covering for women). The commentary cites several hadith to support the permissibility of entry with covering, and concludes that since entry is permissible, paying wages is also permissible.

Key Terms
حمام (hammam): Public bathhouse
حجام (hajjam): Cupper, one who performs hijamah (cupping therapy)
تعارف (ta'aruf): Customary practice of people, used as a basis for permissibility

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof for the permissibility of taking wages for cupping (hijamah)?
A) Consensus of Muslims
B) Customary practice of people
C) The Prophet himself got cupped and paid the cupper
D) It is a form of charity

Key Takeaway
Wages for hammam (with proper covering) and hijamah are permissible in Hanafi fiqh, supported by custom, consensus, and prophetic practice.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Taking Payment for Bathhouse and Cupping
States and proves permissibility of wages for hammam and hijamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking payment for bathhouse and cupping and explain the proofs (dalil) including the role of custom and consensus in overriding qiyas.

Core Idea
Custom and consensus override analogy: payment for bathhouse and cupping is permissible.

This passage from the Book of Rentals establishes that it is permissible to charge for the use of a bathhouse and for the services of a cupper. While some hadith seem to condemn bathhouses, the Hanafi school relies on widespread custom and the consensus of Muslims to uphold the contract's validity. The ruling also addresses a potential qiyas objection — that the unknown details of the service invalidate the contract — and overrides it with istihsan based on accepted practice.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its scope
Identify the two sub-issues: payment for bathhouse (hammam) and payment for cupper (hajjam). The matn clearly states permissibility for both.
The ruling is from al-Quduri's matn, a Zahir al-Riwayah text.
2
Examine the proof for the bathhouse
The proof is twofold: customary practice (ta'aruf) and the hadith 'What the Muslims consider good is good in the sight of Allah.' This establishes that the acceptance of the community legitimises the transaction.
The hadith is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud as mawquf but treated as marfu'.
3
Examine the proof for cupping
The proof is the prophetic action: the Prophet himself had cupping and paid the wage. Additionally, the work (cupping) and the wage are known, making it a valid ijarah.
This is an explicit Sunnah (fi'li).
4
Understand the qiyas objection and its override
Some scholars argue that because the amount of water and time in a bathhouse are unknown (jahalah), the contract should be invalid by analogy. The author responds that this qiyas is overridden by istihsan because of the continuous practice of Muslims and consensus.
This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that 'urf (custom) can outweigh qiyas when supported by ijma.
5
Identify the practical consequence
The ruling means that both contracts are valid and enforceable. The wage received is lawful (halal) and not tainted by the condemnation of immodesty in bathhouses, provided modesty is maintained.
The condemnation is directed at immodesty, not the transaction itself.

ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى الرجال والنساء عن دخول الحمام ثم رخص للرجل ان يدخلوا في الميازر

احذروا بيتا يقال له الحمام، قالوا: يا رسول الله انه يذهب بالدرن و ينفع المريض قال: فاستتر به

ان الله نظر في قلوب العباد بعد قلب محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم فوجد قلوب اصحابه خير قلوب العباد فجعلهم وزراء نبيه يقاتلون على دينه فمارأه المسلمون حسنا فهو عند الله حسن و مارأوه سيئا فهو عند الله سيئ

و قد رأى الصحابة جميعاً ان يستخلف ابو بكر
نیز حدیث مذکور کو ابو داؤد طیالسی نے مسند میں، ابونعیم نے حلیہ میں، بیہقی نے کتاب الاعتقاد میں اور حافظ طبرانی نے معجم میں بطریق مسعود ی عن عاصم، عن ابی وائل عن عبد اللہ بن مسعود بھی روایت کیا ہے اس کی اسناد بھی درجہ حسن سے نازل نہیں ہے۔ پھر یہ اثر چونکہ ایسے امور میں سے ہے جن میں قیاس و اجتہاد کو دخل نہیں۔ کیونکہ یہ امر وحی کے بغیر معلوم نہیں ہو سکتا اس لئے یہ حدیث مرفوع کے حکم میں ہے۔ تلیه حدیث مذکور ما رأه المسلمون يا ماراہ المومنون میں مسلمین یا مؤمنین سے عموماً جنس مراد ہے یا استغرق یا معہود اور اصول سے معلوم ہے کہ معہود مقدم ہوتا ہے تو اس سے خاص صحابہ مراد ہوئے۔ سیاق عبارت یہی ہے اور یہ دارمی وغیرہ کی بعض روایات ابن مسعودؓ میں مصرح وارد ہے۔ پس اجماع صحابہ کے حجت ہونے پر تو حدیث سے استدلال تام ہے۔ رہا عموماً مسلموں کے اتفاق و اجماع کا حجت ہونا سو اس پر استدلال پورا نہیں ہو سکتا۔ علاوہ ازیں کل کا اجماع ثابت بھی نہیں۔ جب کہ بعض اکابر کا اختلاف موجود ہے۔ پھر یہ بھی مخفی نہیں کہ معدود ہونے کی وجہ سے صحابہ کرام کا اجتماع ممکن تھا اور اب اس کا علم ناممکن ہے۔ بہر کیف ظاہر حدیث مذکور میں صرف صحابہ کرام کا اجماع مراد ہے جن کی نسبت قرآن کریم میں
Book of Rentals. He said: It is permissible to take payment for the bathhouse and the cupper. As for the bathhouse, due to the customary practice of people, and ignorance is not considered because of the consensus of the Muslims. The Prophet said: 'What the Muslims consider good is good in the sight of Allah.' As for the cupper, due to the narration that the Prophet had cupping performed and gave the cupper his wage, and because it is a hire for a known work with a known wage, thus it is permissible. Commentary: His statement 'He said' etc. - In this statement there are two issues: one is the permissibility of the wage of the bathhouse and the other is the permissibility of the wage of cupping. First, there is disagreement among scholars regarding the bathhouse because some hadith condemn the bathhouse. Therefore some scholars declared the wage of the bathhouse prohibited, and some differentiated between male and female bathhouses, permitting entry for men but not for women. Due to the hadith that the Prophet forbade both men and women from entering the bathhouse, then he permitted men to enter wearing a waist-wrapper. Also from Aisha that women from Syria visited and she warned them about undressing outside their homes. However, according to most scholars, there is no harm in both types of bathhouses because women also need to bathe for menstruation and postnatal bleeding. The condemnation is only when bathing without covering. If one covers or wears a waist-wrapper, there is no harm. Narrations indicate that entering the bathhouse with covering is permissible. And it is evident that when one enters the bathhouse, he will have to pay the wage, so these narrations also indicate the permissibility of the wage for the bathhouse, and it is established that like rent for houses and shops, there is no harm in the wage for the bathhouse. His statement: 'And he did not consider ignorance' etc. - Some people said that in the bathhouse, the amount of water cleaned and the duration of stay are unknown, so the contract would not be permissible due to the unknown work. The author of Hidayah answers that qiyas requires that, but because of the customary practice of the people and their conduct without objection, the analogical evidence is not considered valid because practice and custom are given precedence over qiyas due to the consensus of the Muslims. The evidence is the following hadith. His statement: 'What the Muslims consider good' etc. - This hadith is narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud as mawquf, recorded by Imam Ahmad, Hafiz Bazzar, Hakim, and Bayhaqi. The text: 'Allah looked into the hearts of the servants after the heart of Muhammad, and found the hearts of his companions to be the best of hearts, so He made them the ministers of His Prophet, fighting for His religion. So what the Muslims consider good is good in the sight of Allah, and what they consider bad is bad in the sight of Allah.' This effect is treated as marfu' because it is from matters that cannot be known without revelation. The hadith indicates that the consensus of the companions is meant. The argument for the authority of the companions' consensus is complete from the hadith. As for the consensus of all Muslims generally, the argument is not complete, and moreover, complete consensus is not established when there is disagreement among leading scholars. And it is not hidden that the gathering of the companions was possible due to their limited number, but now it is impossible to know. In any case, the apparent meaning of the hadith is only the consensus of the companions, concerning whom the Quran states [the text ends here].
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is from the Book of Rentals in Ashraf al-Hidayah, a commentary on al-Hidayah. It presents and proves the Hanafi ruling that it is permissible to charge for the use of a bathhouse (hammam) and for the services of a cupper (hajjam). The author begins by quoting the matn: 'He said: It is permissible to take payment for the bathhouse and the cupper.' The reasoning for the bathhouse is twofold: first, the widespread customary practice (ta'aruf) of people transacting such rentals without objection, which amounts to a form of consensus (ijma'); second, the hadith 'What the Muslims consider good is good in the sight of Allah,' which establishes the authority of communal practice. For cupping, the proof is the Prophetic practice: the Prophet himself had cupping done and paid the wage, and the work is known and the wage specified, making the contract valid.

The commentary clarifies that despite some condemnatory hadith about bathhouses, the majority of scholars uphold permissibility because the condemnation relates to immodesty, not the transaction itself. The entry of women is also permitted if they cover properly. The passage then addresses a potential qiyas objection: since the amount of water used and time spent in the bathhouse are unknown, a strict analogy would render the contract invalid due to jahalah (ignorance). However, the author overrides this qiyas with istihsan based on overwhelming customary practice and the consensus of Muslims. This demonstrates a key Hanafi principle: established practice ('urf) and general acceptance override rigorous analogy.

The commentary further discusses the hadith 'What the Muslims consider good,' tracing its chain to Abdullah ibn Mas'ud as a mawquf narration that nonetheless functions as marfu' because it deals with matters unknowable without revelation. The author notes that the term 'muslimun' here specifically refers to the Companions, whose consensus is authoritative. He argues that the hadith fully supports the authority of the Companions' consensus but does not necessarily prove the consensus of all Muslims at large, especially when disagreement exists. Thus, the ruling is firmly grounded in the practice of the early community and the explicit approval of the Prophet.

Key Terms
حمام (hammam): A public bathhouse. The text discusses the permissibility of charging for its use.
حجام (hajjam): A cupper; one who performs hijamah (cupping therapy).
تعارف (ta'aruf): Customary practice; what people are accustomed to and consider normal in transactions.
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance regarding the details of a contract (e.g., amount of work, time).
اجماع (ijma): Consensus of the Muslim community (or specifically the Companions) as an authoritative source.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the main reason that qiyas (analogy) requiring the bathhouse rental to be invalid due to jahalah is not followed?
A) Because the work in the bathhouse is actually known and specified
B) Because of customary practice (ta'aruf) and consensus (ijma) of the Muslims that override qiyas
C) Because the hadith on cupping proves payment for services is always valid
D) Because jahalah is not a valid cause for invalidity in Hanafi law

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits charging for bathhouses and cupping based on custom, consensus, and prophetic practice, overriding the strict qiyas that would require precise specification of work.

Bathhouse Lease Valid Due to Custom Overriding Analogy
Response to objection about invalid lease due to unspecified work.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school validates a bathhouse lease with unspecified work based on custom (تعامل) and cite the supporting hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Custom (تعامل) overrides analogy when universally practiced and accepted by Companions' consensus.

In Hanafi fiqh, certain contracts like a bathhouse lease may seem invalid under strict analogy due to unspecified work. However, the school gives weight to established custom that has been consistently practiced without objection. This lesson examines the ruling, the objection based on analogy, and the proof from the hadith 'ما رأى المسلمون حسنا فهو عند الله حسن' which establishes the authority of customary consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
Determine the core question: Is a lease (ijarah) of a bathhouse valid when the exact amount of work (e.g., water cleaned, duration) is not specified?
This is a common issue in muamalat where contractual terms may be ambiguous.
2
Recognize the Opposing View
Understand the objection based on qiyas: some scholars argue that since the work is unknown, the lease is invalid because uncertainty (jahalah) vitiates the contract.
This is the default position under strict analogy.
3
Understand the Hanafi Response
Learn how Al-Marghinani (in Al-Hidayah) rebuts the objection: although qiyas suggests invalidity, the prevailing custom (تعامل) of the people takes precedence because it is continuous and accepted without objection.
This illustrates the Hanafi principle that custom can override qiyas when it reflects community consensus.
4
Examine the Proof
Analyze the hadith narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (marfu'an fi al-ma'na): 'What the Muslims consider good is good with Allah'. The passage explains that this hadith, though technically mawquf, carries the ruling of marfu' and specifically refers to the Companions' consensus.
The discussion also addresses the chain of narration and why it is sound.
5
Confirm the Conclusion
Conclude that the bathhouse lease is valid (sahih) based on custom, and that the Hanafi school relies on this position as mufta bihi.
The practical effect: such leases are enforceable despite unspecified work, due to established custom.

نیز حدیث مذکور کو ابو داؤد طیالسی نے مسند میں ، ابونعیم نے حلیہ میں، بیہقی نے کتاب الاعتقاد میں اور حافظ طبرانی نے معجم میں بطریق مسعود ی عن عاصم، عن ابی وائل عن عبد اللہ بن مسعود بھی روایت کیا ہے اس کی اسناد بھی درجہ حسن سے نازل نہیں ہے۔ پھر یہ اثر چونکہ ایسے امور میں سے ہے جن میں قیاس و اجتہاد کو دخل نہیں۔ کیونکہ یہ امروحی کے بغیر معلوم نہیں ہو سکتا اس لئے یہ حدیث مرفوع کے حکم میں ہے۔ تلیہ حدیث مذکور ما رأه المسلمون يا ماراہ المومنون میں مسلمین یا مؤمنین سے عموماً جنس مراد ہے یا استغرق اور معہود اور اصول سے معلوم ہے کہ معہود مقدم ہوتا ہے تو اس سے خاص صحابہ مراد ہوئے ۔ سیاق عبارت یہی ہے اور یہ دارمی وغیرہ کی بعض روایات ابن مسعودؓ میں مصرح وارد ہے۔ پس اجماع صحابہ کے حجت ہونے پر تو حدیث سے استدلال تام ہے۔ رہا عموماً مسلموں کے اتفاق و اجماع کا حجت ہونا سو اس پر استدلال پورا نہیں ہو سکتا۔ علاوہ ازیں کل کا اجماع ثابت بھی نہیں ۔ جب کہ بعض اکابر کا اختلاف موجود ہے۔ پھر یہ بھی مخفی نہیں کہ معدود ہونے کی وجہ سے صحابہ کرام کا اجتماع ممکن تھا اور اب اس کا علم ناممکن ہے۔ بہر کیف ظاہر مدیث مذکور میں صرف صحابہ کرام کا اجماع مراد ہے جن کی نسبت قرآن کریم میں
اولئك هو المؤمنون حقا اولئک هم الصادقون، اولئک هم المفلحون وغیرہ بکثرت آیات صریحہ وارد ہیں کہ صحیح معنی میں کامل مومنین یہی حضرات تھے۔ بخلاف مابعد کے کہ وہ لوگ اگر چہ مؤمن ہیں لیکن کوئی قطعی دلیل نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ محل ایمان قلب ہے۔ اور اس پر اللہ جل شانہ کے علاوہ کسی کو اطلاع نہیں ہے۔ یہ اور بات ہے کہ آدمی اپنے اعتقاد کے مطابق یقین رکھتا ہے کہ وہ مسلمان ہے لیکن یہ ہرگز نہیں کہہ سکتا کہ میرے قلب میں وہ ایمان ہے جو اللہ تعالیٰ نے پسند فرمایا ہے۔ (عین بہذیب)
His statement 'and he did not consider the [ignorance]'... Some people have said: In a bathhouse, the amount of water etc. that is cleaned and the duration of stay there are unknown; thus because the work is unknown, the lease is not valid. The author of Hidayah is responding: Analogy would require this, but because the custom of people (تعارف ناس) and their practice with acceptance has been ongoing, the analogical proof is not considered; because practice (تعامل) takes precedence over analogy, and there is consensus of the Muslims on this. Its evidence is the following hadith. His statement 'ما رأى المسلمون...' This hadith is narrated from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) as a stop (موقوف) hadith; its takhrij is by Imam Ahmad and Hafiz Bazzar in Musnad, Hakim in Mustadrak, and Bayhaqi in Madkhal. 'Indeed Allah looked into the hearts of servants after the heart of Muhammad (peace be upon him), and found the hearts of his companions the best of hearts, so He made them deputies of His Prophet, fighting for His religion. So what the Muslims see as good is good with Allah, and what they see as evil is evil with Allah.' Allah looked... So what the Muslims see as good is good with Allah, and what they see as evil is evil with Allah. Ibn al-Hadi states that this hadith is also narrated as elevated (مرفوع) from Anas, but its chain is dropped; so the stopped version is established, which Hakim called sahih al-isnad, and Hafiz Ibn Hajar in al-Diraya considered its chain as hasan. In Hakim's narration there is also the addition: 'And all the companions saw that Abu Bakr should be the successor.' Also this hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud al-Tayalisi in Musnad, Abu Nu'aym in Hilya, Bayhaqi in Kitab al-I'tiqad, and Hafiz Tabarani in Mu'jam via Mas'ud from Asim from Abu Wa'il from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud; its chain is not below the level of hasan. Moreover, this effect (اثر) is among matters where analogy and ijtihad have no scope, because it cannot be known except through revelation; thus this hadith is in the ruling of marfu'. Then, throughout this hadith 'ما رأه المسلمون' or 'ما رآه المؤمنون'—the word 'Muslimin' or 'Mu'minin'—is it general for the entire genus, or comprehensive, or for the known (معہود)? And from usul it is known that the known (معہود) takes precedence, so it specifically means the Companions. The context of the phrase is this, and it is explicitly mentioned in some narrations of Darimi etc. from Ibn Mas'ud. So for the consensus of the Companions being a proof, the deduction from the hadith is complete. As for the consensus of all Muslims generally being a proof, the deduction is not complete; besides, the consensus of all has not been established, given the existence of disagreement among some major scholars. Also it is not hidden that due to being limited, the gathering of the noble Companions was possible, whereas now knowledge of it is impossible. In any case, the apparent meaning of this hadith is only the consensus of the noble Companions, about whom the Quran says: 'Those are the believers in truth, ...' etc. many clear verses that in the true meaning they were the complete believers. Unlike those after, who although are believers, there is no definitive proof; because the seat of faith is the heart, and none except Allah has knowledge of it. It is another matter that a person believes according to his conviction that he is a Muslim, but he can never say that in my heart is that faith which Allah has approved. (Ayn Bihdhib)
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof concerning the validity of a lease (اجارہ) for a bathhouse (حمام) where the exact amount of work (e.g., water cleaned, duration) is unspecified. The author of Hidayah addresses an objection: some scholars argue that since the work is unknown, the lease is invalid under analogy (قیاس). The response is that although analogy would suggest invalidity, the prevailing custom (تعامل) of the people overrides analogy, because the practice has been continuously accepted without objection. This is based on the hadith 'ما رأى المسلمون حسنا فهو عند الله حسن' (What the Muslims consider good is good with Allah). The hadith is discussed in detail: it is a marfu' in meaning from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, with chains verified as hasan or sahih. The text then clarifies that the term 'Muslims' in the hadith refers specifically to the Companions, because the context indicates the known group (معہود) and their consensus is a definitive proof. The discussion concludes that the consensus of the Companions is a valid proof, while the consensus of all Muslims generally is not used here due to difficulty in verification. Therefore, the lease of a bathhouse with unspecified work is valid based on custom.

Key Terms
تعامل (ta'āmul): Customary practice of the people that is continuously accepted without objection.
اجماع (ijmā'): Consensus of the Muslim community, specifically the Companions here, as a proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi position, why is a lease of a bathhouse valid even though the work (amount of water cleaned, duration) is unspecified?
A) Because the owner can specify the work later.
B) Because the customary practice (تعامل) of the people overrides the strict analogy (قیاس) requiring specification.
C) Because the bathhouse is considered mubah (permissible) property.
D) Because the hadith allows any lease without specification.

Key Takeaway
Custom (تعامل) can override analogy in Hanafi fiqh when it reflects an established and accepted practice, as demonstrated by the validity of a bathhouse lease with unspecified work.

Prohibition of Taking Wages for Studding (عسب التيس)
Inter-madhhab dispute on studding wages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wages for animal studding, identify the primary dalil, and evaluate the opposing Maliki position.

Core Idea
Taking a wage for studding is haram; a voluntary gift is permissible.

This lesson examines a specific transaction: paying a fee for the service of a male animal covering females. While such arrangements may seem practical, the Hanafi school holds them strictly forbidden based on explicit prophetic guidance. We will explore the primary evidence, the exception for gifts, and how the Maliki school differs.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its proof
Identify the ruling (haram) and the primary dalil: the hadith 'إن من السحت عسب التيس'. Understand that the prohibition applies specifically to a contracted wage (اجرة), not a voluntary gift (كرامة).
The word 'سحت' means unlawful gain.
2
Identify the opposing school's view
The Maliki school, along with some early scholars, permits taking a wage for studding under conditions (known mountings and duration). Their basis is the practice of the people of Medina and a broader interpretation of the gift hadith.
Imam Malik relied on 'عمل أهل المدينة'.
3
Analyze the opposing dalil
The Maliki dalil includes the hadith of the man from Kalb who was allowed a gift. They argue this indicates permissibility. Examine why this does not override the explicit prohibition.
The hadith explicitly forbids the wage but permits a gift.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between a stipulated wage (اجرة) and a non-stipulated gift (كرامة). The explicit prohibition cannot be overridden by local custom or a specific case of gift.
Hanafis, Shafi'is, and many Companions hold the prohibition.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference is that under Hanafi law, a studding wage contract is invalid and the fee is haram; under Maliki law, it is valid with conditions. The mufta bihi is the Hanafi prohibition.
The gift exception is accepted by all.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

تشریح قوله وهوان يواجر .. الخ - صاحب ہدایہ نے حسب التيس “ کی تغییر و هو ان يواجر اٹھ سے کر کے یہ بتلایا ہے کہ کلام میں مجاز ہے کہ تمہیں بول کر مطلق محل مراد لیا ہے۔ جیسے لفظ مرسن ( بمنعی رسی ڈالنے کی جگہ ) بول کر مطلق انف مراد لیتے ہیں ۔ یقال عسب (ض) الفحل اناقة عسبا بمعنی نر کو مادین پر ڈالنا۔ اب اس فعل کی اجرت لینا جائز ہے یا نہیں ؟ سو ابن ابی ہریرہ اور امام مالک اس کے جواز کی طرف گئے ہیں۔ بشرطیکہ اجرہ نزوات معلومہ اور مدت معلومہ پر ہو۔ حضرت حسن اور ابن سیرین سے بھی رخصت منقول ہے۔ حضرت عطاء فرماتے ہیں۔ لا تعطه على طراق الفحل اجرا الا ان لا تجد من يطرقك - حضرت قتاده کا بھی یہی قول ہے۔ سیحون نے ابن وہب سے نقل کیا ہے۔ وہ کہتے ہیں کہ میں نے عبد العزیز بن ابی سلمہ سے اس کی بابت دریافت کیا ہے۔ تو آپ نے فرمایا ۔ لاباس بذالک۔ ابن القاسم کہتے ہیں کہ امام مالک نے اس کے جواز کا قول اس لئے کیا ہے کہ انہوں نے اس پر اہل مدینہ کا عمل پایا ہے جو ان کے نزدیک حجت ہے۔ ابن الجوزی نے اتحقیق میں ان کے لئے ترندی و نسائی کی حدیث انس سے
استدلال کیا ہے۔ ان رجلا من كلاب سأل النبي عن عسب الفحل فنهاه فقال : يا رسول الله انا نطرق الفحل فنکرم فرخص له في الكرامة
قبیلہ کلاب کے ایک شخص نے حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے نر کو مادہ پر چھوڑنے کی اجرت کے متعلق دریافت کیا تو آپ نے منع فرمایا۔ اس نے کہا۔ یا رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم ہم نر کو چھوڑتے ہیں۔ اور انعام پاتے ہیں۔ پس آپ نے اس کو انعام لینے کی اجازت دے دی۔ لیکن حضرت علی ، ابو ہریرہ ، براء بن عازب وغیرہ صحابہ کی ایک جماعت اور امام اوزاعی، ابونور، ابوسلیمان ، امام ابوحنیفہ، امام شافعی
The wage for studding is forbidden. He said: And it is not permissible to take wages for studding a male animal (عسب التيس), which is to lease a male to mount females, because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'Indeed among unlawful gain (سحت) is the studding fee of the he-goat.' And what is meant is taking wages for it. Explanation: 'عسب' means to cover, mount; 'تیس' is a wild goat; 'فحل' is the male of any animal; 'لینزو' means to mount; 'سحت' is forbidden, impure earnings that bring shame. Translation: And it is not permissible to take wages for putting a male over females. And that is to hire a male for him to mount females, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that among unlawful earnings is the covering of the male, and what is meant is taking wages for it. (2) Explanation of his statement 'and it is...' - The author of Hidayah changed the expression 'عسب التيس' to 'هو ان يواجر' to show that there is a figure of speech in the speech: he used the phrase and intended the absolute place. For example, they say 'مرسن' (place for tying a rope) intending the absolute nose. It is said 'عسب الفحل أناقة عسبا' meaning to put the male over females. Now, is it permissible to take wages for this act? So Ibn Abi Huraira and Imam Malik went towards its permissibility, provided the wages are for known mountings and a known period. A concession from Hasan al-Basri and Ibn Sirin is also reported. Ata said: Do not give him wages for the covering of the male unless you cannot find anyone to cover for you. Qatada has the same statement. Sahnun transmitted from Ibn Wahb that he asked Abd al-Aziz ibn Abi Salama about it, and he said: There is nothing wrong with it. Ibn al-Qasim said that Imam Malik's statement of permissibility is because he found the practice of the people of Medina upon it, which is a proof in his view. Ibn al-Jawzi in al-Tahqiq deduced for them from the hadith of Anas narrated by Tirmidhi and Nasa'i: 'A man from the tribe of Kalb asked the Prophet about the studding fee of the male, and he forbade him. The man said: O Messenger of Allah, we cover the male and receive a gift. So he permitted him to accept the gift.' A man from the tribe of Kalb asked the Prophet about the wage for putting a male over a female, so he forbade him. He said: O Messenger of Allah, we cover the male and receive a gift. So he permitted him to accept the gift. But Ali, Abu Huraira, Bara' ibn Azib, and a group of Companions, and al-Awza'i, Abu Thawr, Abu Sulayman, Imam Abu Hanifa, Imam al-Shafi'i...
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the ruling of taking wages for studding a male animal (عسب التيس). The Hanafi ruling, as stated in the matn, is that it is forbidden (حرام) based on the hadith 'إن من السحت عسب التيس' (Among unlawful gain is the studding fee of the he-goat). The author clarifies that the prohibition applies to a specific wage for the act of covering. However, a gift (كرامة) given voluntarily is allowed, as shown in the hadith of the man from Kalb. The text then presents the dissenting positions: Ibn Abi Huraira, Imam Malik, Hasan al-Basri, Ibn Sirin, Ata, Qatada, and Abd al-Aziz ibn Abi Salama permitted it with conditions (known mountings and duration). Imam Malik relied on the practice of the people of Medina. The Hanafi position, shared by the majority of Companions and later imams (Abu Hanifa, Shafi'i, etc.), is prohibition. The exception for a gift is accepted by all. Thus, the lesson emphasizes that studding fees are حرام but a gift is permissible.

Key Terms
عسب التيس (asb al-tays): The act of a male animal covering a female, and by metonymy, the wage for that act.
السحت (al-suht): Unlawful, impure earnings that are forbidden and bring shame.
كرامة (karāmah): A voluntary gift or reward, as opposed to a contracted wage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, what is the ruling on taking a wage (اجرة) for a male animal covering females (عسب التيس)?
A) It is permissible if the number of mountings is known.
B) It is haram (forbidden) based on the hadith.
C) It is makruh (disliked) but not haram.
D) It is permissible only if the animal owner also receives a gift.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, taking a contracted wage for animal studding is haram, while a voluntary gift is permissible, based on explicit prophetic prohibition.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate

Hiring for Acts of Worship: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Presents Hanafi ruling and Shafi'i disagreement on hiring for acts of worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on hiring for acts of worship and apply the principle of 'ta'ah specific to Muslims' to novel cases.

Core Idea
You cannot hire for Muslim-specific worship; payment must be a gift, not a contracted fee.

Is it permissible to receive a salary for leading prayers or teaching Quran? The Hanafi and Shafi'i schools differ on this critical issue. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling, its underlying principle, and the Shafi'i counter-evidence, helping you understand the legal boundaries of hire contracts (ijarah) in worship.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: it is not permissible (la yajuz) to hire for acts of worship like adhan, hajj, imamat, teaching Qur'an and fiqh. Extract the general principle: every ta'ah specific to Muslims is not subject to ijarah.
The principle is 'كل طاعة يختص بها المسلم لا يجوز الاستيجار عليه'.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position
State Imam al-Shafi'i's view: it is valid to hire for any act that is not individually obligatory (fard 'ayn) on the hired person.
They argue it is a hire for a known work that is not personally obligatory.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
Understand the dalil: the hadith prohibiting the price of a dog and the stud fee of a stallion (عسب الفحل). This shows that receiving payment for things that should be given freely is prohibited, and acts of worship are analogous.
The hadith is narrated by Ibn Umar and Abu Hurairah.
4
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Review the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: the Prophet approved taking a fee for ruqyah with Surah al-Fatihah, saying the most worthy thing for taking a fee is the Book of Allah.
This seems to permit payment for reciting Qur'an.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response and thamarah
The Hanafi response distinguishes between ujrah (stipulated fee) and karamah (voluntary gift). The ruqyah incident involved a gift, not a pre-arranged hire. Therefore, the general prohibition stands. The practical difference: Hanafis forbid salary for muezzin; Shafi'is allow it (if not personally obligatory).
The thamarah al-khilaf is the validity of payment to mosque employees.

امام شافعی وغیرہ حضرات کے حدیثی ادلہ حسب ذیل ہیں۔
(1) صحیحین کی حدیث ابوسعید خدری،
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۲
قال: انطلق نفر من اصحاب النبي في سفرة سافروها حتى نزلوا على حي من احياء العرب فاستـضـا فـوهم فابو ان يضيفوهم فلدغ سيد ذالك الحى فسعوا له بكل شيء لا ينفعه شيء فقال بعضهم لو اتيتم هولاء الرهط الذين نزلوا لعلة ان يكون عندهم شيء فاتوهم فقالوا ان سيدنا لدع وسعينا له بكل شيء لا ينفعه فهل عند احد منكم من شيء فقال بعضهم ! نعم والله اني لارمى ولكن والله لقد استضفناكم فلم تضيفونا فما انا براق لكم . براق لكم حتى يجلعوا لنا جعلا فصالحوهم على قطيع من الغنم فانطلق يتقل عليه ويقراء الحمد لله رب العلمين فكانما نشط من عقال فانطلق يمشى و ما به علة قال : فأوفوهم جعلهم الذى صالحتموهم عليه فقال بعضهم اقتسموا فقال الذى رقي: لا تفعلوا نأتى النبى فنذكر له الذى كان فننظر ما يامرنا فقدموا على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فذكروا له ذالك
فقال: وما يدريك انها رقية؟ ثم قال : قد اصبتم اقتسموا واضربوا لي معكم سهماً. حضرت ابوسعید خدریہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اصحاب رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کی ایک جماعت سفر میں گئی۔ اور عرب کے ایک قبیلہ کے ہاں اتری۔ پس ان سے مہمانداری طلب کی مگر انہوں نے مہمانداری کرنے سے انکار کر دیا۔ ( اسی اثنا میں ) اس قبیلہ کے سردار کو بچھو نے ڈس لیا لوگوں نے بڑے جتن کئے ۔ مگر کچھ فائدہ نہ ہوا۔ پھر کچھ نے مشورہ دیا کہ اگر تم ان کے پاس جاؤ جو یہاں وارد ہوئے ہیں تو شاید ان کے پاس کچھ ہو۔ پس وہ آکر بولے۔ لوگو! ہمارے سردار کو بچھونے کاٹ لیا ہے اور ہم نے بڑی تدبیریں کیں مگر کارگر نہیں ہو ئیں تو کیا تم میں سے کسی کے پاس کوئی تدبیر ہے؟ کسی نے کہا ہاں میں دم کرتا ہوں مگر ہم نے تمہارا مہمان بننا چاہا تم نے انکار کر دیا۔ سو میں دم نہ کروں گا جب تک کہ اس کا معاوضہ نہ دو گے۔ چنانچہ انہوں نے بکریوں کا ایک ریوڑ دینے کا معاہدہ کر لیا۔ پس ایک صحابی نے جا کر سورۃ فاتحہ پڑھ کر دم کیا وہ فوراً اچھا ہو گیا۔ جیسے کوئی جانور کھول دیا جاتا ہے اور وہ یوں چلنے لگا گویا اسے کوئی تکلیف ہی نہیں تھی۔ اس نے کہا۔ انہیں معاوضہ دے دو۔ جوان سے طے ہوا ہے بعض صحابہ نے کہا۔ تقسیم کر لو۔ لیکن جنہوں نے دم کیا تھا وہ بولے ایسا نہ کرو۔ تا کہ آنکہ ہم حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پاس پہنچ کر واقعہ بیان کریں اور دیکھیں کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا کیا ارشاد ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ انہوں نے حاضر خدمت ہو کر ماجرا کہہ سنایا۔ آپ نے فرمایا تمہیں کیسے پتہ چلا کہ سورۂ فاتحہ ایک دم بھی ہے۔ فرمایا تم نے اچھا کیا تقسیم کر لواور میرا حصہ بھی نکال لو ۔
۲) حدیث ابن عباس جس کی تخریج امام بخاری نے کتاب الطب میں کی ہے۔ ان نفراً من اصحاب النبى مروا بماء فيهم لدي او سليم فعرض لهم رجل من اهل الماء فقال اهل فيكم من رواق فان فى الماء رجلا لديغا او سليما فانطلق ارجل منهم فقراء بفاتحة الكتاب على شاء فبراء فجاء بالشاء الى اصحابه فکرهوا ذالک و قالوا اخذت على كتاب الله اجراحتی قدموا المدينة فقالوا: يا رسول الله : اخذ على كتاب الله اجرا فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ان احق ما اخذتم عليه اجرا كتاب الله.
And it is not permissible to hire for adhan and hajj, similarly for imamat and teaching Qur'an and fiqh. The principle is: every act of worship that is specific to a Muslim is not permissible to hire for according to us (Hanafis). According to al-Shafi'i, it is valid for every act that is not personally obligatory on the hired person, because it is a hire for a known work that is not personally obligatory on the hired person, so it is permissible.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage presents a key ruling in the Book of Ijarah (hire). The author states the Hanafi position that it is not permissible to receive wages for religious acts such as adhan, leading prayer (imamat), teaching Qur'an and fiqh, and performing hajj. The general principle is that any act of worship (ta'ah) that is specific to Muslims (i.e., only a Muslim can perform it) cannot be subject to a hire contract. The reason is that these acts are purely for the sake of Allah and their reward is in the Hereafter; taking worldly payment undermines their spiritual nature. The text then mentions the opposing view of Imam al-Shafi'i, who allows hiring for such acts as long as they are not individually obligatory (fard 'ayn) on the hired person. The Shafi'i argument is that it is a contract on a known work that is not obligatory on the specific hired person, so it is valid. The commentary elaborates that if the act becomes individually obligatory (e.g., only one qualified person is available for imamat), then even the Shafi'i view agrees it is impermissible. The passage then provides hadith proofs for the Shafi'i position, including the famous hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri about ruqyah (incantation) with Surah al-Fatihah, where the Prophet allowed taking a fee for it. The Hanafi response distinguishes between a gift (karamah) and a contracted fee (ujrah), stating that what was permitted was a gift, not a stipulated hire. The passage also notes that hiring for teaching Torah to a dhimmi is allowed because it is not specific to the Muslim faith.

Key Terms
استيجار (istijar): The act of hiring someone for a service, equivalent to 'ijarah' (hire contract) in this context.
طاعة (ta'ah): An act of obedience to Allah, specifically acts of worship that are prescribed for Muslims only.
كرامت (karamah): A gift or favor given without prior stipulation, as opposed to a contracted fee (ujrah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is hiring for acts like adhan and teaching Qur'an not permissible?
A) Because the Prophet explicitly forbade taking payment for the Book of Allah.
B) Because these acts are specific to Muslims and their reward is for the Hereafter, not worldly payment.
C) Because the hired person is not skilled enough to perform the act.
D) Because the school follows the principle of istihsan, which prohibits all hire contracts.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits hiring for acts of worship specific to Muslims; any compensation must be unsolicited and unconditional.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate

Dispute over Taking Wages for Quran Recitation
Presents Shafi'i proofs and Hanafi counter-proofs on wages for Quran recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking wages for Quran recitation and explain how the Hanafi school rebuts the Shafi'i proofs from the hadith.

Core Idea
The Prophet's command 'لا تأكلوا به' prohibits wages for Quran; specific permissions for ruqya do not override the general prohibition.

This lesson examines a well-known disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the permissibility of receiving compensation for reciting or teaching the Quran. The Shafi'i school relies on explicit hadith where the Prophet approved payment for ruqya (healing recitation) and stated that the most worthy compensation is for the Book of Allah. The Hanafi school, however, holds that a general command from the Prophet prohibits taking any wages for acts of worship like Quran recitation. We will analyse the proofs from both sides and understand the practical consequences of this ikhtilaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling of the Hanafi school on taking wages for Quran recitation, teaching, and adhan. Note the key proof text.
The ruling is haram; the proof is the hadith 'اقرءوا القرآن ولا تأكلوا به'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognise that Imam al-Shafi'i and others permit taking wages for these acts. List their key proof texts.
The Shafi'i proofs include the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, Ibn Abbas, and Sahl ibn Sa'd.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand how the Shafi'i school derives permissibility from the specific incidents, especially the ruqya hadith where the Prophet approved taking a flock of sheep.
The Prophet said: 'How did you know it is a ruqya? You did well; divide it and give me a share.'
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Learn how the Hanafi school rebuts the Shafi'i proofs. They argue that the general prohibition is not abrogated and the specific cases are limited to ruqya as a medical treatment or subject to interpretation.
The Hanafis also cite the hadith forbidding wages for adhan, extending the prohibition by qiyas.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Understand the practical difference: in the Hanafi school, contracts for teaching Quran or giving adhan for payment are invalid and the wages are haram; in the Shafi'i school, such contracts are valid.
This affects everyday transactions like hiring a Quran teacher or paying an imam.

(1) صحیحین کی حدیث ابوسعید خدری،
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۲
قال: انطلق نفر من اصحاب النبي في سفرة سافروها حتى نزلوا على حي من احياء العرب فاستـضـا فـوهم فابو ان يضيفوهم فلدغ سيد ذالك الحى فسعوا له بكل شيء لا ينفعه شيء فقال بعضهم لو اتيتم هولاء الرهط الذين نزلوا لعلة ان يكون عندهم شيء فاتوهم فقالوا ان سيدنا لدع وسعينا له بكل شيء لا ينفعه فهل عند احد منكم من شيء فقال بعضهم ! نعم والله اني لارمى ولكن والله لقد استضفناكم فلم تضيفونا فما انا براق لكم . براق لكم حتى يجلعوا لنا جعلا فصالحوهم على قطيع من الغنم فانطلق يتقل عليه ويقراء الحمد لله رب العلمين فكانما نشط من عقال فانطلق يمشى و ما به علة قال : فأوفوهم جعلهم الذى صالحتموهم عليه فقال بعضهم اقتسموا فقال الذى رقي: لا تفعلوا نأتى النبى فنذكر له الذى كان فننظر ما يامرنا فقدموا على رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فذكروا له ذالك
فقال: وما يدريك انها رقية؟ ثم قال : قد اصبتم اقتسموا واضربوا لي معكم سهماً. حضرت ابوسعید خدریہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اصحاب رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کی ایک جماعت سفر میں گئی۔ اور عرب کے ایک قبیلہ کے ہاں اتری۔ پس ان سے مہمانداری طلب کی مگر انہوں نے مہمانداری کرنے سے انکار کر دیا۔ ( اسی اثنا میں ) اس قبیلہ کے سردار کو بچھو نے ڈس لیا لوگوں نے بڑے جتن کئے ۔ مگر کچھ فائدہ نہ ہوا۔ پھر کچھ نے مشورہ دیا کہ اگر تم ان کے پاس جاؤ جو یہاں وارد ہوئے ہیں تو شاید ان کے پاس کچھ ہو۔ پس وہ آکر بولے۔ لوگو! ہمارے سردار کو بچھونے کاٹ لیا ہے اور ہم نے بڑی تدبیریں کیں مگر کارگر نہیں ہو ئیں تو کیا تم میں سے کسی کے پاس کوئی تدبیر ہے؟ کسی نے کہا ہاں میں دم کرتا ہوں مگر ہم نے تمہارا مہمان بننا چاہا تم نے انکار کر دیا۔ سو میں دم نہ کروں گا جب تک کہ اس کا معاوضہ نہ دو گے۔ چنانچہ انہوں نے بکریوں کا ایک ریوڑ دینے کا معاہدہ کر لیا۔ پس ایک صحابی نے جا کر سورۃ فاتحہ پڑھ کر دم کیا وہ فوراً اچھا ہو گیا۔ جیسے کوئی جانور کھول دیا جاتا ہے اور وہ یوں چلنے لگا گویا اسے کوئی تکلیف ہی نہیں تھی۔ اس نے کہا۔ انہیں معاوضہ دے دو۔ جوان سے طے ہوا ہے بعض صحابہ نے کہا۔ تقسیم کر لو۔ لیکن جنہوں نے دم کیا تھا وہ بولے ایسا نہ کرو۔ تا کہ آنکہ ہم حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے پاس پہنچ کر واقعہ بیان کریں اور دیکھیں کہ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا کیا ارشاد ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ انہوں نے حاضر خدمت ہو کر ماجرا کہہ سنایا۔ آپ نے فرمایا تمہیں کیسے پتہ چلا کہ سورۂ فاتحہ ایک دم بھی ہے۔ فرمایا تم نے اچھا کیا تقسیم کر لواور میرا حصہ بھی نکال لو ۔
۲) حدیث ابن عباس جس کی تخریج امام بخاری نے کتاب الطب میں کی ہے۔ ان نفراً من اصحاب النبى مروا بماء فيهم لدي او سليم فعرض لهم رجل من اهل الماء فقال اهل فيكم من رواق فان فى الماء رجلا لديغا او سليما فانطلق ارجل منهم فقراء بفاتحة الكتاب على شاء فبراء فجاء بالشاء الى اصحابه فکرهوا ذالک و قالوا اخذت على كتاب الله اجراحتی قدموا المدينة فقالوا: يا رسول الله : اخذ على كتاب الله اجرا فقال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ان احق ما اخذتم عليه اجرا كتاب الله.

كتاب الاجارات
چند اصحاب نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کا چشمے والوں کے پاس سے گزر ہوا جن میں ایک سانپ کا ڈسا ہوا یا بچھو کا کا نا ہوا تھا پس ان میں سے ایک نے آکر کہا۔ کیا تم میں کوئی دم کرنے والا ہے۔ کیونکہ اہل چشمہ میں سے ایک سانپ کا ڈسا ہوایا بچھو کا کاٹا ہوا ہے۔ پس ایک صحابی گئے اور کچھ بکریوں کے بدلے سورہ فاتحہ پڑھ کر دم کر دیا وہ تندرست ہو گیا اور یہ بکریاں لے کر اپنے ساتھیوں کے پاس آگئے ۔ انہوں نے اس کو نا پسند کیا اور کہا آپ نے کتاب اللہ پر اجرت لی ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ انہوں نے مدینہ پہنچ کر عرض کیا۔ یا رسول اللہ انہوں نے کتاب اللہ پر اجرت لی ہے۔ آپ نے فرمایا سب سے زیادہ تم جس پر اجرت لینے کے حقدار ہو وہ
کتاب اللہ ہے۔
۳) صحیحین کی حدیث سہل بن سعد الساعدی جس کے آخر میں ہے۔ هل معك من القرآن شيء؟ قال: معى سورة كذا سورة كذا قال اذهب فقد انكتحها بما معك من القرآن
کیا تیرے پاس قرآن سے کچھ ہے؟ عرض کیا! فلاں فلاں سورتیں ہیں۔ فرمایا جا قرآن کے باعث میں نے تیرا اس کے
ساتھ نکاح کر دیا۔
احناف کی دلیل
ولنا قوله عليه السلام اقرء وا القرآن ولا تأكلوا به وفى آخر ما عهد رسول الله عليه السلام الى عثمان بن ابي العاص وان اتخذت مؤذنا فلا تأخذ على الاذان اجرا
ترجمہ ہماری دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے کہ قرآن پڑھاؤ اور اس کے عوض مت کھاؤ اور جو عہد حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت عثمان بن ابی العاص سے لیا اسکے آخر میں ہے کہ اگر تجھ کو مؤذن کیا جائے تو اذان پر اجرت مت لے۔
تشریح قوله ولنا قوله ... الخ احناف وغیرہ کے روایتی ادلہ حسب ذیل ہیں۔ ...اقرأ القرآن ولا تاکلوابه اه
(احمد، اسحاق بن راہویہ، ابن ابی شیبہ، عبد الرزاق، عبد بن حمید، ابویعلی موصلی، طبرانی عن عبد الرحمن بن شبل ، بزار عن عبد الرحمن بن عوف،

ان من أخر ما عهد الى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ان اتخذ مؤذنا لا ياخذ على الاذان اجراً

حدیث مغیرہ بن شعبة قلت : يا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ! اجعلنی امام ،قومی قال قد فعلت ثم قال: صل بصلاة اضعف القوم ولا تتخذ مؤذنا ياخذ على الاذا اجراً (بخاري في تاريخه) حدیث عبادہ بن صامت قال: علمت ناساً من اهل الصفة القرآن فاهدى الى رجل منهم قوساً
Book of Hiring. Benefit: The hadith proofs of Imam Shafi‘i and others are as follows: (1) Hadith in Sahihayn from Abu Sa‘id al-Khudri: He said: A group of the Prophet’s companions set out on a journey until they stopped at a tribe of the Arabs. They asked for hospitality but they refused. Then the chief of that tribe was stung (by a scorpion). They sought everything for him but nothing helped. Some said: Go to those men who have stopped – perhaps they have something. They came and said: Our chief has been stung and we have tried everything; does any of you have something? One said: Yes, by Allah, I can recite ruqya, but by Allah, we asked you for hospitality and you did not host us, so I will not perform ruqya for you until you give us a fee. So they agreed on a flock of sheep. He went, recited al-Hamd (Surah al-Fatiha) over him, and it was as if he was released from a fetter, and he walked with no ailment. He said: Pay them their agreed fee. Some said: Divide it. The one who recited said: Do not do that; we should go to the Prophet and tell him what happened and see what he commands. They came to the Messenger of Allah and mentioned it. He said: How did you know it is a ruqya? Then he said: You did well; divide it and give me a share with you. (Then Urdu translation/paraphrase of the same hadith.) (2) Hadith of Ibn Abbas, authenticated by Bukhari in Kitab al-Tibb: Some companions of the Prophet passed by a watering place where there was a man stung or bitten. A man from the people of the water came and said: Is there anyone among you who can perform ruqya? There is a man at the water who is stung or bitten. So one of them went and recited the Opening of the Book (Surah al-Fatiha) over some sheep, and he recovered. He brought the sheep to his companions, but they disapproved and said: You took wages for the Book of Allah. When they came to Madinah they said: O Messenger of Allah, he took wages for the Book of Allah. The Messenger said: The most worthy thing for which you take wages is the Book of Allah. (Then Urdu translation/paraphrase.) (3) Hadith in Sahihayn from Sahl ibn Sa‘d al-Sa‘idi, at the end of which: Do you have any (Quran) with you? He said: I have such-and-such surahs. He said: Go, I have married her to you for what you have of the Quran. (Urdu paraphrase.) The proof of the Hanafis: And for us is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Recite the Quran and do not eat thereby' and at the end of the covenant the Messenger of Allah took from ‘Uthman ibn Abi al-‘As: 'If you take a mu’adhdhin, do not take wages for the adhan.' Translation: Our proof is the Prophet's command: Teach the Quran and do not eat from it, and in the covenant he made with ‘Uthman ibn Abi al-‘As: if you take a mu’adhdhin, do not take wages for the adhan. Commentary on 'And for us is his saying...' The transmitted proofs of the Hanafis and others are as follows: ... 'Recite the Quran and do not eat thereby' (narrated by Ahmad, Ishaq ibn Rahawayh, Ibn Abi Shayba, ‘Abd al-Razzaq, ‘Abd ibn Humayd, Abu Ya‘la al-Mawsili, al-Tabarani from ‘Abd al-Rahman ibn Shibl, al-Bazzar from ‘Abd al-Rahman ibn ‘Awf, Ibn ‘Adi from Abu Hurayra). The Prophet commanded: Teach the Quran and do not eat from it. And: 'Indeed from the last things the Messenger of Allah covenanted was: If you take a mu’adhdhin, let him not take wages for the adhan' (narrated by the four Sunan compilers, Ahmad, al-Hakim from ‘Uthman ibn Abi al-‘As). Hadith of Mughira ibn Shu‘ba: I said: O Messenger of Allah, appoint me imam of my people. He said: I have done so. Then he said: Lead the prayer like the weakest of them, and do not take a mu’adhdhin who takes wages for the adhan (Bukhari in his Tarikh). Hadith of ‘Ubada ibn al-Samit: He said: I taught some people of the Suffa the Quran, and a man gave me a bow as a gift...
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the permissibility of taking wages (ujrah) for reciting or teaching the Quran. The author, in his commentary on al-Hidayah, first presents the Shafi'i proof texts (three hadiths) that apparently permit such compensation: (1) the famous hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri where the Prophet approved the taking of a flock of sheep for ruqya with Surah al-Fatiha; (2) the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet explicitly said 'The most worthy thing for which you take wages is the Book of Allah'; (3) the hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd where the Prophet permitted marriage with the Quran as mahr. These are strong evidences for permissibility. Then the author presents the Hanafi proofs: (1) the Prophet's command 'Recite the Quran and do not eat thereby' which is a general prohibition; (2) the covenant with ‘Uthman ibn Abi al-‘As forbidding wages for the adhan, which is analogically extended to recitation and teaching; (3) additional hadith affirming the prohibition. The Hanafi position is that taking wages for any act that is a religious obligation (like teaching Quran, adhan, and by extension ruqya if considered a form of treatment) is prohibited (haram) because it is a means of using the Quran for worldly gain. The Shafi'i position, however, considers these acts permissible based on the specific permissions in the hadith, arguing that the general prohibitions are abrogated or specific. The practical result (thamarah al-khilaf) is that in the Hanafi school, one cannot legally contract to receive payment for teaching Quran, giving adhan, or performing ruqya with Quranic recitation, whereas in the Shafi'i school such contracts are valid. The author, as a Hanafi commentator, upholds the Hanafi view, relying on the general command of prohibition.

Key Terms
رقية (ruqya): Recitation of Quranic verses or supplications for the purpose of healing or protection from harm.
أجرة (ujrah): Compensation or wages given in exchange for a service, specifically here for reciting Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on taking wages for teaching the Quran?
A) Permissible (ja'iz)
B) Recommended (mustahabb)
C) Prohibited (haram)
D) Disliked (makruh tanzihi)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits taking wages for Quran recitation and teaching based on the general command 'اقرءوا القرآن ولا تأكلوا به', and this ruling applies to all acts of worship.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
intermediate
10 min
Wages for Teaching Quran: Hanafi vs Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute with expansion on Hanafi proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on taking wages for teaching the Quran, compare it with the Shafi'i position, and identify the operative fatwa (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Teaching Quran for wages is originally prohibited in Hanafi but permitted by istihsan to preserve Quran memorization.

The permissibility of taking wages for teaching the Quran is a classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. The Hanafi school initially prohibited it, drawing on clear prophetic commands and rational analogy to other acts of worship. The Shafi'i school, relying on two key hadith, considered it permissible. Later Hanafi jurists, however, modified the ruling by istihsan due to changing circumstances, making it the relied-upon fatwa for contemporary practice. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the rebuttals, and the final operative position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds: the original ruling is prohibition (makruh tahrimi) because taking wages for an act of worship (qurbah) is invalid, and teaching cannot be guaranteed. Note the later permissibility by istihsan.
The prohibition is based on hadith and qiyas; the istihsan is a later development.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Shafi'i school holds that taking wages for teaching the Quran is permissible. They cite specific incidents from the sunnah.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the two main Shafi'i proofs: (1) the hadith of the companion who recited Surah al-Fatiha as ruqya and received sheep, with the Prophet's approval; (2) the hadith of Sahl ibn Sa'd where the Prophet married a man to a woman with the dowry being what he knew of the Quran.
These ahadith are sahih and are found in the two Sahihs.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response rebuts each Shafi'i proof: the ruqya hadith is specific to ruqya, not general teaching; the marriage hadith deals with dowry (mahr), not wages for teaching. The Hanafi textual proofs (e.g., 'اقرءوا القرآن ولا تأكلوا به') and rational analogies to salah and sawm take precedence.
The Hanafi rational argument also includes the teacher's inability to guarantee learning, making the contract void due to uncertainty (gharar).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Shafi'is allow hiring a Quran teacher for a wage; Hanafis originally forbid it. However, the later Hanafi istihsan effectively aligns the operative ruling with permissibility in modern times, though the underlying legal reasoning differs.
The term 'وعليه الفتوى' signifies the operative position for fatwa.
